### D126 — Member images are served by the app from a private GCS bucket, not via Cloud CDN behind a load balancer (replaces D23's signed-cookie/CDN mechanism; removes the load balancer)
Headshots and thumbnails are served by the **Cloud Run backend**, reading them from a **private GCS bucket**, under the **same origin** as the SPA and API — `/img/*` reaches Cloud Run via a **Firebase Hosting rewrite** — and gated by the **ordinary Book session cookie** (the same cookie that authenticates `/api/*`). The versioned URLs (`/img/headshots/{id}/{version}.webp`, `/img/thumbnails/{id}/{version}.webp`) are returned with `Cache-Control: private, max-age=31536000, immutable`, so the browser caches each image permanently and never re-fetches it. This **replaces D23's mechanism**: the **Cloud CDN signed cookie** and the **external HTTPS load balancer / URL map** D23 implied are both **removed**, and with them the only component in the architecture that cannot scale to zero. The bucket is **private** — read only by the backend's service account, with no public objects and no object ACLs as the access-control surface. D23's coarse members-only grant is preserved (any authenticated brother may view any photo); because the app now mediates reads, image visibility can additionally **track record visibility** (an `unlisted` or de-brothered brother's photo is not served to a brother who guessed the URL) — a small tightening, not a new requirement. The lazy-load + overscan-lookahead + idle-prefetch thumbnail architecture (D9/D42) is **unchanged**; only the *origin* of the bytes changes (the app, not the CDN edge). Firebase Hosting's free managed TLS and its static CDN for the SPA bundle are **retained**.
**Why:** D23 chose signed cookies over signed URLs on their own merits, but the Cloud CDN it rides on requires an external HTTPS load balancer, which on GCP bills a **fixed ~$18–25/month** — permanent, in production, regardless of traffic — the one thing that breaks Book's otherwise ~$0 idle floor (the rest of the stack scales to zero by design, D83). At Book's scale the load balancer buys almost nothing: the image corpus is tiny (≈700 brothers, a few hundred ~30–60 KB headshots plus ~5 KB thumbnails, ≈15–20 MB total, fetched at most a few hundred times ever), and the slow-connection win the design cares about (D73–D76) is **immutable browser caching**, which the versioned-URL model preserves with or without a CDN — edge caching is marginal for a US-centric, ~700-member audience. Serving the bytes through Cloud Run converts a fixed standing charge into a **usage-proportional** one that, at this volume, lands comfortably inside Cloud Run's always-free tier (≈$0; a couple of dollars a year in the worst plausible case), while **simplifying** the security model (one cookie; no separate CDN signing key or signed-cookie TTL to manage) and keeping the whole front end same-origin via Firebase Hosting + a Cloud Run rewrite. The residual cost — image bytes traverse the single instance, and the first image after an idle scale-to-zero pays a cold start — is immaterial at this scale and already an accepted condition (D119).
**Supersedes / amends:** replaces the Cloud-CDN-signed-cookie + load-balancer image mechanism of **D23** (its coarse-grant policy stands); **D9 / D42** (thumbnails are app-served, not CDN-edge-served; the prefetch architecture is unchanged); **D24** (there *is* now an image read path through the app, and `/api` vs `/img` are separated by a Hosting rewrite, not a load-balancer URL map); **D64** (managed TLS is on Firebase Hosting + Cloud Run only — no CDN/load-balancer certificate); **D85** (headshots are served by the app, not direct from GCS/CDN to the client); **D94** (a removed photo is confirmed gone via the GCS object-version purge and the app/browser cache, not "the CDN not serving superseded objects"); **D107** (the image origin is `'self'` in the CSP `img-src`; with no CDN cookie, the host-only-cookie discipline centers on the session cookie); **D109 / R18** (a cap-lapse on an image read surfaces as a `401`/`403` *from the app*, handled by the same re-auth-and-retry); **D125** (image fetches now reach the app, but quiet reading stretches still let the instance scale to zero). **No load balancer or Cloud CDN is provisioned in staging or production.** Records to `ENGINEERING-DESIGN §1.3`/`§2.5`/`§2.7`/`§6.4`/`§6.6`, `API-SPEC §1.1`/`§1.2`/`§2`/`§3`/`§6`, `DATABASE-SCHEMA §7`, `CODING-PROJECT-PLAN §4`/Phase 1/Phase 4, `PRD §4`/`§5.6`. **(Forrest's call, 2026-06-25.)**

---

## Phase 1b implementation notes (2026-06-26)

*Implementation findings from building the Ghost auth bridge, the SPA shell, and the session gate. These record where the build met reality; they change no decision.*

### N1 — Ghost members JWTs are RS512 over a 1024-bit key; verify with Node crypto, not jose (concretizes D104/§2.1)
The design specified verifying the Ghost token against Ghost's JWKS with the algorithm "pinned to Ghost's asymmetric key, rejecting `alg:none` and every symmetric algorithm" (D104) without naming the concrete algorithm. Building and live-testing the verifier surfaced two concrete facts: (1) Ghost's members API signs with **RS512**; (2) **the RSA key is only 1024-bit** (confirmed against the live `staging.pbe400.org` JWKS — one RSA key, 1024-bit modulus). The allowlist is the **asymmetric RS family** (`["RS256","RS512"]`, env-overridable via `GHOST_JWT_ALGS`), preserving D104's property exactly (excludes `alg:none` + all symmetric, foreclosing the unsigned-token and HS256-with-the-public-key forges). **The load-bearing gotcha: the `jose` library enforces a 2048-bit minimum modulus on its *verify* path and throws `RS512 requires key modulusLength to be 2048 bits or larger`, so jose rejects EVERY real Ghost token.** This is core Ghost behavior (Ghost Pro's member key is 1024-bit too — TryGhost/Ghost#24831), so it applies to **production as well**, not just staging. Fix: keep jose's `createRemoteJWKSet` for the JWKS *fetch/rotation/single-flight* (D87) — its length check is only in *verify*, not key resolution — but do the actual signature check with **Node's `crypto.verify`** (no modulus floor), plus explicit `kid`/`iss`/`aud`/`exp`/`nbf` checks, in `ghost-provider.ts`. Because verification only ever feeds an RSA public key into an RSA digest, there is no code path that could perform a symmetric verification, so the alg-pin property is if anything tighter. Regression-locked by a test that signs RS512 over a 1024-bit key. The `iss`/`aud` are the Ghost site's `…/members/api` and the member email is in `sub` — as §2.1 assumed (for ghost-staging these are `https://staging.pbe400.org/members/api`; pbe400.org for prod).

### N2 — The single live relay serves both staging and production via a hardcoded callback allowlist
The Ghost-side relay (`pbe-news-ghost-theme/book.hbs`, route `/book/`) routes a signed-in member to Book's `/auth/callback` by selecting the destination from a **hardcoded allowlist keyed by a `target` query param** (`staging` → `pbe-book-staging.web.app`, `prod` → `book.pbe400.org`) — never from the query string verbatim, so it cannot become an open redirect (D104). The backend's `POST /api/auth/start` builds the relay URL with the env-configured `GHOST_BRIDGE_TARGET`, which is how one additive route on the live Ghost site serves both environments (the D72 mechanism).

### N3 — New backend environment variables (Phase 1b)
The production/staging API now reads: `GHOST_JWKS_URL`, `GHOST_JWT_ISSUER`, `GHOST_JWT_AUDIENCE`, `GHOST_BRIDGE_URL`, `GHOST_BRIDGE_TARGET` (and optional `GHOST_JWT_ALGS`). All have pbe400.org-shaped defaults in `apps/api/src/index.ts`; staging sets `GHOST_BRIDGE_TARGET=staging` via the Cloud Run deploy (`.github/workflows/deploy-staging.yml` and `infra/provision-staging.sh`). The `sessions` and `authNonces` Firestore collections get native **TTL policies on `expiresAt`** (provisioned in `infra/provision-staging.sh`); expiry is also enforced in code, so the TTL is a sweeper, not the enforcement point (D125).

### N4 — Dev sessions map to fixed fake profile ids
The `DevIdentityProvider` assigns each role a fixed Constitution id (brother → 5001, manager → 5002, admin → 5003) so a dev session has a real backing record for `/api/me` and the directory's own-row overlay (D82). These ids sit at the bottom of the generated fake range (`FAKE_ID_FLOOR` = 5001), so the default dataset always contains them. For staging UAT through the **real** Ghost bridge, `tools/fake-data/src/link-staging-tester.ts` links a real Ghost email to a fake profile as admin (guarded to `-staging` projects).

### N5 — The session cookie must be named `__session` (Firebase Hosting strips all other cookies)
With Firebase Hosting fronting Cloud Run (D126), Hosting **strips every request cookie except one named `__session`** before forwarding to the backend — a deliberate CDN constraint. The Phase 1b live test made this concrete: the handshake fully succeeded (`POST /api/auth/session` → 200, JWT verified, nonce consumed, email resolved, session persisted, `Set-Cookie` issued) but the very next `GET /api/me` returned 401, because the browser's `book_session` cookie was dropped by Hosting and never reached the app. D107 chose the name `book_session` before D126 put Hosting in front of `/api/*`, so the conflict was latent and only appears behind Hosting (local dev's Vite proxy forwards every cookie, so it worked there). Fix: the cookie is named **`__session`** (`apps/api/src/identity/session-cookie.ts`). All its other attributes are unchanged (`HttpOnly`, `Secure`, `SameSite=Strict`, host-only, session-scoped). This applies identically to production (also Hosting-fronted). The `__session`-only rule also means a future need for a *second* cookie behind Hosting would have to multiplex onto `__session` or move that endpoint off the Hosting path. Amends D107's cookie name.

## Phase 2a implementation notes (2026-06-26)

*Implementation findings from building the full `Profile` schema, the shared validation module, and the Canonical Name derivation (CODING-PROJECT-PLAN Phase 2, session 2a). These record where the build met reality; they change no decision.*

### N6 — One identifier, the Constitution ID, named `id` (concretizes DATABASE-SCHEMA §2/§3.1)
The schema specifies a single brother key: the Constitution signing number, carried as the numeric `id` field and, because Firestore requires string document keys, as `String(id)` for the document key (§2) — there is no second identifier. The Phase-0 walking-skeleton `Profile` had drifted from this: it carried both a string `id` (a Firestore-document-id wrapper, e.g. `"fake-5247"`) **and** a separate `constitutionId: number`, following the generic "every record has a string `id`" habit while parking the real number in `constitutionId`. The real logic always keyed on the number (the email index, the by-id lookup, the session `profileId`); the string `id` was never more than a doc-id wrapper. Phase 2a reconciles this to the schema: the redundant string surrogate is removed and the field is the schema's single numeric **`id` (`type BrotherId = number`, "Constitution signature number")**, with the Firestore document key written as `String(id)` at every data-access boundary. No identifying value changed — only the field name (`constitutionId` → `id`) and the removal of the surrogate. The number remains the brother's **real-world physical Constitution signature number**, caller-supplied on create and never auto-assigned (API-SPEC §3) and immutable after creation (§8); the genesis bulk-loader writes the real roster numbers, and the fake generator uses ids above #5000 so a placeholder can never be mistaken for a real low signing number. (The field name `id` was Forrest's call, 2026-06-26: keep the schema's idiomatic primary-key name, with the meaning pinned by the `BrotherId` alias and the field doc.)

### N7 — The bundled country list is stored as codes, with display names derived from `Intl.DisplayNames`
The schema bundles the ISO 3166-1 country list and the US/CA subdivision vocabularies as build-time constants (§1/§8, D37). For countries, the implementation (`packages/shared/src/geo.ts`) stores only the **alpha-2 code set** (a compact space-separated string split into a `Set` at load) and derives each country's display name at render time from the platform's built-in **`Intl.DisplayNames`** (available in Node and the browser, zero dependency) rather than a hand-maintained code→name table — so there is no second copy of country names to drift from the standard, and validation needs only code membership. The US/CA subdivision lists (short and stable, including `DC` and the military codes `AA`/`AE`/`AP`) are authored with display names directly. This is a representation choice within the schema's "bundled constant" intent; it changes no decision.

### N8 — The de-brother sign-in denial is now enforced (concretizes D115/§2.1)
ENGINEERING-DESIGN §2.1 requires that a resolved-but-de-brothered profile be denied a Book session (the belt-and-suspenders Book-side half of D115, since de-brothering also deletes the Ghost member). Phase 1b left this as an unenforced hook because the `debrothered` field did not yet exist. With the field now in the schema (Phase 2a), the check is wired in `GhostIdentityProvider`: a resolved profile with `debrothered.isDebrothered === true` is rejected with `403 debrothered` (API-SPEC §2) before a session is minted, regression-locked by a test. The de-brother *server action* that raises the flag and drives the Ghost lifecycle remains Phase 5 (D115); only the read-side denial lands here.

## Phase 2b implementation notes (2026-06-26)

*Implementation findings from building the server-side privacy projection across all roles and the role/capability matrix (CODING-PROJECT-PLAN Phase 2, session 2b). They change no decision; they record how the access-control floor was built.*

### N9 — The projection and the write matrix are driven by two exhaustive `keyof Profile` tables (concretizes D5/D82/D106, §9/§8)
The read projection (D5/§9) and its write-side dual (D106/§8) are each expressed as a **declarative table classifying every `Profile` field**, in `packages/shared`: `FIELD_VISIBILITY` (field → visibility class, with toggle fields naming their `PrivacyFlags` switch) and `WRITE_RULE` (field → PATCH write rule). Both are typed `Record<keyof Profile, …>`, so a field added to `Profile` later **fails to compile** until it is deliberately classified — a new field can never leak into a projection, or become writable, by being forgotten. The backend `projection.ts` only *executes* `FIELD_VISIBILITY` (iterating it and copying permitted fields), keeping the server the single enforcement point while the *classification* lives in `shared` so the SPA can read the same source to gate its controls in Phases 3–4 (the D50 shared-logic precedent). The projected wire shape is the shared `Profile` with disallowed fields **omitted** (`Partial<Profile>`, D3), so per-role correctness is guaranteed by the exhaustive role×class tests rather than separate per-role output types; this revised the Phase-2a `BrotherProfile` Pick type the 2a projection had deliberately left as a stub for 2b. (Approach chosen with Forrest before coding, 2026-06-26: table-driven over per-role hand-lists.) The split read (D82) is realized as `projectForRole` (the caller-independent bulk projection, brother cached / manager+admin computed fresh) plus `projectSelf` (the owner's own record in full, via `GET /api/me`); a cross-caller-isolation test asserts the bulk projection is a pure function of `(profiles, role)`, closing review finding S1. The named privileged *actions* (delete, role-change, mark-deceased, de-brother, verify, export, backup, Ghost-sync) are deliberately **not** in `WRITE_RULE` — they are gated at their own dedicated endpoints in later phases, and several mutate fields `WRITE_RULE` marks `protected` precisely so they cannot ride the general PATCH path.

### N10 — `unlisted` and `debrothered` share `adminNote`'s read class (`staff-internal`) in the projection table (concretizes §9 D124/D115)
DATABASE-SCHEMA §9 names `adminNote` as the canonical `staff-internal` member and describes `unlisted`/`debrothered` as "staff-only flags." In the field-visibility table their **bulk-read** behavior is identical to `adminNote`'s — visible to managers and admins, hidden from ordinary brothers — so they are classified `staff-internal` there rather than inventing a seventh class. Their *other* facets are handled outside this read table, exactly as the schema requires and so nothing is lost: the owner sees his own `unlisted`/`debrothered` via the wholesale `projectSelf` (which excludes only `adminNote` and the system-internal `ghostMemberId`, §9's "full record except `adminNote`"); their differing **write** rules live in `WRITE_RULE` (`unlisted` is owner-or-admin `consent`, `debrothered` is `protected`/dedicated-action — D124/D115); and the **whole-record hide** they drive is the projection's record-level omission for brothers, not a field-level rule. This is a modeling choice within §9's taxonomy, not a change to who-sees-what; it changes no decision.

## Phase 2c implementation notes (2026-06-26)

*Implementation findings from building Book's first write path — the `PATCH /api/profiles/{id}` save path with optimistic concurrency and the reconcile seam (D25), and the audit stream (D61) — plus the single-record read (CODING-PROJECT-PLAN Phase 2, session 2c). They change no decision; they record how the write floor was built. (Scope and the one open call — folding the dataset-level structural checks into this session — were settled with Forrest before coding, 2026-06-26.)*

### N11 — The PATCH path assembles 2a's validator and 2b's matrix behind the OCC guard, in a fixed order (concretizes D25/D28/D106/D50, API-SPEC §3/§1.4)
The save path (`apps/api/src/routes/profiles.ts`) is the first writer, so it is where the access-control floor's two halves finally execute. The guard sequence is fixed: **object-level predicate** (`canActOnProfile`, the IDOR guard → `403`) → **`If-Match` required** (`428`) → **record exists** (`404`) → **per-field allowlist** (`partitionWritableFields`; any rejected field → `403`, never a silent drop) → **validation** (the shared `validateProfile` over the *merged* `stored ⊕ patch` record, plus the structural checks below → `422`) → the **D28 verification side-effect** and server stamps → the **conditional write** (`412` on a stale token). The verification side-effect is fully server-driven (the verification fields are `protected`, so they cannot ride the patch): an **owner** edit auto-(re)verifies (`lastVerifiedDate`/`verifiedBy` set); a **manager/admin** edit on another brother clears an existing verification; **deceased records are exempt**. A patch that changes nothing (deep-equal) is a no-op — no write, no verification touch, no audit. `lastModified` is stamped on every real write, and `newsletterConsentChangedAt` whenever `allowNewsletterEmail` changes (D103).

### N12 — The structural checks the shared validator defers are finalized here against the in-memory dataset (concretizes D50/D97, DATABASE-SCHEMA §8)
The shared `validation.ts` is a pure module and explicitly leaves the rules that need the whole dataset "to the write path." Per the pre-coding scope call, those are implemented here, where the cache holds the authoritative dataset: **email-namespace uniqueness** (a new primary/alternate address claimed by a *different* record — or an ambiguous one — → `422`; primary and alternate may not be the same address, D97), and **big-brother existence with a cycle walk** up the current graph. These cost nothing given the in-memory indexes and close the gap that would otherwise let a write mint a duplicate email or a big-brother cycle.

### N13 — Concurrency token = Firestore `updateTime`, encoded opaquely; a deleted-doc precondition is a 412, not a 404 (concretizes D25, API-SPEC §1.4)
The OCC token is Firestore's server-authoritative `updateTime`, surfaced as the `ETag`/`If-Match` and encoded opaquely as `"<seconds>.<nanoseconds>"` (full precision, so two writes inside one millisecond cannot collide into one token). The cache tracks the token per record (`concurrencyToken(id)`), so the single-record read emits it with **zero Firestore reads**, and `applyUpdate` advances it in lock-step with the committed write (read-your-writes; D83). The write is one conditional `update(data, { lastUpdateTime })` — Firestore enforces the precondition natively, no read-modify-write race. An emulator test proves the real `412`; route tests drive the whole flow (including 412) against an in-memory `ProfileStore` double. One finding: a write whose target was **deleted** under a held token surfaces as `FAILED_PRECONDITION` → `412` (the reconcile route — repull then `404`), *not* `NOT_FOUND`; so `MissingProfileError`/`404` is defensive only on the always-precondition path.

### N14 — The audit stream is structured-JSON-to-stdout with names-not-values enforced structurally; the per-write recompress stays synchronous for now (concretizes D61/P10, ENGINEERING-DESIGN §6.1/§1.5)
The audit stream (`apps/api/src/audit/audit-log.ts`) is an injectable `AuditLog` over a sink that writes one labeled JSON line to stdout — no SDK, per D61. The **names-not-values** discipline is structural, not a convention: an `AuditEntry` carries a `fields` *name* list and has nowhere to put a value, so a contact value cannot reach the log even by mistake (a test asserts it). PATCH emits `profile.update` (changed field names, `ok`) and the two write-denial `403`s (`denied`), each with the `X-Cloud-Trace-Context` correlation id when present (D99); the module is the seam the later privileged actions plug into. Per the plan, the on-write brother-payload recompression runs **synchronously** for now — the off-event-loop debounce and the GCS cold-start snapshot (D84/D85) are deferred to Phase 7; writes are rare at this phase and the simple synchronous rebuild is what the floor needs first.

## Phase 3a implementation notes (2026-06-27, post-staging-review fixes)

### N15 — The column lens is mirrored into the URL and history changes are push, not silent (refines D30/D31)
After a live-data review on staging, two refinements to D31's state model. **(1) Discrete view changes push a history entry** so the browser back/forward buttons walk through them: a sort toggle and every column action (show/hide, reorder, resize-commit) call nuqs with `history: "push"`; live search-as-you-type and an in-flight resize *drag* stay on `replace` so they don't flood history with a keystroke- or pixel-per-entry. D31's literal "updated *silently*" wording was the original `replace`; this is the deliberate departure. **(2) The column lens (order + widths) is mirrored into the URL** (`?cols=…`, only when non-default) so a view is shareable and history-walkable — D30/D31 originally kept columns out of the URL precisely so a shared link couldn't clobber the recipient's saved columns, and that protection is preserved by a single rule: a URL that arrives carrying `cols` is *applied* to that view but **never written back to localStorage**; only the user's own edits update their saved default. localStorage remains the durable default and seeds the URL on first load (`useColumnLens.ts`).

### N16 — Column widths are user-resizable, persisted in the lens, keyboard-operable (new; not in PRD/visual design)
A drag-to-resize affordance the original design omitted but real data demanded (full emails/cities/names were unreadable at fixed widths). Each non-thumbnail header carries a trailing resize separator (`role="separator"`, the ARIA window-splitter pattern) that is **keyboard-operable** (focus + arrow keys nudge the width) so resizing never *requires* a drag — satisfying WCAG 2.5.7 (Dragging Movements) alongside the pointer drag, consistent with the column-reorder grip's keyboard path (D79). Widths persist per-column in the lens (localStorage + URL, N15), clamped 64–640px.

### N17 — The Directory "Major" column is labelled "Course"; status treatments + the chip/avatar visuals were brought to the visual-design spec
MIT majors are **courses**, so the column header reads "Course" (the underlying field stays `majors`; the broader doc terminology is a later propagation). The staging review also surfaced visual-fidelity gaps now closed against `visual-design/`: the avatar is the spec's radial-gradient-ground + translucent silhouette + initials (and the initials ignore the `'YY` token, so it's "DH" not "D'"); the primary course renders as a course-area **chip**; the deceased **mourning band** is ink (not gold), cuts across the upper-right corner along the "╲" diagonal, and is inset so the circle rim shows; and the manager/admin **IN MEMORIAM** (gold-outline), **UNLISTED** (slate, eye-off), and **DE-BROTHERED** (strike-through + outline badge + red ✕ avatar) treatments were pulled forward from 3c so staff-only records are actually distinguishable.

### N18 — Staging is re-seeded on every deploy (refines the manual seed ritual)
The staging environment had drifted from the code (its profiles predated the fixture-name change, since a deploy never re-seeds). To make drift structurally impossible, the deploy workflow now runs the full clean-replace seed — wipe+seed profiles, wipe+seed images, relink the tester — **between** the Hosting deploy and the Cloud Run deploy, so the new revision cold-starts on fresh data. It is gated by the `STAGING_AUTOSEED` repository variable (set to `false` to skip — e.g. during Phase-8 UAT, so real testers' state survives a deploy). Needs the deployer SA's `roles/datastore.user` (Firestore) on top of its existing `storage.admin` (the image bucket); **staging only** — a prod deploy must never re-seed.

## Phase 3b implementation notes (2026-06-27, Name Search)

*Implementation findings from building Name Search (CODING-PROJECT-PLAN Phase 3, session 3b): the `@pbe/name-search` matcher, its Web Worker, the in-grid highlighting, and the build-time phonetic A/B (D35/D66/D110/D123). Scope and the two pre-coding calls — the nickname dictionary source, and running the A/B **outside the repo** on the real roster — were settled with Forrest before coding.*

### N19 — Phonetic algorithm locked to **Beider-Morse** by an A/B over the real roster; BM is sourced from `bmpm`, not talisman (resolves D66; amends D35/D66 mechanism)
The Double-Metaphone-vs-Beider-Morse A/B (D35/D66) was run as an **offline harness outside the git tree** (so the real names can never be committed), over the **real PBE roster** (`mystery-email-addresses/constitution.csv`, 1,050 brothers) with 3,907 generated (query → expected-brother) pairs spanning the error classes D66 names — transpositions, vowel swaps, consonant-doubling drift, sound-alike/transliteration rules, and middle-name lookups. The harness imports the *shipping* matcher so it tests exactly what runs. Result, on the recall-favoring criterion (favor recall if precision tolerable; size/latency tie-breakers only): **Beider-Morse wins.** Overall recall 97.6% (BM) vs 97.4% (Double Metaphone) vs 94.0% (Fuse+nicknames only), but the decisive margin is the **sound-alike class — 98.7% (BM) vs 95.7% (DM) vs 87.7% (none)** — which is exactly the international-names case that made phonetic matching an MVP need (D35). Precision is effectively identical (≈13.7 results/query, ~1.3% of the roster), and BM's higher cost (~900 ms one-time index build, ~2× per-query time) is **entirely inside the Web Worker** (D110), off the main thread, so the latency tie-breaker never touches the UX. `DEFAULT_SEARCH_CONFIG.phonetic = "beider-morse"`. **Mechanism correction:** D35/D66 said both algorithms come "from the talisman library," but talisman 1.1.4 ships **no Beider-Morse**; BM is therefore sourced from the `bmpm` package (MIT, zero-dep, run `Accuracy.APPROX` / `"any"` language for maximum recall), while **Double Metaphone stays from talisman**. The choice is config-flagged and the harness re-runnable, so the experiment can be repeated against migrated/anonymized data without code changes.

### N20 — Name Search is a pure shared package behind a Web Worker, with highlighting kept deliberately dependency-light (concretizes D35/D110/D123, ENGINEERING-DESIGN §1.6)
The matcher lives in **`packages/name-search`** — pure logic, no DOM — so the SPA's Web Worker and the (external) A/B harness build and query the *identical* index, which is what keeps the harness honest. Layers, all over name tokens split on spaces and hyphens with **AND across query tokens** (D35): exact/substring, **Fuse.js** typo tolerance, **Beider-Morse** phonetics (N19), and a **bidirectional common-nickname expansion** (D123) whose dictionary was curated from the public-domain `carltonnorthern` diminutives lookup down to common Western given names. The worker (`search.worker.ts` + `useNameSearch.ts`) is **progressive enhancement** (D110): the grid filters immediately via a main-thread substring match, and the richer fuzzy/phonetic/nickname matching switches on when the worker posts `ready` after building its index from a structured-clone of the in-memory name records; phonetic codes are recomputed each load, never persisted (no name-keyed PII on disk, D95). There is **no relevance ranking** — search returns an unordered id set and the user's chosen sort is always honored (D35). Matched characters are highlighted in results (`HighlightedName`, brand-gold `<mark>`, AA-contrast); crucially the **highlight path imports none of the phonetic libraries** — Beider-Morse/talisman/Fuse stay **worker-only** and off the Directory landing page (D74). The worker chunk is 24 KB brotli; total shipped JS ~143 KB, within the 250 KB budget.

**Highlighting follows the worker's actual match (refines the above, post-staging-review).** The first cut recomputed "what to highlight" on the main thread (substring + nickname + edit-distance), which had two visible gaps Forrest caught on staging: a Beider-Morse-only sound-alike (e.g. `kathryn`→Catherine) wasn't highlighted because the main thread can't run BM, and a match that came from a *non-Name-column* field (e.g. `khalid` hitting the full legal name) wasn't highlighted because highlight only ran on the canonical Name. Fix: `searchDetailed` returns, per matched brother, the **folded tokens of his that actually matched** (across exact/typo/nickname/Beider-Morse), and the worker ships that `Map<id, Set<token>>` back (structured clone carries `Map`/`Set` natively). `highlightRanges(display, query, matchedTokens?)` then marks a word **character-level** for a direct substring of a query token, else **whole-word** when its folded form is one the worker matched — so the right words light up across **every** name column (Name, Full Name, Mug Name) and for every match kind, still with **no phonetic library on the main thread**. Before the worker is ready the caller passes no tokens, so only the substring layer fires — exactly matching the main-thread substring fallback. Also: a **Mug Name** column was added to the grid/picker (optional, all roles — it's a public, searched field that simply lacked a column), and the fake-data generator now produces **whimsical, name-unrelated mug names** (single words + 2–3-word phrases, ~35% of brothers; PRD's "Hilbert Space Pilot" flavor) so the field is testable.

## Phase 3b-2 implementation notes (2026-06-28, interstitial Directory fixes)

*An interstitial batch between Name Search (3b) and filters/export (3c): four Directory issues Forrest found in live testing, settled with him before coding. None change architecture; each brings the running app back in line with the PRD or fills a test gap.*

### N21 — The app shell is full-bleed; reading-oriented content self-constrains (refines the visual-design container default)
The masthead, banner, main, and footer were capped at `max-w-6xl` (~1152px), so on a wide desktop the Directory grid stopped at roughly half the viewport and forced horizontal scrolling that the screen had room to avoid. The cap was the visual-design handoff's default container, not a load-bearing choice, and PRD §5.6/§5.7 already anticipate the grid scrolling horizontally only when columns *genuinely* exceed the width. The shell is now **full-width with responsive gutters** (`px-4 sm:px-6 lg:px-8`), so the grid uses the whole screen and the masthead controls stay aligned to the grid's right edge. Reading-oriented blocks constrain their **own** measure instead of relying on a shell-wide cap: the error/empty-state cards take `max-w-2xl`, the placeholder keeps `max-w-prose`, and the footer notice keeps its `max-w-2xl`. The future Profile page (Phase 4) is expected to do the same. Note: grid **column** widths remain fixed pixels (deterministic frozen-column offsets, N16); a full-width shell gives room to show more columns without scroll but does not auto-stretch columns to fill slack — that would be a separate change.

### N22 — The Class column shows the full 4-digit year; the `'YY` form stays only in the Canonical Name (concretizes §5.6.1)
The dedicated **Class** column rendered the apostrophe-two-digit form (`'72`) via `formatClassYear`, duplicating the token that already lives inside the Name column's Canonical Name. The standalone numeric column now renders the plain **4-digit year** (`1972`), which is what makes it independently scannable, sortable, and (in 3c) range-filterable; the `'YY` form is reserved to the Canonical Name where it is part of the canonical display format (D12/D15). Em-dash placeholder unchanged for an unknown year.

### N23 — The fake-data generator plants a guaranteed Canonical Name collision (supports §5.1 testing)
Canonical Name disambiguation (append `(#id)` when two brothers render an identical `First Last 'YY`, §5.1/D15) was only ever exercised by random chance in the generated dataset, so it was effectively untested in the live UI. The deterministic generator now **plants a fixed collision**: the first `COLLISION_COUNT` (2) records are forced to a shared identity — `William Evan '19` at #5001/#5002 — and forced living, listed, and not de-brothered so both stay visible to every viewing role. The forcing overrides values *after* the PRNG draws (`… && !planted`), so the stream — and every other record — stays byte-stable. A generator test asserts both planted records resolve to the disambiguated `William Evan '19 (#500x)` form.

### N24 — The masthead font-size control is restored (implements PRD §5.3, USER-MANUAL §11) *(Linear: OFC-176)*
PRD §5.3 has always specified a three-step **Normal / Large / Larger** font-size preference (a readability accommodation for the older-alum audience, alongside dark mode), but it was dropped from the visual-design pass and never built. Restored as a deliberate **mirror of the theme stack** (D30): a pure `fontScale.ts` (steps → root font-size **100% / 112.5% / 125%**, persisted in `localStorage["book-font-size"]` with Normal stored as the key's absence), a `FontSizeProvider`/`useFontSize`, a `FontSizeToggle` segmented control seated immediately left of the theme toggle in the masthead, and a second **no-FOUC** inline script in `index.html` that sets the root font-size before React paints (its percentages must stay in sync with `SCALE_PERCENT`). Because the UI is sized in `rem`, scaling the root scales the whole interface, including the help icons. The control matches the theme toggle's a11y treatment (segmented `fieldset`/`legend`, descriptive `aria-label`s since the "A" glyph alone is ambiguous, `aria-pressed`, ≥24px targets) and the visual-design COMPONENTS.md now documents it. Caveat tied to N21/N16: the grid's fixed-pixel column widths do not grow with the font scale, so at Larger some grid cells may truncate; the page stays usable (PRD §5.5) and a rem-based grid width model is left as future work.
*Later updated by: **D131** — the font-size control (and the theme toggle) moved out of the inline masthead into the avatar menu.*

### N25 — The SPA shell is served `no-cache` at every route, not just `/index.html` (fixes a stale-bundle window; D73–D76)
Live testing surfaced a returning browser pinned to an **old SPA bundle** with zero network traffic until a hard reload. Root cause: Firebase Hosting `headers` rules match the **requested path**, not the rewrite target. The shipped rule set the shell to `no-cache, must-revalidate` only on the literal `/index.html`, but the path actually requested is `/` (and `/brother/:id`, `/auth/callback`) — all rewritten to index.html but **not** matching `/index.html` — so they fell through to Firebase's default `Cache-Control: max-age=3600`. The browser then served a stale HTML shell from cache for up to an hour, and that shell referenced the *previous* content-hashed assets, which are `immutable` — so a pushed fix could be invisible for up to an hour (longer for an open tab). Fix: the no-cache rule now uses a catch-all `source: "**"`, with the content-hashed-asset rule (`*.js|css|woff2|svg|png|webp|ico` → `max-age=31536000, immutable`) kept. **Rule order is load-bearing:** Firebase Hosting applies **the last matching `headers` rule** when two overlap, so the catch-all must come **first** and the asset rule **last** — otherwise the catch-all clobbers assets to `no-cache` (observed live on the first attempt, where the asset rule was first; the asset came back `no-cache` and the order was swapped). Net effect: the ~1.6 KB shell revalidates on every load (normally a 304), big assets stay immutable, and a pushed bugfix is picked up on the next reload/navigation. The **open-tab** case (a tab never reloaded) is unaddressed by HTTP caching and is filed as a follow-up (a no-cache `/version.json` the SPA polls → calm "refresh to update" toast; Linear, tag PBE). Live headers are confirmed by `curl` after each deploy (`/` → no-cache; a `.js` asset → immutable).

### N26 — The Name Search placeholder is short; the example/teaching lives in helperText (D111/§5.9)
The search field's placeholder (`"Search by name — e.g. Smyth, or Bill"`) was wider than the 256px field and clipped — and a placeholder can't be scrolled or selected, so the cut-off text was unreadable. Placeholders must never carry essential instructions (D111/§5.9), and the example + capabilities already live in `helperText` (the SR description today, the "?" popover later), so the placeholder is shortened to **`"Search by name…"`** and the field widened a step (`sm:w-64` → `sm:w-72`, 288px) for headroom. No information lost.

### N27 — Double-click-to-auto-fit column widths (built in Phase 3c; extends N16)
**Built in Phase 3c** (`apps/web/src/pages/directory/autofit.ts`): double-clicking a column's resize boundary (or pressing **Enter** on the focused separator — the keyboard twin, D79) snaps that column to the width of its widest **data** value, measured over the whole in-memory dataset with a canvas `measureText`, clamped to the 64–640 bounds, and persisted in the lens. The non-text control columns (Select, Star, Thumbnail) are excluded (not resizable); the Course chip gets a small per-value allowance. Original rationale follows. Like Excel/Sheets, double-clicking a column's resize boundary should snap that column to the width of its widest **data** value. It is practical here precisely because Book holds the **whole dataset in memory** (D4): the widest value is computed by measuring every row's display string for that column with a canvas `measureText` against the column's actual font — cheap and synchronous (~1,200 rows is sub-millisecond, no layout thrash) — which also sidesteps the **virtualized** grid (only ~30 rows are ever in the DOM, so DOM measurement of all rows is impossible). Result is clamped to the existing 64–640px bounds and includes the header label width. Design notes for the 3c session: (1) gesture is **double-click** on the existing resize separator (single-drag still resizes), and it needs a **keyboard twin** (e.g. Enter on the focused separator) since double-click is pointer-only — the a11y gate D79; (2) **non-text columns** need rules — Photo (avatar) and the Name composite and the Course **chip** aren't plain text, so either give them a sensible fixed auto-fit or exclude them; (3) auto-fit measures at the **current** root font-size (N24), so after a font-size change the user re-triggers it — which also makes auto-fit the natural escape hatch for the Larger-setting truncation noted in N24/N21. Persist the resulting width in the lens like any manual resize (N16).

### N28 — The export-audit endpoint is `POST /api/exports` (implements D92; Phase 3c)
D92 mandated a "thin notify endpoint" for the client-side CSV export but left its path unspecified. Phase 3c defines it as **`POST /api/exports`** (API-SPEC §4a): manager/admin-only (the same gate as the action bar, D41), body `{ scope: "selection" | "view", count }`, response `204`, writing one `export` audit entry (actor, scope, count, timestamp — names/counts, never data, per §6.1/D61). The audit entry's `targetId` is omitted because a whole-directory export has no single target; `AuditEntry` gained optional `scope`/`count` and an optional `targetId` to carry this. The SPA's ping (`notifyExport`) is fire-and-forget — the download has already happened, so a failed ping never surfaces to the user.

### N29 — Course (majors) display names: a bundled interim vocabulary (Phase 3c follow-up)
The Directory's Course filter and the course chips needed human-readable names ("6-3 — Computer Science and Engineering"), but DATABASE-SCHEMA §6.2 / D69 specify the `majors` vocabulary as a runtime-editable **Firestore collection** (loaded via the `/api/profiles` `majors` field, currently `[]`), which isn't built yet. As an interim, the display names for **the codes the dataset currently uses** are bundled in `@pbe/shared` (`majors.ts`: `MAJORS`/`MAJOR_CODES`/`courseName`/`courseLabel`) — the same way `geo.ts` bundles country names. The Course filter labels and the chip's hover/accessible name use `courseLabel`; the chip's visible text stays the **code** (how MIT majors are named). A generator test asserts every emitted code resolves in the vocabulary (no orphan codes). The Firestore-backed, admin-editable vocabulary (D69) remains future work; moving to it is an API-internal change since the SPA already consumes names through a lookup. Forrest's call (2026-06-28): scope the interim to codes-in-use, not the full MIT catalog.

### N30 — Phase 4 re-planned after the 4a-1 live review (Profile page split into seven sessions)
Forrest live-tested **4a-1** (the Profile view/edit spine, committed `679a13e`) on staging and gave a batch of feedback. The original three-session Phase 4 (4a/4b/4c) is re-planned into **seven** sessions (see CODING-PROJECT-PLAN §Phase 4): **4a-1** (done), **4a-2** role impersonation + the "Profile" avatar shortcut (N31), **4a-3** Profile navigation & the unsaved guard (N33 + OFC-65), **4b-1** the special controls (the original 4b), **4b-2** edit-form polish — layout/validation/copy (N35), **4c** (original scope unchanged), and a new **4d** prev/next through the directory set, promoted to MVP (N32). The split is locked now (Forrest's call): 4b genuinely held two coherent units (make the deferred fields editable, then lay out/validate/polish the now-complete field set), and the two new features (impersonation, prev/next) are net-new scope. The union of these sessions covers **all** of original-Phase-4 scope plus the feedback — there is no separate "return to 4a" step; 4a-1's one partial item (the back-button guard) is finished in 4a-3.

### N31 — Role impersonation: admins/managers step **down** a role for testing (server-side effective role)
**New feature (Forrest, 4a-1 review; built in 4a-2).** There is no easy way to test what managers/brothers see — only admins. Add **step-down impersonation**: an admin may impersonate manager or brother, a manager may impersonate brother (never escalate; brothers cannot impersonate). The crux is that it is **server-side**, not a client flag: an **effective role** is stored on the session alongside the immutable **real role**, and `/api/me`, `/api/profiles`, `/api/profiles/:id`, and the write-capability checks (`canActOnProfile`/`canWriteField`) all use the **effective** role — so the lower projection is what's actually downloaded and the lower powers are actually enforced (a client-only flip would leave the admin holding the full dataset and test nothing). `/api/me` returns `{ role: effective, realRole, impersonating }`; the masthead shows the impersonation items and "Stop impersonation" gated on **realRole**, and the start/stop endpoint checks **realRole** so a user can never lock themselves out. Identity (`profileId`) is unchanged — only the role. Switching reloads the page so the lower projection is fetched. **Available in production**, not staging-only: an admin already sees all data, so impersonation only *restricts* their view (and is genuinely useful for support — "what does this brother see?"); start/stop is **audited** (D61 stream). This touches the session/auth core (D125), hence its own session. **Built in 4a-2 (2026-06-30).** Implementation notes: the **user-facing wording is "View as"** (Forrest, 4a-2) — the avatar menu says "View as Brother" / "Stop viewing as Brother" and the masthead shows a "Viewing as <role>" pill, because nobody is being deceived and the object is a role, not a person; the **mechanism keeps the "impersonate" vocabulary** internally (the `/api/me/impersonate` endpoints, the `impersonate.start`/`impersonate.stop` audit actions carrying a non-PII `targetRole`, the `canImpersonate` helper). The effective role lives in `Session.effectiveRole` behind an `effectiveRole(session)` accessor and is persisted via `SessionStore.setEffectiveRole` (cold-start-safe per D125).

### N32 — Prev/next profile navigation is MVP (forward/back through the directory's set)
**Promoted to MVP (Forrest, 4a-1 review; built in 4d).** From a Profile page the user can step **forward/back through the Directory's currently filtered + sorted set**, in that order — the same need the Ghost newsletter theme already had to satisfy (readers complained about having to bounce back to a list between articles), so Book will draw the same complaints without it. Approach (4d): when navigating from a Directory row, stash that row's **ordered id-list** (and the Directory's URL) so the Profile page can resolve prev/next and the "back to where I was" target; a cold deep-link with no stashed set simply hides the prev/next controls (graceful), and the design can later be upgraded to re-derive the set from the URL's filter/sort state if always-on is wanted. Prev/next are ordinary push navigations between display pages (each shows its own correct record), so they coexist cleanly with the N33 edit-history model.

### N33 — Edit mode must not accumulate browser history (no anachronistic edit pages); built on a data router
**Refines D31/D43 (Forrest, 4a-1 review; built in 4a-3).** With edit as its own URL and the page refetching current data on every history entry, repeated save→edit→save cycles pile up display↔edit entries that, walked backward, all show *current* data (confusing/anachronistic). New model: clicking **Edit pushes one** history entry (so Back from edit → display), and **Save and Cancel pop it** (`navigate(-1)`) rather than pushing a new display entry — so no matter how many edit cycles, history stays `[…, Directory, display]` and **Back from display always reaches the Directory**, never a stale edit page. Edges: the post-save toast moves to a non-URL channel; a direct deep-link to `/edit` (nothing to pop) falls back to replacing with the display URL. This is built atop the **React-Router data-router migration** (OFC-65) that also gives the unified `useBlocker` unsaved-changes guard (the back-button half 4a-1 left out). Same session also removes the **redundant post-save GET** — Save currently does PATCH *then* the display remounts and refetches; the PATCH response already returns the updated record, so dropping the second round-trip fixes the slow Save→display transition Forrest noticed.

**Built in 4a-3 (2026-06-30).** Implementation notes: the app moved from `<BrowserRouter>` to `createBrowserRouter` + `<RouterProvider>` with the tree `RootLayout` (holds `NuqsAdapter` inside the router) → `GateLayout` (session gate + `AppShell`) → `{Directory, brother/:id}`; the theme/font/**session** providers wrap `RouterProvider` (none read router state). The Profile page became a **shared layout route**: `ProfileContainer` (`brother/:id`) owns the fetch, `record`/`etag`, `submit`, and the toast, hosting `view` (index) and `edit` children via `Outlet` context — so view↔edit no longer remounts, which is what lets the **PATCH response be reused** (the old GET is gone) and lets the **toast live in container state** (the non-URL channel). Exit nav is decided by **history-state tags**: the Edit link carries `state:{fromProfile:true}` so `exitEdit()` pops (`navigate(-1)`) or, on a cold deep-link to `/edit`, replaces with the display URL; Directory row navigations carry `state:{fromDirectory:true}` so the **"← Directory"** affordance pops back to the actual Directory entry (restoring its URL filters and history-state scroll) or falls back to `/`. The guard is two-layer: `useUnsavedGuard` keeps `beforeunload`, and `useBlocker(dirty)` (now available under the data router) catches Back / in-app links / Cancel through one `ConfirmDialog`, with a `bypass` ref flipped on a deliberate Save so it never self-prompts. **Forrest's 4a-3 addendum:** the masthead crest + wordmark is now a `<Link to="/">` "home" affordance (conventional logo behavior) — a fresh navigation to the Directory available on **every** page (Directory, Profile, the future Admin page), deliberately distinct from "← Directory" (which restores where you were); in edit mode it flows through the same dirty-form blocker. The History-API utilities (`useScrollRestoration`, `useHistoryFlag`) coexist with the data router's own `history.state` keys (they merge, not replace) — re-verified by the existing scroll-restoration and sort-history e2e. Tests: `e2e/profile-nav-4a3.spec.ts` (the no-anachronistic-history walk, the no-redundant-GET assertion, the Back-button and in-app-link blocker, ← Directory + logo home, axe 2.2 AA); full gate green (296 unit + 18 emulator + 68 e2e).

**Scroll-restoration follow-ups (live-tested by Forrest, 2026-06-30; commits `514a950`/`37cc6b2`/`8c23bd6`).** The data-router migration surfaced three latent bugs in `useScrollRestoration` (the D31 Directory scroll save/restore), each found in live staging testing and fixed in turn: (1) it keyed the offset by `location.search`, but nuqs writes the Directory's query params (sort, the `?cols=` lens mirror) *after* mount, so the forward save and the back-restore used different keys on any view carrying URL state → now keyed by the **stable per-entry `location.key`**; (2) under an active **Name Search** the restore fired against the interim main-thread substring set before the Web Worker grew it (D110/D123), clamping the offset → restoration now gates on a `settled` signal from `useNameSearch` (worker has answered *this* query) and won't *save* before it has restored; (3) the decisive one — on the Back remount the restore ran before the **TanStack virtualizer had sized the list** (tiny `scrollHeight`), clamping `scrollTop` to 0 → restoration now **re-applies across animation frames until the offset sticks**. The committed regression test (`e2e/directory-scroll-4a3.spec.ts`) reproduces the worker + virtualizer-sizing race with return-side fetch latency. (Tooling note for future built-asset debugging: `playwright.config.ts` sets `reuseExistingServer: !CI`, so local iteration can silently run against a stale preview build — kill port 4173 and run with `CI=1`.)

### N34 — `middleName` is retained (it is used by Name Search and CSV export, not edit-only)
**Resolved (Forrest, 4a-1 review).** The question was raised whether `middleName` could be dropped as apparently edit-only. Audit (2026-06-29): it is **not** edit-only — it is an indexed **Name Search** field (`packages/name-search` tokenizes it, so a brother is findable by middle name) and a **CSV export** column (`packages/shared/src/csv.ts`). Dropping it would remove both capabilities and churn the schema across every delivered doc, for a field that is harmless to keep. **Kept.** (Brothers who want a formal full name still also have `fullLegalName`.)

### N35 — 4a-1 live-review polish bundle (copy, layout, validation, toggle) → 4b-2
**Forrest, 4a-1 review; built in 4b-2.** A bundle of edit-form fixes:
- **Copy** (consent + display): MITAA → "May be shared with the MIT Alumni Association." / "Will not be shared with the MIT Alumni Association."; newsletter → "You will receive PBE News by email."; the address toggle is about the **whole address** (the toggle governs whether *any* address is visible to peers — copy-only, **no projection change**), so its text says "address," not "city & state"; the section/field label **"Majors" → "Courses"** (the data field stays `majors`; matches the Directory's N15 rename); the **mug name** is shown on the display page.
- **Directory-Listing toggle reversal:** present it as the **positive "Listed in the directory"** (on = listed/visible, matching every other privacy switch); the stored field stays `unlisted` (a presentation flip, no data change).
- **Layout** (revises the delivered visual-design pass — update COMPONENTS.md to match): a **larger headshot** (stored 512², shown 120²; enlarge on desktop, shrink on mobile) and **fuller use of the second column** (contact beside the enlarged photo; spouse/courses to the right of employer), keeping DOM order = reading order (WCAG 1.3.2, D32). Also the **privacy-toggle row alignment**: lay the first three switches out with the same insets as the boxed subgroups so all switches and `?` buttons align.
- **Validation:** add **`noValidate`** to the form to suppress the browser's native validation bubble (the "different colors" Forrest saw — native UI, not ours), leaving only our inline errors; and **stronger phone normalization** in the shared validator — require a country code (default `+1`), and for NANP (`+1`) numbers accept `(xxx) xxx-xxxx` or `xxx-xxx-xxxx` and reformat to one canonical form on save (international numbers still allowed, so NANP formatting applies only to `+1`).

## Phase 4b-1 implementation notes (2026-06-30, the special controls)

### N36 — The special controls: one Radix-backed Combobox, the address block goes editable, repeatable rows sanitized centrally *(Linear: OFC-179)*
Phase **4b-1** turned the four read-only edit fields (D46/D37) into real editors. The decisions made building it:

- **The headless-library call landed on Radix Popover** (Forrest's call, this session). One reusable `Combobox` (`apps/web/src/components/Combobox.tsx`) composes the floating panel / portal / collision handling / outside-click from `@radix-ui/react-popover`, and the **listbox keyboarding** (`role="listbox"`/`option`, `aria-activedescendant`, ↑/↓/Home/End/Enter/Esc, type-to-filter) over it — Radix has no activedescendant *combobox* primitive, so that logic is hand-written but lives in exactly one tested place. Both the majors "Add a course" picker and the Big-Brother typeahead consume it. This is the dependency the **4c** crop modal (Radix Dialog) and the **Phase 6** `?` toggle-tips (Radix Popover) will reuse. The WAI-ARIA listbox pattern (non-focusable options on `<div>`s) trips two Biome a11y rules (`useSemanticElements`, `useFocusableInteractive`) that model only the roving-tabindex pattern; both are turned **off for this one file** via a scoped `biome.json` `overrides` entry — the pattern is correct (axe 2.2 AA passes), the linter just doesn't model it.
- **The address block became fully editable** (street1–3, city, postal, country, state/province), not just the subdivision — you can't have a country-driven State/Province without its surrounding fields editable, and 4b-2's "fuller second column" is layout polish, not field enablement. The country-driven rule (D37) is a pure, unit-tested helper (`address-edit.ts` `applyCountryChange`): US/CA → a code dropdown (name shown, code stored), anywhere else → free text; new/blank addresses default `country` to `US`; switching to a country whose **controlled vocabulary** can't hold the current subdivision clears it with a brief note (a free-text country has no vocabulary, so a prior value is kept as free text, not cleared).
- **Big Brother + Little Brothers source the roster from a session-cached bulk read.** Both need the whole dataset; `bigBrotherId` is `public`, so the existing brother projection already carries every pointer. `useRoster` (`apps/web/src/lib/useRoster.ts`) memoizes one `GET /api/profiles` in a module-level promise, reused across profile opens (byte-frugal for the slow-link audience — [[project-audience-slow-connections]]); relationships render progressively while it loads. Derived Little Brothers are the reverse `bigBrotherId` edge, read-only, never stored; the existence/no-cycle check stays server-authoritative (a loop returns 422 → the existing inline-error path). The Directory keeps its own separate bulk fetch for now (a future dedup).
- **Progressive-disclosure repeatables keep a trailing blank row in the draft for display, sanitized out before validation/diff/save.** `repeatables.ts` `sanitizeRepeatables` drops fully-blank link/contact rows (they aren't data) before the shared validator, the patch diff, and the dirty bit see them; blank rows only ever sit at the end (Add is disabled while one is open), so a kept row's sanitized index still matches its rendered index and the per-row error lookup stays aligned. A partly-filled link (label, no URL) is kept and flagged. **`ProfileView` gained a Links display** (`rel="noopener noreferrer"`, D107) so saved links aren't write-only.
- **Two pre-existing 4a e2e locators were tightened** (not behaviour changes): the emergency-contact editor adds a second "Email" field, and the majors editor's dnd-kit context renders its own empty `role="status"` live region — so the 4a Email-field and save-toast assertions are now scoped to their region rather than matching globally.

Bundle: shipped JS rose to **194.2 KB brotli** (from ~149 KB) — Radix Popover's popper/floating-ui/dismissable-layer stack — still within the 250 KB budget (D74), and a one-time cost amortized across 4c and Phase 6.

**Live-review fixes (Forrest, 2026-06-30, three items; the fourth — phone validation/canonical formatting — is correctly the N35 / 4b-2 work and was deferred there):**
- **Big-Brother changes now propagate to the *other* brother's derived Little-Brother list.** Little Brothers are computed from the session-cached roster, and the cache was a snapshot — so after re-pointing A's `bigBrotherId` to B, B's page still showed the pre-save edge. `useRoster` became a tiny subscribable store (`useSyncExternalStore`); a successful save calls `applyProfileToRoster(record)` to patch the saved record (name / class year / `bigBrotherId`) into the cache in place, so navigating to the new (or former) Big Brother recomputes the reverse edge with no second download.
- **One chip for every relationship.** Big Brother and Little Brothers now render through a single `RelationshipChip` in **both** view and edit (a calm pill + name link; the edit Big-Brother chip adds the × remove). Resolves the inconsistency Forrest saw — a large coloured link for Big Brother vs. small muted chips for Little Brothers in view, and a different chip-with-coloured-link in edit.
- **Leaving US/CA clears a stranded subdivision code.** `applyCountryChange` was keeping the value whenever the new country had no controlled vocabulary, which stranded a 2-letter code as bare free text (US `MA` → United Kingdom left "MA"). Corrected rule: keep the value only if it stays meaningful — under a new **controlled** country it must be a valid code in that country's set; under a **free-text** country it is kept only if the *old* country was also free text. So US/CA → anywhere non-US/CA now clears with the note, US↔CA still clears a non-matching code, and genuine free-text region data survives free-text→free-text.

## Phase 4b-2 implementation notes (2026-07-01, the edit-form polish bundle)

### N37 — 4b-2 built: the N35 polish bundle, plus how each item landed *(Linear: OFC-177)*
Phase **4b-2** implemented the N35 live-review bundle. The decisions/details made building it:

- **Phone canonicalization is one shared function, server-authoritative.** `normalizePhone` (in `packages/shared/src/validation.ts`, exported) returns the single stored form or `null`, so validation (`null` → invalid) and the write path (non-null → store it) share one parser — no drift. **NANP (country code `+1`) → `+1 (617) 555-1234`; every other international number → E.164** (`+` then digits). A bare number defaults to `+1` when it is a NANP length (10, or 11 with a leading `1`); otherwise it needs an explicit country code and is rejected. The API PATCH path (`profiles.ts` `canonicalizePhones`) rewrites both the primary `phone` **and each `emergencyContacts[].phone`** before validation and write (Forrest's call: both fields, server-side); an unparseable value is left as-is so the validator still reports it inline rather than dropping it, and an empty string (cleared field) is left alone. The PATCH response carries the canonical value, which the container reuses (no post-save GET, N33), so the reformat is visible immediately. **Note (factual):** Forrest grouped Mexico with US/Canada, but Mexico is country code **+52**, outside the NANP — so Mexican numbers render as E.164, not the `+1 (…)` form; US and Canada (both genuinely +1) get the pretty form. Matches N35 as written; a Mexico-specific format would be separate work.
- **The directory-listing switch is a presentation inversion, not a data change.** The `unlisted` field is unchanged; the switch is shown as the positive **"Listed in the directory"** (on = listed) via `CONSENT_COPY.listed` with the value/onChange inverted at the call site (`!unlisted`). The view-page preferences digest shows the off-state ("you don't appear …") with a hollow marker.
- **Mug name surfaced on the display page** as a quoted nickname under the name (it was editable but write-only — the same gap 4b-1 fixed for Links). **"Majors" → "Courses"** completed on the display page and in the reconcile-notice `FIELD_LABELS` (the editor and Directory already renamed; data field stays `majors`).
- **`noValidate` on the form** suppresses the browser's native validation bubble, leaving only the inline errors.
- **Responsive headshot** (96² mobile → 132² desktop) via a `--headshot-size` CSS variable set at the `sm` breakpoint, read by both the `<img>` and a new `Avatar` `sizeVar` prop so photo and initials-fallback scale together. **Privacy-toggle alignment:** the first three per-field switches got the same box insets (border + `p-3`, transparent) as the boxed subgroups so switches and `?` buttons line up.
- **"Fuller second column" reflow (first cut, for staging review — N35 said build the best attempt).** Both view and edit: **Professional & personal runs full width with an internal two-column grid** — employer / job title / links on the left, **spouse and courses to the right** — and Relationships moved to its own full-width block beneath it. Contact / Emergency and the restricted Privacy / Record-status pairs keep their two-up rows; "contact beside the enlarged photo" was read conservatively (Contact stays the first block below the identity band rather than being lifted into the photo band, which the 132px-photo-vs-tall-field math makes awkward and which would orphan Emergency). To be refined against the rendered staging page. All 29 profile e2e specs (incl. axe 2.2 AA on view + edit) stay green; bundle 194.7 KB brotli.

**Second polish pass (Forrest live-testing staging, 2026-07-01):**
- **Phone bug fixed:** a `+1` number that wasn't exactly 11 digits fell through to the generic E.164 branch and was wrongly accepted (`+16175551`, `+161755513456789`). Since country code 1 is the whole NANP and no other code begins with 1, `normalizePhone` now requires an explicit-`+1` number to be exactly 11 digits or rejects it. (Bare numbers were already handled: only 10, or 11-with-leading-1, are accepted.)
- **International (E.164) display left unchanged — a deliberate no:** Forrest asked whether we could insert a space after the country code (e.g. `+44 117…`) without maintaining a country-code table. We can't reliably: ITU-T E.164 country codes are **variable length (1–3 digits)** and, apart from the single-digit zones (1 = NANP, 7 = Russia/Kazakhstan), telling a 2-digit code from a 3-digit one **requires the actual assignment table** (they're prefix-free but not length-derivable — e.g. `+44` UK vs `+420` Czechia). libphonenumber does this but is ~200 KB+, which would blow the bundle. So per Forrest's stated condition ("if we'd have to build a database of country codes, leave the display unchanged"), E.164 numbers render as `+` then digits with no interior space.
- **Field-name labels unified.** One `FIELD_LABEL_CLASS` (uppercase, letter-spaced, muted — the display read-out style) now drives every field label in **both** view and edit (`FieldShell`, `LockedField`, and the ad-hoc Courses / Links / Big-Brother / Little-Brothers labels), replacing the edit form's inconsistent sentence-case/foreground/semibold mix.
- **Edit-page section & field wording/layout:** added an **"Identity"** section eyebrow over the name band; `fullLegalName` helper "compound name" → "compound names"; **"Constitution ID" → "Constitution signer number"** (UI only — the field is the record id; brothers call it the signer number) and narrowed it to a single identity-grid cell (was full-width, oddly wide for a 4-digit value); **address block reordered** to City / State-Province then Postal / Country, with **"Postal code" → "Postal/ZIP code"** and **"State / Province" → "State/Province"**; Relationships little-brothers note → "Set automatically based on who names this brother as their Big Brother."; consent copy → "You won't receive PBE News by email.", "You'll be emailed when someone replies to your comments.", "You won't be emailed when someone replies to your comments."
- **The "Saved" toast moved from the bottom to a third down the viewport** (`top-1/3`) — the bottom placement on a long profile was easy to miss.

**Third polish pass (Forrest live-testing staging, 2026-07-01):**
- **Links row alignment fixed.** The links editor grid was `sm:items-end`, so a validation error under the **Label** field grew that column and shoved the **URL** field (and Remove button) down. Switched to `sm:items-start` and gave the Remove button a label-height spacer, so the two inputs and the button stay aligned regardless of an error hanging below either field.
- **N38 — US ZIP validation (US only).** `validateProfile` now checks that a **US** `address.postalCode` matches `NNNNN` or `NNNNN-NNNN` (the ZIP+4 form); every other country's postal code is left unvalidated — the format space outside the US is too large and varied to police, and ~all of the membership is US. *(Linear: OFC-178)* Threaded as an inline `postalError` on the Postal/ZIP field (shows on Save, like the country/state errors).
- **Big-Brother search now uses the Directory's Name Search.** The typeahead was doing only the `Combobox`'s built-in substring filter, so "Bill" found no Williams. It now runs the **same `useNameSearch`** (Fuse fuzzy + Beider-Morse phonetics + the common-nickname dictionary in the Web Worker, with the instant substring fallback — D35/D110/D123) the Directory uses: the `Combobox` gained an `onQueryChange` callback so a parent can drive matching, and a scoped `BigBrotherPicker` (mounted only while the picker is on screen — a brother with no Big Brother — so the index isn't built on every profile open) feeds the matched-id set back through the `Combobox`'s `filter`. New e2e proves "Bill → William Hayes". No bundle change (name-search was already shipped for the Directory).

## Phase 4c/4d pre-session planning decisions (2026-07-02)

*A planning review of the two remaining Phase-4 sessions was run before implementation, against the delivered docs (API-SPEC §§3–6, D28/D47–D51/D80/D94/D98/D115/D122) and the shipped code (the capability matrix, the `/img/*` route, the Dockerfile, the 4a-3 navigation state). It surfaced one spec hole, one mis-sliced Phase-5 deferral, and several pre-decidable implementation calls; Forrest reviewed and approved each on 2026-07-02. Recorded pre-build — with deliberately prescriptive detail — so the implementing sessions execute rather than re-derive. Tickets: 4c-1/4c-2 = OFC-69/OFC-70; 4d = OFC-67.*

### N39 — Phase 4c splits into 4c-1 (headshot pipeline + image visibility) and 4c-2 (verification, mark-deceased, admin controls)
The former single session 4c is two sessions, each with its own tests-green gate. **4c-1:** the headshot crop-and-stage pipeline (`PUT`/`DELETE /api/profiles/{id}/headshot`, the react-easy-crop Radix Dialog, the sharp encode, N42), the `/img/*` strict-path/per-record-visibility hardening (N43), and the D94 purge infrastructure. **4c-2:** the verification surfacing + `POST /api/profiles/{id}/verify` (D48), the mark-deceased endpoint and In Memoriam flow (N40), and the admin on-profile controls — `DELETE /api/profiles/{id}`, `PUT /api/users/{id}/role` with the last-admin safeguard (N44), and the de-brother/reinstate UI over `PUT /api/profiles/{id}/debrothered` — all against the `GhostLifecycle` seam (N41).
**Why:** honoring the review's findings makes the original 4c six server actions (each with audit + emulator tests) plus a crop modal, verification UI, mark-deceased flow, admin controls, image-route hardening, and an infra change — comfortably the largest session in Phase 4, larger than 4a or 4b, both of which ended up splitting (the N30 precedent). The split line is natural: 4c-1 is the image slice end-to-end; 4c-2 is the privileged-action slice (its endpoints share the dedicated-audited-server-action pattern).

### N40 — Mark-deceased is a dedicated endpoint, `PUT /api/profiles/{id}/deceased`, and the Book-side consent force-off + D80 snapshot land with it in 4c-2 (only the Ghost *push* is Phase 5)
The planning review found a genuine spec hole: the capability matrix (`packages/shared/src/capabilities.ts`) classifies `deceased` as `protected` — unwritable via PATCH by every role, "owned by a dedicated server action" — but API-SPEC specified no such endpoint (verify, de-brother, delete, and change-role all had one). The endpoint is now specified (API-SPEC §3) mirroring the de-brother shape: `PUT /api/profiles/{id}/deceased` with body `{ "deceased": true, …the five D122 fields }` (or `false` to reverse), **manager/admin** auth, audited. Because PATCH rejects the `deceased` field entirely, **later staff edits to the deceased fields** (fixing a typo'd obituary link) also ride this endpoint — a re-`PUT` with `deceased: true` and the corrected fields. **Scope correction to the original 4c ticket:** the ticket deferred "deceased-forces-both-flags-off" to Phase 5 wholesale; that mis-slices D80. Marking deceased forces both email-consent flags off *in Book's data*, **snapshots** the prior consent + verification state at mark time, restores the snapshot on un-mark, and stamps `newsletterConsentChangedAt` — all pure Firestore logic with no Ghost involved, and it ships in **4c-2**. Phase 5 adds only the *push* of the resulting state to Ghost.
**Why:** if 4c-2 shipped mark-deceased without the snapshot, any brother marked deceased before Phase 5 would have nothing to restore on un-mark (exactly the silent consent-data loss D80 exists to prevent), and Phase 5 would be retrofitting semantics into a live flow. The `newsletterConsentChangedAt` stamp is also what D103's most-recent-change-wins reconcile keys on, so it must be written at the true change time, not backfilled.

### N41 — Delete and de-brother are coded against an injected `GhostLifecycle` seam, stubbed until Phase 5
`DELETE /api/profiles/{id}` and `PUT /api/profiles/{id}/debrothered` are specified **Ghost-first** (delete/create the Ghost member first; abort cleanly on failure with a `502`, Book untouched — D96/D98/D115), but the Ghost write path is Phase 5. 4c-2 defines a `GhostLifecycle` interface (`deleteMember` / `createMember`) injected through `BuildServerOptions` exactly like `IdentityProvider` and `AuditLog`, and implements both endpoints' fixed ordering against it. The 4c-2 implementation is a stub that succeeds and logs (`"ghost-lifecycle: would delete member for profile <id>"`); unit tests use a **failing fake** to prove the abort-clean contract (Ghost step fails → 502 `ghost_delete_failed`/`ghost_create_failed`, no Firestore/GCS/cache mutation). Phase 5 swaps in the real client without touching the endpoints.
**Why:** the ordering and failure semantics are the hard, testable part of these endpoints; leaving them as a Phase-5 TODO would bake in a shape Phase 5 has to retrofit, and the seam pattern (dev/real identity provider, injectable audit log) is already the codebase's established way to defer an integration without deferring its contract.

### N42 — Headshot pipeline implementation calls: client downscale, fresh `ETag` on the image writes, no D28 coupling, and the sharp/Fastify/Cloud Run practicalities
Settled pre-build for 4c-1 (all reflected in API-SPEC §6):
- **The client downscales before upload.** The crop dialog renders the cropped region through a canvas to **≤1024×1024 JPEG (quality ≈0.9)** and uploads that — a multi-megabyte phone photo must not cross the wire of a DSL-class connection ([[project-audience-slow-connections]]), and the canvas re-encode strips EXIF/GPS metadata (a privacy win). The server still magic-byte-checks and re-encodes regardless (never trust client bytes — D107). Accepted upload types are `image/jpeg` and `image/png` only; the file input accept-lists those and the client shows a clear error for anything else (notably `.heic` — iPhone *Safari* converts HEIC→JPEG on file inputs, but desktop browsers cannot decode HEIC in a canvas); the server's `415` is the backstop.
- **`PUT`/`DELETE …/headshot` return a fresh `ETag`** (plus the updated `hasHeadshot`/`headshotVersion`), and `ProfileContainer` applies both to its held record. The image write advances the profile document, so the client's concurrency token goes stale mid-Save; since 4a-3 the container deliberately reuses the PATCH response instead of refetching, so without this a photo-included Save (D50 order: text PATCH → photo PUT) leaves a stale token and the user's *next* edit hits a spurious 412. The server-side write is unconditional (no `If-Match` on the image sub-resource) but must advance the `ProfileCache` token in lock-step via the existing `applyUpdate` mechanism (read-your-writes, D83).
- **Headshot changes do not participate in the D28 verification coupling.** The auto-verify/courtesy-unverify side-effect remains defined on the PATCH path only; a photo replace/remove by any role leaves verification untouched. (Verification attests the textual record; one simple rule beats an owner/staff asymmetry. Corollary: a photo-only Save produces a no-op PATCH — the 2c deep-equal short-circuit — and must not raise the courtesy-unverify dialog.)
- **sharp is an `apps/api` production dependency** — a native module, kept external to the esbuild bundle like every other runtime dep; the Dockerfile's pruned-`node_modules` runtime stage ships it with zero deploy changes (Cloud Build's `npm ci` installs the linux-x64 prebuilt; Windows dev gets win32-x64). Pin the version; implement the ≈40 MP decode cap with `limitInputPixels`.
- **Fastify needs a raw-image content-type parser and a per-route `bodyLimit`** on the upload route (the default is 1 MB and would 413 everything); oversize uploads get a graceful `413`. With the client downscale in place a legitimate upload is well under 2 MB; set the limit at **8 MB** as margin.
- **Cloud Run memory guard:** the instance holds the profile cache and `--max-instances=1`, so a decode spike is a whole-app OOM risk. Bump the service to **1 GiB** (staging deploy flags + `provision-staging.sh` + the prod runbook note) and serialize uploads through a small in-process semaphore (concurrency 1) — uploads are rare; queueing them is invisible.
- **The D94 purge is implemented, not just asserted:** on replace/remove the server **deletes the superseded GCS objects** (each version is a distinct key — nothing else ever removes them), and the bucket gets **object versioning + a 90-day noncurrent-age lifecycle rule** (added to `provision-staging.sh` and the infra README, and to the prod provisioning notes) so a deleted object remains recoverable for D94's window.

### N43 — `/img/*` parses its path strictly and enforces per-record visibility at the *effective* role (4c-1)
The Phase-1 image route streams any existing object under the session gate; its own comment defers per-record visibility to Phase 4, and ENGINEERING-DESIGN §6.6 lists that check among the security-critical exhaustive tests — but it was absent from the 4c ticket. 4c-1 lands it: the route accepts **only** `headshots/{id}/{version}.webp` and `thumbnails/{id}/{version}.webp` (anything else → 404, which also forecloses reading arbitrary bucket objects through the rewrite), resolves `{id}` against the in-memory cache, and returns **404 when the caller's effective role** (4a-2 View-as included) **cannot see that record** — an unlisted or de-brothered brother's image is withheld from a brother-role caller, mirroring the record projection (D126, API-SPEC §6).
**Why:** 4c-1 is when real member photos start existing, so the window between "photos exist" and "visibility enforced" should be zero; and the strict parse is cheaper than any allowlist reasoning about what else might land in the bucket.

### N44 — `PUT /api/users/{id}/role` creates the `users` document if absent (amends API-SPEC §5's "404 if no such user")
`users` documents are created lazily on first sign-in (R20), so "404 if no such user" would make a brother who has never signed in un-promotable — not what an admin expects from the role selector. Amended: the endpoint 404s only when no **profile** with that id exists; a missing `users` document for an existing brother is **created with the given role** (the R20 create-if-absent pattern, `{ id, role }`, stars untouched). The last-admin invariant is checked server-side against a Firestore `users where role == admin` query (a rare action; trivial at `--max-instances=1`), and every change is audited with before/after role (D106; "before" is `brother` for a created-if-absent doc, the role a first sign-in would have received).

### N45 — 4d prev/next rides per-entry history state with a `directoryDelta` counter; "← Directory" becomes `navigate(-delta)` *(Linear: OFC-171)*
