The OFC-67 stash approach is confirmed, with the mechanism fixed pre-build: **(1)** navigating from a Directory row passes the ordered id-list of the *current filtered+sorted view* (the already-computed `rows`) via React Router `location.state` — ~1,200 ids ≈ 8 KB, persisted in `history.state` so it survives a same-tab reload — from **all three** entry points (whole-row click, name link, card link). **(2)** Each history entry's state carries `directoryDelta`: the row click sets `1`, and every Prev/Next push re-carries the stash with `directoryDelta: previous + 1`. **(3)** "← Directory" changes from `navigate(-1)`-when-`fromDirectory` to **`navigate(-directoryDelta)`** — landing on the *true* Directory entry as a POP, so the existing `location.key`-keyed scroll restoration and the URL's filters work unchanged; because each entry carries its own delta, the scheme stays correct if the user walks Back mid-chain. A cold deep-link (no state) hides the controls (the ticket's graceful degradation). **(4)** Stale-set behavior: a stashed id can stop resolving between stash and click (deleted, de-brothered, unlisted, newly deceased — 4c makes this real); MVP shows the normal not-found state with prev/next still rendered so the user steps past it (no auto-skip). **(5)** Prev/next render only on the **display** page (edit keeps the N33 one-entry model and the blocker); accessible names carry the target ("Next: James Smyth ’84"), ends of the set disable, targets ≥24 px, and a "12 of 431" position readout (nearly free from the stash index) aids orientation. The "re-derive the set from the URL" upgrade is deliberately **not** built (it would drag the worker-based Name Search re-execution and OFC-68 into scope for no MVP benefit).
**Why:** 4a-3's data-router migration already paid most of 4d's tax; the delta counter is the one genuinely new mechanism, and it exists because a prev/next *chain* breaks the 4a-3 assumption that the Directory entry is always exactly one step back.

### N46 — The concurrency `ETag` is a quoted entity-tag; `If-Match` is normalized before compare (OFC-92 / OFC-90)
Book's Phase-2 write path emitted the optimistic-concurrency token as a **raw, unquoted** `ETag` (`ETag: 1751490000.123`) and compared the echoed `If-Match` byte-for-byte. HTTP entity-tags are defined as *quoted* strings, and an intermediary — Firebase Hosting fronting Cloud Run (D126) — or the browser may quote or `W/`-weaken the value in transit. If any hop rewrote it, the echoed `If-Match` would no longer string-equal the stored token, the conditional write's precondition would never match, and **every legitimate save would return a spurious `412` in production** — invisible to the `app.inject` unit tests, which never cross an HTTP layer. Fix (API-SPEC §1.4): emit a **spec-compliant quoted** `ETag` (RFC 9110 §8.8.3) and **normalize** an incoming `If-Match` — strip an optional `W/` weak prefix and the surrounding quotes — back to the raw `<sec>.<nanos>` token before the conditional write. Paired change (OFC-90): a token that is not `^\d+\.\d+$` (a bare word, `*`, a truncated value) now decodes to a *failed precondition* (**412** reconcile) instead of constructing `Timestamp(NaN)` and escaping the store's `code`-only catch as a **500**. Internally the server still deals only in the raw `updateTime` token; the quoting is purely the wire representation. Verified against a real staging save through Firebase Hosting — a first save and an immediate second save both round-trip cleanly.
**Why:** the token is a *wire contract*, not an internal detail. A future client — or any caching/proxy layer placed in front of `GET`/`PATCH /api/profiles/{id}` — must know the tag ships quoted and that the server strips `W/`+quotes on the way back in; a byte-for-byte re-implementation that assumes the old raw form would silently reintroduce the 412 storm. Part of the OFC-86 Phase-2 code-review remediation (PR #12), which also hardened the shared string validators (JSON `null` → 422 not 500, OFC-89), made record hydration fault-tolerant so one malformed Firestore doc can't 500 the whole directory (OFC-91), inverted `projectSelf`'s safe default onto the exhaustive visibility table (OFC-97), and fixed the email-index self-ambiguity that could lock a brother out of sign-in/edit (OFC-87/OFC-88).

### N47 — Phase 4c-1 implementation notes (the image slice)
Settled while building the headshot pipeline (OFC-69); each refines, not revises, N42/N43.
- **Two new injected seams, mirroring `ProfileStore`/`AuditLog`.** (1) An **`ImageStore`** (`apps/api/src/data/images.ts`: `put`/`delete`/`read`) with a real `GcsImageStore` and an in-memory fake, so the whole pipeline and the `/img/*` read run against doubles in unit tests (there is no local GCS). (2) An **unconditional** write method on `ProfileStore` — `updateUnconditional(id,{set,remove})` — for the headshot pointer advance: it carries **no `If-Match`** (N42) but still requires the doc to exist (a deleted record → `MissingProfileError` → 404), and returns the fresh token the cache advances on in lock-step (D83). The opaque `headshotVersion` is minted by an injected `mintVersion` (default `crypto.randomUUID`) so tests are deterministic and the token is never a guessable counter (R16).
- **Write ordering is direction-dependent (both honour D98's "pointer never names a missing object").** `PUT` writes the two objects **first**, then advances the pointer, then best-effort-purges the superseded version (D94); `DELETE` flips `hasHeadshot` off **first**, then purges — so at no instant does a live pointer reference a deleted object. Purges are best-effort (a failed delete leaves a versioning/lifecycle-recoverable orphan, never a failed request). A `DELETE` with no current headshot is a no-op: no write, no audit, current token returned.
- **Two new audit actions** — `headshot.update` / `headshot.remove` — each logged names-not-values as the field `headshot` (D61). No verification coupling (N42): a photo-only Save produces a no-op text PATCH and never re-verifies or raises the courtesy-unverify dialog.
- **Client crop = `react-easy-crop` v6 in a `@radix-ui/react-dialog`, lazily loaded** (`React.lazy`) so both land in an async chunk off the Directory/landing critical path (D74; the crop dialog + its CSS are ~9 KB brotli, downloaded only when a brother opens the editor). The crop is keyboard-operable (react-easy-crop pans on arrow keys) with a native range slider for zoom, so the drag has a non-drag alternative (WCAG 2.5.7 / D47). The staged blob is a canvas-downscaled ≤1024² JPEG (EXIF stripped); the server re-encode is the authority (D107).
- **Infra consequence:** the *runtime* service account now needs `storage.objectAdmin` on the image bucket (it creates and deletes objects, not just reads), and Cloud Run is bumped to `--memory 1Gi` with an in-process concurrency-1 upload semaphore so a sharp decode spike can't OOM the single cache-holding instance (N42). Object versioning + a 90-day noncurrent-age Delete lifecycle give D94 its recovery window.
- **Code-review remediation (OFC-123–132, applied on the PR before merge):** decode the original **once** into the 512² headshot and derive the 96² thumbnail from *that* buffer — sharp's `clone()` shares a decode only for stream input, so cloning a Buffer + `Promise.all` double-decoded and doubled peak memory (OFC-123, the critical one); rebuild the cache record from the **current** entry after the store write so a concurrent PATCH during the encode is not clobbered in the read model (OFC-125); retain the staged crop on a failed photo-save so retry actually retries (OFC-124); audit the 403 IDOR denial like the PATCH route (OFC-126); clamp the client crop rect to the source bounds so an out-of-bounds selection can't bake black JPEG wedges (OFC-127); reset the `<img>` error flag on URL change (OFC-128); scope the raw-image body parser to an encapsulated plugin so it does not shadow other routes (OFC-131); parallelize the two independent object writes (OFC-132); delete the now-dead `isImageObjectKey`/duplicate regex in favor of `parseImageObjectKey` (OFC-130); and make the in-memory store model a missing doc so the route's undo-purge + 404 branch is unit-tested (OFC-129).

### N48 — Phase 4c-1 live-test follow-ups (two rounds, all shipped)
Findings from Forrest's live testing on staging, fixed in PRs #16/#17 after the pipeline merged:
- **Provisioning drift closed.** The 4c-1 runtime-SA upgrade (`objectViewer`→`objectAdmin`, needed to WRITE headshots) and the D94 bucket versioning/lifecycle lived only in `provision-staging.sh`, which the deploy workflow doesn't run — so they never reached the live bucket and the first upload 500'd on a GCS write-403. Fix: the deploy workflow (`deploy-staging.yml`) now **reconciles the image bucket's IAM + versioning + lifecycle on every deploy** (idempotent; the deployer's `storage.admin` covers it). A prod deploy workflow must carry the same step. General lesson: a change that lives only in a provisioning script never reaches an already-provisioned environment unless the deploy reconciles it.
- **Test data now seeds headshots, not just thumbnails.** `seed-staging-images` (written pre-4c-1) uploaded only 96² thumbnails, so a `hasHeadshot` record showed a real thumbnail in the Directory but 404'd on its Profile page → avatar fallback. `author:thumbnails` now also emits 512² `fixtures/headshots/`, and the seeder uploads **both** keys per record (same tint), so Directory and Profile are consistent.
- **Deceased records are editable by staff.** The 4a treatment hid the Edit button for any deceased record (`canEdit && !deceased`); this blocked staff from managing a deceased brother's photo/fields. The `!deceased` guard is removed — `canEdit` already restricts to staff (a deceased record has no living owner), and staff-editing-deceased is sound (PATCH skips the D28 verification side-effect for deceased; the headshot endpoint permits staff). The dedicated mark-deceased / In-Memoriam-field flow remains **4c-2**.
- **Status marks on the large photo, not just the thumbnail.** The masthead avatar now shows the signed-in brother's **headshot thumbnail** (via `AvatarThumbnail`), updating in place on an own-photo change (`SessionContext.applyOwnHeadshot`, no `/api/me` refetch). The **de-brother ✕** now overlays the Profile/edit headshot too (shared `DebrotheredMark`), mirroring how the deceased mourning band already showed on both sizes.
- **Non-decision confirmed:** the tinted no-photo avatar backgrounds are an intentional per-brother "color family" (`Avatar`/visual-design ASSETS.md), not fake photos.

### N49 — Phase 4c-2 implementation notes (the privileged-action slice)
The five dedicated audited server actions (verify, mark-deceased, de-brother, delete, change-role) and their Profile-page UI, built to API-SPEC §3–§5 and DECISIONS N40/N41/N44. Notes worth carrying forward:
- **Two separate system-internal consent snapshots (D80), not one.** `Profile` gains `deceasedConsentSnapshot` and `debrotherConsentSnapshot` (new shared `ConsentSnapshot` type: both consent flags + the verification stamp). Mark-deceased and de-brother are **orthogonal** (both may be set), so a single shared slot would let the second action capture the first's already-forced-off flags and restore stale values — the exact silent consent-loss D80 exists to prevent. Both fields are visibility-class **`system-internal`** (like `ghostMemberId`) and `WRITE_RULE` **`protected`**, so the exhaustive projection/capability tables strip them from every client payload and forbid them on PATCH automatically; `SelfProfile`'s type-level omit was widened to match the runtime strip. (Forrest chose the two-field design at planning.)
- **Deceased forces consent off; de-brother does not.** Per API-SPEC §3, the *first* raise of deceased forces both email flags off + snapshots + stamps `newsletterConsentChangedAt`; a re-`PUT` on an already-deceased record only edits the five facts (no re-snapshot, no re-force — else the snapshot would capture the forced-off state). De-brother snapshots but leaves the Book consent flags as they were: the Ghost member deletion (Ghost-first) is what stops the mail, and the reconcile treats a de-brothered profile as expected-to-have-no-Ghost-member (D99). Both restore their snapshot on reversal.
- **`PUT …/deceased` is replace semantics.** The body's five D122 fields replace the deceased block (an omitted field clears), which is how staff correct a typo'd obituary link (a re-`PUT` with the corrected fields) — PATCH still rejects `deceased` entirely (N40).
- **Verify is frozen — a no-op — on a deceased record.** API-SPEC lists only a 404 error for verify, but D48 freezes verification while deceased. Realized without a new error: verify on a deceased record writes nothing and returns the current verification + current `ETag` (still 200), and the UI hides the Verify affordance for deceased records. The `>2-year` staleness nudge and the owner-vs-staff copy split live in the client.
- **The privileged writes are unconditional + fresh-`ETag`, like the headshot (N42).** verify/deceased/de-brother carry no `If-Match`; each advances the profile document and returns a fresh `ETag` the container applies in place, so a subsequent PATCH from the warm container doesn't spuriously 412. They share one audited role-tier guard (`authorizePrivileged`: owner-or-staff / staff / admin at the **effective** role, N31 — a "View as" step-down loses the power) and a `commitStatusWrite` helper (unconditional write → `cache.applyUpdate` onto the *current* cached record, OFC-125).
- **`GhostLifecycle` seam (N41).** `deleteMember`/`createMember` injected through `BuildServerOptions` exactly like `IdentityProvider`; the 4c-2 default is `StubGhostLifecycle` (succeed-and-log), which is the intended behavior until the Phase-5 Ghost write path. Delete and de-brother call it **Ghost-first**; a thrown error → `502 ghost_delete_failed`/`ghost_create_failed` with Firestore/GCS/cache untouched (proven by a failing-fake unit test). Phase 5 swaps in the real client without touching the endpoints.
- **Delete: reference-scrub then idempotent deletes.** New `ProfileStore.delete` (idempotent), `ProfileCache.applyDelete(id, scrubbed)` (removes the record + folds in reference-scrubbed referrers with their fresh tokens in one atomic swap), and `cache.referrersOf(id)`. The route clears `bigBrotherId` on every referrer (each `updateUnconditional`, token captured for the cache), pulls `id` from every `users.stars`, purges the current-version image objects (best-effort), then deletes the `users` and `profiles` docs — all idempotent so a re-run completes a partial delete (D98). On success the SPA navigates to the Directory (which re-downloads).
- **Change-role: new grouped `AdminUserStore` seam.** `setRole` (create-if-absent, returns the prior role — `brother` for a created doc, N44), `deleteUser`, `removeStarFromAll`, injected as one required `adminUsers` option (`FirestoreAdminUserStore` real, `InMemoryAdminUserStore` fake). The **last-admin invariant** runs inside `setRole`'s Firestore **transaction** (a `users where role==admin` count consistent with the write) → `409 last_admin`. Audited with dedicated `fromRole`/`toRole` audit fields (D106). *(A brother's current role lives in the private `users` collection, not the `profiles` projection — the build initially rendered the role control as a role-agnostic "set to" selector because of that. **Superseded by N50:** the visual design shows the current role, so 4c-2's first live review added `GET /api/users/{id}/role` to fetch it and rebuilt the control as the specified segmented control.)*
- **Tests:** +25 API unit (`status.test.ts`, `admin.test.ts`), +6 emulator (`FirestoreAdminUserStore` incl. the transactional last-admin invariant against a cleared baseline; `ProfileStore.delete` idempotence), +5 e2e (`profile-4c2.spec.ts`, incl. axe 2.2 AA with the mark-deceased dialog open). Full gate green.
- **Code-review remediation (OFC-133 → OFC-134–138, all fixed before merge):** **OFC-134 (High)** — `DELETE` had no last-admin guard (D106 lockout risk, compounded by the role-hiding UI); added `AdminUserStore.isLastAdmin` and a pre-Ghost `409 last_admin` check (audited `denied`), with the web `deleteProfile`/`DeleteControl` surfacing it and API-SPEC §4 updated. **OFC-135 (Medium)/OFC-138 (Low)** — the delete's reference-scrub folded a **pre-await** referrer snapshot into the cache (a concurrent PATCH to a referrer during the scrub window was silently clobbered) and ran the writes sequentially; the scrub now `Promise.all`s the writes and **re-reads each referrer from the cache after its write** (the `commitStatusWrite`/OFC-125 re-base discipline). **OFC-136 (Low)** — `commitStatusWrite` could regress the cache token if a concurrent write advanced it during the await; added `isTokenNewer` (`<sec>.<nanos>` compare, monotonic per doc) and keep the newer token. **OFC-137 (Low)** — the client `setDeceased`/`setDebrothered` shallow-spread couldn't drop a server-removed key; now replaces the held record from the server's authoritative projection (mirrors the PATCH path). Regression tests added for each of OFC-134/135/136. The reviewer's dropped (false-positive) candidates are recorded on OFC-133: the `tx.get(Query)` "invalid" claim, the missing optional-chaining on the status sub-objects (guaranteed well-shaped by `normalizeHydratedProfile`), the `<output>` announcement, and admin self-demote-while-other-admins-exist.

### N50 — Phase 4c-2 live-test fixes (role control matches the visual design; delete preserves Directory state)
Two issues from Forrest's first live test of 4c-2, both fixed as a follow-up (shallow — no `/code-review`):
- **The Change-role control now matches the visual design.** The build shipped a `<select>` dropdown ("Select a role…") that never reflected the brother's *current* role — a design-fidelity miss, not a considered choice (the build wrongly assumed the role was "not shown" because it isn't in the `profiles` projection). `visual-design/references/Profile.dc.html` specifies a **segmented control** (Brother / Manager / Administrator) with the current role **highlighted**, and the admin identity line even reads "Member · Brother" — so the role *is* meant to be visible to admins. Fix: a new admin-only **`GET /api/users/{id}/role`** (`AdminUserStore.getRole`; API-SPEC §5) supplies the current role, and `RoleControl` is rebuilt as the segmented control (modeled on the masthead `FontSizeToggle` — `<fieldset>` + `aria-pressed` buttons; selecting a segment applies immediately, matching the design's no-separate-Apply treatment; `409 last_admin` keeps the current role and explains). **General lesson: check the delivered visual-design reference for a control before inventing one — a "the data isn't there" instinct can mask a design that assumed the data would be fetched.**
- **Delete now returns to the Directory *entry*, preserving filters/search/sort + scroll.** `removeProfile` did `navigate("/")`, which opened a fresh, unfiltered Directory at the top — losing the user's place. Fixed to the same discipline as "← Directory" (`backToDirectory`): `navigate(-1)` when the profile was reached from a Directory row (`location.state.fromDirectory`), so it POPs to the true Directory entry (its URL query state + `location.key` scroll restoration intact); the Directory refetches on remount, so the just-deleted brother is gone. Cold deep-link with no entry to pop falls back to the Directory home.

*Later updated by: D128 — `role` moved onto the `Profile` (read-public since OFC-199), so the Role control reads the current role straight off the record it already holds; the `GET /api/users/{id}/role` endpoint this entry added is removed and the write re-paths to `PUT /api/profiles/{id}/role`.*

### N51 — Phase 4c-2 live-test fixes round 2 (the filter panel always returns collapsed)
From Forrest's continued live testing: after Directory → profile → Back, the filter panel's expanded/collapsed state was **inconsistent** — it derived `open` from the active-filter count (`useState(activeCount > 0)`), and since the Directory **remounts** on the Back-navigation (the panel unmounts on profile-nav, remounts on Back — confirmed by instrumentation), the returned panel was expanded-iff-filters-active regardless of its state before clicking through. **Forrest's call: don't persist yet another display-state item — just always return the panel collapsed.** Fix: initialize `open` to `false` on every mount (`FilterPanel.tsx`); the header's "N active" badge still signals that filters are applied while the panel is closed, so nothing is hidden. Also affects a fresh visit (always collapsed) — consistent and intended. **Test lesson (cost a while to diagnose): a regression e2e that clicked a row link and *immediately* `page.goBack()` flaked/failed because Back interrupted the in-flight route transition before the Directory unmounted (a test-only race, not real usage) — the reliable pattern is to wait for the profile to actually render (`Directory heading toBeHidden`) before going Back. Compounded by the stale-preview-build trap (`reuseExistingServer`): rebuild + fresh preview per iteration.**

## Phase 4d implementation notes (2026-07-04, prev/next through the directory set)

### N52 — 4d prev/next: the stash is the *displayed* set (search included); the nav model is a pure derivation; the bar renders on display + not-found
Built to the pre-settled N45 mechanism (OFC-67), with these implementation calls:
- **The stashed set is the currently *displayed* rows — search ∩ filter ∩ sort — not just filter+sort** (Forrest's clarification this session). This falls out for free: the three entry points already receive the Directory's final `rows` array (which `Directory.tsx` computes as "search ∩ filters ∩ starred-only ∩ deceased default, then sorted"), so each entry point stashes `rows.map(r => r.id)` via one shared `entryNavState(ids)` call per grid/cards render at the three sites: whole-row click ([DirectoryGrid.tsx](../../apps/web/src/pages/directory/DirectoryGrid.tsx) `onRowClick`), the Canonical Name link (the grid name `Cell`), and the card link ([DirectoryCards.tsx](../../apps/web/src/pages/directory/DirectoryCards.tsx)). *(The id-list's storage was reworked by OFC-141 below — it now lives once in a `sessionStorage` store and `location.state` carries only a `stashId` handle.)*
- **The prev/next model is a pure, unit-tested derivation** off `location.state` + the current id (`apps/web/src/pages/profile/directory-nav.ts` `deriveDirectoryNav`), returning `{hasStash, ids, delta, index, total, prevId, nextId}`. It is keyed only on the resolved id-list and the current id — **never the loaded record** — which is exactly why it stays correct on the **not-found** path: a stale stashed id (deleted / de-brothered / unlisted / newly deceased — 4c made these real) is still a *member* of the id-list, so `index >= 0`, `hasStash` holds, and the user can step past it (no auto-skip). `delta` falls back to 1 for a legacy `fromDirectory` entry without the counter and to 0 for a cold deep-link (→ "← Directory" goes to `/`).
- **`directoryDelta` replaces the 4a-3 `navigate(-1)`-on-`fromDirectory`.** Both "← Directory" (`backToDirectory`) and the post-delete return (`removeProfile`) now `navigate(-directoryNav.delta)` — popping the *whole* Prev/Next chain to the true Directory entry, so its `location.key`-keyed scroll restoration and URL filters (D31/N33) keep working after any chain length. Each Prev/Next is an ordinary push (`stepNavState` = same ids, `delta + 1`); the container's fetch effect keys on `id`, so the neighbour loads normally. `exitEdit` is untouched (edit keeps the N33 one-entry `fromProfile` model; prev/next never render in edit).
- **One shared `DirectoryNav` bar** (`apps/web/src/pages/profile/DirectoryNav.tsx`) carries ← Directory + Prev/Next + a "12 of 431" readout. It replaces `ProfileView`'s old standalone ← Directory button *and* is rendered above the container's not-found state, so there is a single control on both the display and stale-id screens (the not-found copy points the user at Prev/Next). Prev/Next + readout show only when `hasStash`; ← Directory always shows. Accessibility: Prev/Next carry the accessible names "Previous brother" / "Next brother" (the lighter label — Forrest declined resolving the neighbour's canonical name, which would have cost a `resolveCanonicalNames` pass over the roster on every profile open), disable (leaving tab order) at the ends, and use ≥ 24 px targets (WCAG 2.5.8); the readout is a plain `<span>`, not a live region (a full page navigation is announced by the profile heading).
- Tests: `directory-nav.test.ts` unit cases (neighbours, ends, stale-still-a-member, cold deep-link, delta pass-through/fallback, `stepNavState`) + `directory-stash.test.ts` (put/get round-trip, missing→[], bounded eviction, `entryNavState`) + `e2e/profile-prevnext-4d.spec.ts` (the step walk with end-disabling, the ← Directory chain-pop, the stale-id not-found-with-prev/next, the cold-deep-link hide, and axe 2.2 AA on the display-with-bar).

**Code-review remediation (OFC-140 → OFC-141–145, applied on PR #24 before merge; the max-effort review found no surviving correctness bug — the `directoryDelta`/`navigate(-delta)` model was verified mathematically sound — only quality/robustness/one test gap).**
- **OFC-141 (the substantive one, Forrest chose to fix now): the id-list no longer lives in `location.state`.** The first cut stashed the whole ~1,166-id array in `location.state`, which the browser structure-clones into `history.state` on **every** Prev/Next push — so a long walk held N copies. New `apps/web/src/pages/profile/directory-stash.ts` stores the array **once** in `sessionStorage` (survives a same-tab reload, matching the old persistence) under a `crypto.randomUUID()` `stashId`, with a bounded index (`MAX_STASHES = 24`, persisted so the cap holds across reloads) evicting the oldest; all access is `try/catch`-guarded so an unavailable/full store degrades to hidden prev/next (the cold-deep-link path), never a throw. `location.state` now carries only `{ fromDirectory, stashId, directoryDelta }` (a few bytes/entry). `deriveDirectoryNav` stays **pure** — it takes the already-resolved `ids` (the container reads them from the store in a `useMemo`) rather than reading storage itself. Consequence accepted: walking Back across two *different* Directory searches can drop prev/next on the older one once its stash is evicted (graceful — controls hide, ← Directory still works); the per-entry-copy design never did, but that robustness isn't worth N copies in history. The O(n) `indexOf` for the position is deliberately kept (negligible for the roster). **Live-test follow-up (Forrest saw sessionStorage keys churn as he searched):** the first cut wrote a stash inside the grid/cards `useMemo`, so *every* search/filter/sort re-render wrote a new entry even when no profile was ever opened — the 24-slot ring churned through never-used sets. Fixed by writing **lazily**: the entry points precompute a `stashId` at render (`newStashId`, pure) and only call `putDirectoryStash(stashId, ids)` on the click that actually leaves for a profile (the whole-row `onRowClick` and a modifier-guarded `onClick` on the name/card `<Link>`s — a modified/new-tab click writes nothing, since `location.state` doesn't cross tabs); a Prev/Next step reuses the same `stashId` (no re-write). So searching/filtering/sorting now writes **zero** keys, an entry appears only on a real navigation, re-clicking the same view reuses one key (`putDirectoryStash` dedupes the index), and the cap dropped 24→**12**. **Second follow-up (Forrest: identical stashes still accrued — Directory→A→Directory→A→… left one abandoned stash per visit, since each Directory remount mints a fresh `stashId`): the store now self-empties.** `clearDirectoryStashes()` (removes all `pbe:dirnav:*` keys + the index) runs in a `useLayoutEffect` on the Directory's mount — the Directory route remounts on *every* return (← Directory, browser Back, masthead logo, post-delete), so this catches them all; a *layout* effect makes the clear synchronous before paint/first-click so a fast click-through can't be written then wiped. Rationale (Forrest's): once you're on the Directory a prev/next stash is dead weight and the next click regenerates it; reaching a profile any other way (little-brother link, typed URL) carries no handle and shows no prev/next anyway. Steady state is now **≤1** stash (the current chain), 0 while on the Directory; the sole forgone nicety is Forward-restoring prev/next onto a Back'd-out profile. Regression e2e asserts search churn adds no keys, a nav+chain adds exactly one, and repeated Directory→profile→Directory→profile stays at one (not three).
- **OFC-142 (test gap on a destructive path): added an e2e** — an admin walks a Prev/Next chain (delta 3) then Deletes; asserts the app lands on the **Directory**, not one step into the chain. (The pre-existing 4c-2 delete test already covered the cold-deep-link delta-0 case.)
- **OFC-143 (DRY): extracted `popToDirectory`** in the container — `backToDirectory` and the post-delete return were byte-identical delta-pop blocks; both now call the one helper.
- **OFC-144 (a11y): keyboard focus survives each step.** A step remounts the whole bar (the container's loading→ready cycle), dropping focus to `<body>` and breaking Enter-repeat stepping. The container records the step direction in a ref (survives the remount; the container itself does not unmount) and the freshly-mounted `DirectoryNav` re-focuses the pressed control (or the opposite one when it's disabled at an end). The focus effect is **mount-only by design** (not keyed on the intent) — keying it on the intent made it fire on the transient pre-loading re-render and consume the one-shot signal too early, leaving the real remount with nothing to focus. New e2e asserts focus lands on the Next button after a step and falls back to Prev at the end.
- **OFC-145 (resilience/semantics): the not-found / cold-deep-link escape is a real anchor again.** When there is nothing to pop (`delta === 0`) the ← Directory affordance renders as a React Router `<Link to="/">` (a genuine `<a href="/">` that works even if the router misfires and reads as a link to AT) instead of a JS-only button; when `delta > 0` it stays a button (an `href` can't POP the history chain). Two cold-deep-link e2e locators updated (button→link).
- Final gate green: **451 unit + 30 emulator + 97 e2e**, bundle **209.6 KB** brotli (< 250).

## Cross-cutting trust-boundary security pass (2026-07-04, Phase 4 → Phase 5 interstitial)

The deferred cross-cutting trust-boundary review — scheduled after Phase 4 and before Phase 5 — was performed on main (`ae2fe67`), covering the session lifecycle, the projection point, `/img` gating, the export audit, the Firestore rules, and the full route/identity/relay/deploy surface. **Verdict: no critical or high-severity vulnerabilities** — every load-bearing invariant held (the exhaustive projection table + write-allowlist dual, the audited IDOR guards, step-down impersonation at the effective role, the anchored `/img` key parse, the alg-pinned JWT verify, the transactional single-use nonce, the deny-all Firestore rules, the SameSite=Strict host-only `__session` cookie with no CORS, magic-byte/40 MP-bounded image ingest, names-not-values auditing, the dev provider compiled out of prod, and a secret-free public tree). It surfaced two medium and two low findings, all remediated in one PR before Phase 5 (parent ticket **OFC-146**; children **OFC-147–150**). Decisions **N53–N55**.

### N53 — Session revocation follows trust withdrawal: active revocation at the mutation point, plus a de-brothered-actor gate backstop (amends D22; OFC-147)
Book's session snapshots the caller's real `role` and the gate (`requireSession`) checked only existence + expiry, so for up to the 4-hour cap (D22) a de-brothered, deleted, or **demoted** brother kept their old powers — most sharply, a demoted admin could `PUT /api/users/{self}/role` and **re-promote themselves** before the cap. D22 accepted that window when the session was conceptually in-memory; D125 having moved sessions to Firestore makes targeted revocation cheap, so it is now done in two layers. **(1) Active revocation** — `SessionService.destroyAllForProfile(profileId)` queries `sessions` on the nested `session.identity.profileId` (Firestore auto-single-field-indexed, no composite index), batch-deletes, and prunes the in-memory read-through cache in lock-step (the single instance — D83 — owns both). It is called after the Book write commits in **de-brother raise** (`PUT …/debrothered`), **admin delete** (`DELETE /api/profiles/{id}`), and **role change** (`PUT /api/users/{id}/role`, only when the role actually changes). The revoked count is recorded on the existing audit entry as `sessionsRevoked` (a count, within the §1.4 names-not-values boundary). Reinstating (de-brother reverse) and a no-op role reassignment revoke nothing; mark-deceased deliberately does not revoke (revocation tracks *withdrawn trust*, not death). An admin self-demote (legal while other admins remain) tears down the actor's own session; the response still completes and the next action re-auths silently. **(2) Gate liveness backstop** — the gate additionally rejects **and destroys** a session whose own record is *present-and-de-brothered*, a free `Map` lookup that makes the de-brother revocation structural even if some future path forgets to revoke. It keys on the **positive** de-brothered signal, **not on record absence**: an absent record is ambiguous (a hard delete, a not-yet-hydrated initiate, or a record the cache skipped as malformed — OFC-91), so 401'ing on absence would risk locking out a live brother over a data-quality blip; the hard-delete case is covered by the delete route's active revocation instead. Role *demotion* is not gate-checked (the role lives in `users`, not the profile cache; re-reading it per request would defeat D7/D83) — the role-change revocation handles it. Records to `ENGINEERING-DESIGN §2.3`, `API-SPEC §3`/`§4`/`§5`/`§6.1`; amends D22; cites D83/D115/D125/OFC-91. **Live-confirmed on staging (2026-07-04):** an admin self-delete revoked the actor's live session immediately — the next directory read `401`'d rather than waiting for the 4-hour cap — and re-auth was correctly denied `unlinked_member` (the profile no longer resolves). (Minor UX follow-up noted: the bulk-read `401` surfaces the generic "couldn't load the directory" state rather than D109's graceful "session ended — sign in" re-auth, which was scoped to the edit path.)

### N54 — The D107 security headers are implemented, split SPA/API, with a CI guard pinning the CSP's inline-script hashes (OFC-148)
D107 ratified a strict CSP + `nosniff` + a framing policy + `Referrer-Policy` but no phase had implemented them (Phase 7's hardening list omitted them — the item had fallen between phases). Now: **the SPA** (Firebase Hosting, `firebase.json`) sends `Content-Security-Policy` (`default-src 'self'`; `script-src 'self'` + a **SHA-256 hash of each of the two in-`<head>` no-FOUC setters** — theme + font-size, D30/§5.3 — so **no `'unsafe-inline'` for scripts**; `style-src 'self' 'unsafe-inline'`, mandatory for React inline styles + TanStack Virtual's per-row transforms + the theme/font-scale CSS vars; `img-src 'self' data: blob:` for `/img` + the Avatar gradient + the crop preview; `connect-src 'self'`; `worker-src 'self' blob:` for the Name-Search worker; `frame-ancestors 'none'` — which D109's child-*window* re-auth relies on; `object-src 'none'`, `base-uri 'self'`, `form-action 'self'`), plus `X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff`, `X-Frame-Options: DENY`, `Referrer-Policy: strict-origin-when-cross-origin`, and `Strict-Transport-Security` (explicit, so `book.pbe400.org` gets HSTS at cutover; on the `web.app` staging host Firebase injects its own HSTS that overrides this value — verify the explicit one applies at the custom-domain cutover). **The API + `/img`** responses also get the same four non-CSP headers via a Fastify `onSend` hook — but note (corrected against the live deploy) that **Firebase Hosting applies its `**` header rules to the `/api/**` and `/img/**` rewrite paths too and takes precedence**, so in production those responses actually carry the SPA policy; the `onSend` hook is therefore **defense-in-depth** for direct-to-Cloud-Run access that bypasses Hosting (and a CSP on a JSON/image response is inert either way — it governs document contexts, not the bytes). The CSP was validated by loading the real built SPA under the enforcing policy headless — **zero violations**, React mounts — so the initial-paint surface is proven; the authenticated worker/crop surfaces are covered by the code-justified `blob:`/`worker-src` directives and remain a staging-clickthrough confirmation. **The hash brittleness is fenced by CI**: `scripts/assert-csp-hashes.mjs` (wired as `assert:csp-hashes`, run **after `npm run build`**) recomputes the inline-script hashes from the **shipped** `apps/web/dist/index.html` (falling back to the source `apps/web/index.html` only when there is no build yet — a local pre-build run) and fails the build if `firebase.json` omits any, converting a silent production CSP break into a loud red build. Validating the *built* file rather than source is deliberate (OFC-146 review): it is the artifact Firebase serves and the browser enforces against, so a build-time transform of the inline scripts cannot pass a source-only check. **Phase-7 follow-up:** when Mixpanel lands (D62), add its script/connect origins to the SPA `script-src`/`connect-src`. Records to `ENGINEERING-DESIGN §6.4`; closes the D107/P9 implementation gap; cites D62/D109/D126.

### N55 — Generic 500 body (no internal-error leakage) + ungated sign-out (OFC-149/OFC-150)
Two low-severity shape fixes. **(N55a, OFC-149)** Fastify's default error handler echoed a thrown error's raw `message` into the 500 body — a Firestore/GCS/`firebase-admin` failure could leak project ids, database paths, and internal state to the client. `buildServer` now registers a `setErrorHandler` that, for **5xx**, logs the real error (+ stack + trace id) to stderr and returns a generic `{ error: "internal", message: "Something went wrong." }`; **4xx** keep their standard Fastify `{ statusCode, error, message }` shape (validation / unsupported-type / rate-limit messages are caller-controlled and safe). **(N55b, OFC-150)** `POST /api/auth/signout` was behind the session gate, so a session already past the 4-hour cap would 401 *before* the cookie could be cleared, leaving a dead cookie in the browser. Sign-out is now **ungated** (but still rate-limited): destroy the session if the cookie still resolves, clear the cookie unconditionally, `204` either way. Records to `ENGINEERING-DESIGN §6.1`, `API-SPEC §2`.

### N56 — Residual risks reviewed and accepted (documented, not fixed)
Recorded so the threat model is honest: **(1) Ghost's members JWT is signed with a 1024-bit RSA key** (the reason the verify path uses Node `crypto`, not jose — `ghost-jwks.ts`); a factored key forges sign-in as any member. It is core Ghost behavior (Ghost Pro's key is 1024-bit too), bounded by the nonce, short token `exp`, the 4-hour cap, and fail-closed email resolution — and it belongs beside D105's existing "hardening `pbe400.org` is a threat-model dependency." **(2)** The `state` nonce binds the callback to a Book-initiated flow, not to a specific browser — an attacker holding a stolen *live* Ghost token can mint their own nonce; already the documented D104/§12 residual (token theft requires compromising `pbe400.org`). **(3)** `trustProxy` trusts `X-Forwarded-For`, so the IP-keyed auth rate limit is spoofable — acknowledged in `security/rate-limit.ts`; the session-keyed limits are the load-bearing control. **(4)** `/img` responses cache to browser disk for a year (`private, immutable`) — a deliberate R16/D126 trade against D95's no-PII-on-disk posture (photos only, versioned URLs). Cites D95/D104/D105/D126/R16.

## Phase 5a-1 implementation notes (2026-07-05, the Admin page: scaffolding, banner, backup)

Phase 5's original two sessions grew to three (CODING-PROJECT-PLAN §Phase 5): **5a-1** (this session) ships the admin-only `/admin` route + page scaffolding (D31) plus the two surfaces that carry no Ghost dependency — the **system-message banner** end-to-end and the **Download-backup** JSON export. The **Sync-with-Ghost** and **Bug-reports** cards render as calm not-yet-available placeholders, because their backends depend on the Ghost write path (5b) and the bug-report loop (5a-2). Both live surfaces are proven by unit + emulator + e2e (incl. axe 2.2 AA); light/dark render-probes confirmed the layout before the PR.

### N57 — The system banner: a `config/systemBanner` singleton seam, a public read + admin write, and a shared client context feeding the shell slot (D117)
The banner persists as the DATABASE-SCHEMA §6.3 `SystemBanner` singleton at `config/systemBanner`, behind an injected **`BannerStore`** seam (`FirestoreBannerStore` real + `InMemoryBannerStore` fake — the same store-injection pattern as `ProfileStore`/`AdminUserStore`, wired required into `buildServer`). `set()` is a full replace (not a merge) so a **clear** overwrites the prior message rather than leaving it under `active:false`. **`GET /api/banner`** is any-authenticated-user (behind the gate) and returns `{active:false}` whenever the banner is unset **or** cleared — the message/severity are only ever sent when active, so an inactive banner never leaks its last text; served `Cache-Control: no-cache` (short-lived/revalidated per API-SPEC §10, so an admin's change shows promptly). **`PUT /api/admin/banner`** is admin-only at the **effective** role (N31) via a new shared **`requireEffectiveAdmin`** guard in `privileged-support.ts` (the id-less counterpart to `authorizePrivileged`, for whole-database admin ops with no `:id` subject); it validates `active` is boolean, a set's message is non-empty-trimmed and ≤500 chars, and `severity ∈ {info,warning}` (defaulting `info`), stamps `updatedBy`/`updatedAt`, and writes one **`banner.set`** audit entry carrying a coarse `scope: "set" | "clear"` — never the message text (D61 names-not-values, reusing the existing `scope` field). **Client:** a small **`BannerProvider`/`useBanner`** context (in `GateLayout`, wrapping `AppShell`) fetches `/api/banner` once and feeds the **existing Phase-1b `SystemBanner` slot** (the shell's hardcoded `null` is replaced); the Admin banner card's set/clear call `refresh()` so the masthead updates **without a reload**, and a failed banner fetch swallows to `null` (non-essential chrome must never block the directory). The banner card reuses `SystemBanner` for a faithful live **preview**. Records to `ENGINEERING-DESIGN §6.1`; cites D82/D95/D107/N31; realizes API-SPEC §10 + DATABASE-SCHEMA §6.3.

### N58 — The Download-backup JSON export: an injected `BackupSource`, admin-only, download-attachment framed; the images-zip + nightly job stay in Phase 7 (D63)
`GET /api/admin/backup` is admin-only at the effective role (same `requireEffectiveAdmin` guard) and returns a versioned envelope `{version:1, generatedAt, collections:{profiles,users,config}}` served as a dated download **attachment** (`Content-Disposition: attachment; filename="book-backup-YYYY-MM-DD.json"`, `no-store`), audited as **`backup.download`** with no `targetId` (a whole-database action). The read goes through an injected **`BackupSource`** seam (`FirestoreBackupSource` real + `InMemoryBackupSource` fake) reading the authoritative on-disk Firestore state — each doc captured as `{id, data}` so a future restore is a faithful, key-preserving replay (the `config` singleton's id is not a data field). **Scope for 5a-1 is JSON-only:** the D63 image-object bundle (a zip of the private-bucket headshots/thumbnails) and the nightly automated backup job both fold into **Phase 7**, where the automated-backup + image-version-manifest work lives. `majors` (a bundled vocabulary, N29 — not yet a live collection) and `bugReports` (5a-2) are not in the export until they become live data. **Client:** `downloadBackup()` fetches credentialed → blob → a transient object-URL anchor click, so a `403`/`5xx` surfaces as an `ApiError` the card reports rather than a broken navigation. The reference's fictional "last backup … nightly" line was replaced with honest copy (the nightly job isn't built yet). Records to `ENGINEERING-DESIGN §6.3`; realizes API-SPEC §7; cites D63/D100/D101/N29.

### Phase 5a-1 code-review remediation (2026-07-05; PR #30, parent OFC-182 → OFC-183–190)
The high-effort review found **one genuine behavioral bug** and a set of cleanups; all handled on the PR branch before merge. **OFC-183 (the bug)** — a transient `GET /api/banner` failure was swallowed to `banner = null`, which drove the admin control's Clear-enable and "currently live" indicator, so a blip could hide a *live* banner and disable clearing it. Fixed by giving `BannerContext` a `status: loading|ready|error` (the masthead still treats the banner as non-essential chrome and renders nothing on error, but the **admin card** distinguishes "read failed" from "no banner"): the card shows a retryable error, keeps **Clear enabled** when the read failed (the server `PUT {active:false}` is idempotent), and no longer nulls the last-known banner on a failed refresh. **OFC-185** migrated `registerRoleRead` onto the shared `requireEffectiveAdmin` (a third copy of the session→admin check removed). **OFC-186** hoisted the `info|warning` vocabulary to `@pbe/shared` `BANNER_SEVERITIES`/`BannerSeverity` (server validation set, client toggle, and all unions derive from the one tuple). **OFC-187** dropped `BannerCard`'s copy-context-into-state (`touched` latch + seed `useEffect`) for a `key`-on-banner-identity **remount** of an extracted `BannerForm` (write state lifted to the parent so it survives the remount), converging to server truth; also muted the live preview until there's real message text (choosing "Warning" first no longer flashes a red bar). **OFC-189** narrowed the `PUT /api/admin/banner` response to the public `{active,message,severity}` shape so `updatedBy`/`updatedAt` never reach the client (symmetric with the GET). **OFC-184** extracted `saveBlob(blob, filename)` to `apps/web/src/lib/utils.ts`, shared by `downloadBackup` + the Directory `downloadCsv` (the two had already drifted on the `revoke` try/finally). **Two judgment calls:** **OFC-190** (audit the id-less admin 403s) — **fixed, not closed WAI**: the banner-set and backup-download surfaces are whole-database (site-wide message; every brother's PII), so a stepped-down-admin/non-admin probe is worth the forensic trail; `requireEffectiveAdmin` gained an optional denial-audit context, passed by banner+backup (recording `outcome:"denied"`, no target) but **not** by the role *read* (reads stay non-audited, unchanged). **OFC-188** (backup materializes every collection in one reply) — **accepted for MVP, code unchanged, documented** in `ENGINEERING-DESIGN §6.3` as Phase-7 streaming/cache-reuse work (raw-Firestore read kept for restore fidelity vs. the normalized cache). Refuted during review (not filed): the `downloadBackup` immediate-`revokeObjectURL` "cancels the download" candidate (the identical working `downloadCsv` pattern proves a same-tick revoke after `click()` is safe).

### Phase 5a-1 live-review UI decisions (2026-07-05; PRs #31/#32, Forrest's calls)
Forrest's staging live-test drove a set of Admin-page UI decisions, all merged + deployed. **Naming:** the avatar-menu item is **"Admin Tools"** and the page heading its formal long form **"Administrative Tools"**. **Copy:** the backup card reads "…snapshot of the **PBE Address Book**…" (not "the directory"). **System banner (D117):** the message is **16px semibold** (up from 14px) for visibility; **warning** keeps the destructive **red** as a clean block (no rules); **info** takes the brand **amber** (`--gold-bg-2` + `--gold-text-strong`) bounded by **symmetric** hairline gold rules top+bottom (`border-y --gold-border-2`) — and the masthead `<header>` **drops its own `border-b` whenever a banner shows** so the banner's rules are the only lines at that seam. (Note: the original visual design used amber for *warning*; Forrest deliberately reassigned amber→info, red→warning.) **Navigation:** the Admin page's **"← Directory" uses the history stack** like the Profile page's (N45) — the avatar-menu "Admin Tools" link carries `state:{fromDirectory: onDirectory}` and ← Directory renders as a **button that `navigate(-1)`s** when it came from the Directory (popping back with search/sort/filter/scroll preserved), else a real `<Link to="/">` cold-deep-link escape; the masthead logo stays a distinct fresh-`/` home link. **Q&A resolutions (accepted, no code):** the backup download stays **plain JSON** (inspectable at ~1 MB; becomes a `.zip` in Phase 7 when the archive gains an image folder); **restore stays a Phase-7 offline operator procedure**, not an Admin button (D100/D101); **Lucide** is adopted in one sweep at **Phase 6** (the app's icons — incl. the 4 hand-authored Admin-card SVGs — are inline SVGs today; `lucide-react` was never added).

## Phase 5.5 scheduling (2026-07-06, the interim ticket-batch triage)

### N59 — Phase 5.5 created: the accumulated Linear tickets triaged and batched into seven interim sessions (`5.5a`–`5.5g`), to run between Phases 5 and 6
Forrest's standing bug philosophy governs the triage bar: **if a bug will *ever* be worth fixing, fix it now** — a bug left in Backlog is one we are comfortable *never* fixing. A dedicated triage session audited every PBE-Book Backlog bug against the current code and scheduled all Todo tickets. Outcomes: **(1)** Eleven of the thirteen Backlog bugs — OFC-108–118, the Phase-4 retro-review findings deferred at filing time — were verified **already fixed on `main`** (the retro-remediation PRs #11–#14 implemented each ticket's own suggested fix, but the tickets were never closed); all eleven were closed Done with per-ticket file/line evidence comments. **(2)** OFC-181 (the accepted-residuals tracking ticket, D99/D102/D105) deliberately **stays in Backlog** — accepted-as-designed is precisely the never-fix bar. **(3)** OFC-152 (the CodeQL alert triage) was promoted to Todo. **(4)** All 21 Todo tickets were grouped **by code locality** into seven single-session batches, tagged `5.5a`–`5.5g` in Linear (each label's description names its scope); the batches have no cross-dependencies and can run in any order. The plan text lives in CODING-PROJECT-PLAN §Phase 5.5; the tags are the work queue. Two findings from the triage's code verification are load-bearing for the sessions: **OFC-201's root cause** — the "Add Brother" error is not a regression; **`POST /api/profiles` was never built** (the admin UI link to `/brother/new` exists with no backend create slice), so 5.5a is a build, not a fix — and **OFC-197's split nature** — the deploy autoseed wipes only `profiles`; `users` stars survive deliberately via the tester-link MERGE, and column/width settings are client `localStorage` no deploy can clear, so only the server half is fixable. **One open decision blocks 5.5f:** OFC-139 records role visibility as staff-only ("Forrest, confirmed", 2026-07-03) while the newer OFC-199 (2026-07-06) proposes role columns/filters visible to **all** brothers — Forrest rules before 5.5f starts, and the losing ticket plus the eventual role-visibility DECISIONS entry are corrected to match. **Update (2026-07-07):** an **eighth batch `5.5h` — mobile layout polish** was appended after Phase-5a-2 live testing surfaced two phone-layout issues (OFC-210 masthead element cutoff; OFC-211 the Directory's chrome eating >½ the vertical viewport) that fit none of the existing code-locality batches; Forrest's call to make it a dedicated batch. See CODING-PROJECT-PLAN §Phase 5.5.

## Phase 5a-2 implementation notes (2026-07-07, the bug-report loop)

### N60 — Book is a bug *receiver*, not a bug *tracker*: triage-and-clear (view/copy/delete), with no external-tracker integration (Forrest's call, refines D121)
Forrest reframed the bug-review side after reflecting on maintenance cost: doing bug *management* well in Book would be expensive and complicated, so Book does none of it. Book only **receives** in-app reports (the filing path is unchanged — members still need an easy way to report) and gives an admin a minimal surface to **view, copy, and delete** them; the real tracking happens in the team's external tracker (Linear), into which the admin pastes anything worth keeping. The Admin queue exists **only** because Book has no email (D121 keeps the admin's inbox out of the attack surface) and reading raw Firestore by hand would be cumbersome — so we build the smallest possible viewer, in-app. **A Book→Linear "Transfer to Linear" button was explicitly considered and rejected:** it would (a) give Book its *first* long-lived third-party **write secret** (a Linear API key) to guard/rotate in a public-repo-adjacent deployment — a real escalation of a threat model that until now has had zero outbound-service credentials (D104/D105/D121); (b) couple Book's runtime to Linear's API, schema, availability, and partial-failure/idempotency handling — exactly the "expensive and complicated" machinery being avoided; and (c) skip the human reject step, filing spam/dupes/test entries into Linear as issues to be triaged there. The copy/paste friction it would save is small at this app's volume and is minimized by a per-report **"Copy report"** that puts a preformatted block on the clipboard. If copy/paste proves annoying in practice, the transfer is a possible *future* enhancement — deliberately not filed as a ticket (Forrest agreed it would not be a good idea).

### N61 — `status` is a two-value unread marker (`new`/`reviewed`), delete is terminal; three admin endpoints; the DELETE verb for deletion; misc build notes
The schema's `status: 'new' | 'reviewed'` (DATABASE-SCHEMA §6.4) is kept **as an unread-email marker**, not a lifecycle: `new` = an admin has not yet seen it; `reviewed` = it has been displayed but not deleted; **deletion removes the document** (there is no stored terminal/"resolved" state — the visual design's "Resolved"/"Mark resolved" is superseded by copy+delete). Transitions are one-way (`new`→`reviewed`→deleted). Endpoints added to API-SPEC §10 **before building** (per plan): `POST /api/bug-report` (any authenticated user; tightened to **5/min per session** + **2000-char** description cap, D86; captures `page`+absolute `url`+non-PII `clientContext`), `GET /api/admin/bug-reports` (admin-only at the **effective** role; newest-first, unpaginated, `no-store`; a straight projection — **the submitter's canonical name is snapshotted onto the record at filing** from `session.identity.displayName`, so the admin read touches no roster and the name survives the submitter's later deletion, Forrest's call refining an earlier compute-on-read approach), `POST /api/admin/bug-reports/mark-reviewed` (the `new`→`reviewed` flip, fired by the SPA after rendering so badges show on this visit and quiet on the next), and **`DELETE /api/admin/bug-reports/{id}`** — the dedicated HTTP verb chosen over a uniform `POST …/delete` because it *is* a deletion (Forrest agreed). Mechanism mirrors 5a-1: a `BugReportStore` seam (Firestore `bugReports` + in-memory double) wired required into `buildServer` + both entry points + the ~11 test buildServer sites; `requireEffectiveAdmin` with its OFC-190 denial-audit context guards all three admin endpoints; audit action `bug.report` (scopes `file`/`delete`; the routine mark-reviewed flip is **not** audited to avoid per-visit log spam; names-not-values — never the description text). The filing UI is a **native `<dialog>`** modal (via a shared `ModalDialog` shell that `ConfirmDialog` also uses, so the focus-trap/Escape/inert-background wiring lives in one place — WCAG 2.2 AA) in the masthead control cluster. `clientContext.webVersion` is a Vite `define` (`__APP_VERSION__`, the commit SHA; a later follow-up expanded `clientContext` to device/OS/browser/network best-effort diagnostics and added a server-stamped `apiVersion` — see DATABASE-SCHEMA §6.4). **`bugReports` is deliberately excluded from the D63 backup** — it is transient triage data an admin clears (like `sessions`/`authNonces`), not part of the durable directory a restore reconstructs; including it would have forced a `BACKUP_VERSION` bump and a restore-shape mismatch for no real recovery value (a code-review finding; Forrest's triage-and-clear framing settles it). Gate green: **+13 API unit + 4 store emulator + 3 web format unit + 7 e2e** (incl. filing-dialog + queue axe 2.2 AA); bundle ~214 KB brotli.

## Phase 7.5 planning (2026-07-07, the client data-layer unification and conditional roster read)

### N62 — Phase 7.5 created: unify the two client profile caches into one in-memory store, kept fresh by an app-level versioned conditional read
Raised in a caching-architecture discussion (2026-07-07). The current client data layer has two inefficiencies. **(1)** The Directory re-downloads the whole `no-store` per-role payload on **every** remount — it is served `no-store` with **no read `ETag`**, so there is no `304` path; brotli-precompressed (D84), but a full transfer each time even when nothing changed. **(2)** The Profile page holds a **second, separate** roster copy (a module singleton loaded once per tab) for its Big/Little-Brother derivation — so a common Directory→Profile→Directory trip pulls the full payload two-to-three times into two caches that can also **drift** (the Directory re-fetches on remount and shows fresh data while the Profile page's roster-derived edges, held for the tab, stay stale). **Decision (Phase 7.5):** collapse both into a **single module-level in-memory store** subscribed by both pages (extend today's roster singleton into the canonical store; the Directory reads it instead of its own fetch; the existing `applyProfileToRoster` optimistic fold now feeds the one store, retiring the drift). Keep it fresh with an **app-level versioned conditional read**: the store holds an opaque dataset **version token**; a revalidation sends `GET /api/profiles` with `If-None-Match` (or `?v=`), and the server returns **`304`** (empty) on a match or **`200`** + the already-compressed per-role buffer + a new token on a miss. Server-side this is nearly free — the backend already maintains a dataset **version/ETag in the GCS snapshot, regenerated on every write** (D85), and the brother buffer is precomputed (D84) — so a match is a token compare and a miss serves a ready buffer. The read `ETag` is **qualified by effective role** (`{datasetVersion}.{role}`) so a "View as" switch (N31) can't be served a mismatched projection as a `304`, and a role switch naturally forces a fresh pull. **Revalidate** on Directory mount (replacing today's unconditional refetch) and on tab `visibilitychange`/`focus`, which also turns the cross-user staleness window — a second reader never sees another's edit until a full reload — into "converges on the next Directory mount or tab-focus" for the cost of a tiny conditional request, **without** any WebSocket/SSE push (out of scope; over-built for ≈700 brothers on bursty bi-annual traffic). This is the **data-version analogue of D112/N25's build/contract-version advertisement** (which refreshes stale *code*); the two are complementary and may share a `/api/version`-style surface. **Why a phase, not a ticket:** it is a cross-cutting rewrite of the SPA's primary read path plus an API-contract change, with its own PR, `/code-review`, and test additions (store unit tests, an emulator test for the `ETag`/`304` path, an e2e proving a match skips the download and a version bump forces it) — a self-contained unit deserving its own gate, mirroring how Phase 5.5 was inserted (N59). Scheduled **pre-UAT, between Phase 7 (hardening) and Phase 8 (cutover)** so it lands on a verified delivery baseline. **Precondition:** OFC-212 (the delivered-`Cache-Control` verification) is resolved in Phase 7 first, since the true on-the-wire cache posture shapes the implementation. Full forward design in ENGINEERING-DESIGN **§1.7**; plan entry in CODING-PROJECT-PLAN **§Phase 7.5**.

### N63 — The Phase 7.5 conditional read is app-level and heap-only, so it upholds D95 and does not resurrect D76
The load-bearing subtlety, recorded so a future reader does not mistake N62 for a reversal of D95. D95 (superseding D76) removed the read-side conditional GET **because** D76 served `GET /profiles` `private, no-cache` with an `ETag`/`304` and let the **browser HTTP cache** store the revalidatable body — persisting real PII (names + shared emails/phones) to a shared/public machine's disk with no reliable purge-on-close hook (finding P11). Phase 7.5 reintroduces conditional revalidation **without** that residue, because it operates at a different layer: **(1)** the `/api/profiles` response stays **`Cache-Control: no-store`** — the browser HTTP cache is never involved; **(2)** the conditional logic lives in **application code** — the fetch layer sends the version token and inspects `res.status === 304` itself; and **(3)** the dataset is retained **only in the JS heap** (the module singleton), wiped on tab close and actively cleared on sign-out (`clearRoster`, OFC-118) — the same no-disk posture the roster singleton already has. So the design recovers the **bandwidth** win D95 gave up (a returning/navigating browser revalidates cheaply instead of re-pulling the whole payload) while keeping the **on-disk-PII** invariant D95 exists to protect. It is therefore *not* a reversal of D95 and *not* a reinstatement of D76: it is an app-layer conditional read over a heap-only store, orthogonal to browser caching. Two invariants stay explicitly untouched: the **per-role projection** (D82/D5) — a `304` skips re-sending the *same* projection, it does not widen it — and the **write-side** optimistic-concurrency token (§2.6: per-record `updateTime`/`If-Match`), a different `ETag` at a different granularity from the bulk read's dataset version, which must not be conflated with it. The design remains **pull-based, not real-time**: convergence is bounded by revalidation cadence (N62), not by server push.

## UAT policy (2026-07-07)

### N64 — UAT runs on test data on a non-production environment; the platform mechanism is deferred
*Later updated by: D132 (2026-07-14 — the deferred platform fork is resolved as option (a) refined: UAT runs on **staging** in a frozen-autoseed window, and moves out of Phase 8 into its own **Phase 7.7**; the full plan is `UAT-PLAN.md`. The fake-data/non-prod policy itself is unchanged.)*

Forrest's requirement (2026-07-07), clarifying what "UAT" means in the Phase 8 cluster (CODING-PROJECT-PLAN §9): **user-acceptance testing exercises the app against fake/test data on a non-production platform — never production, never real brother data** — so testers can create, edit, and delete freely without any risk to real brothers. This is a firm policy, not just a convenience: UAT is deliberately kept on the test-data, non-prod side of the line that the real-data migration dry-run and the go-live sit on (they cluster near each other in Phase 8 but are distinct activities). **The platform mechanism is deferred** to UAT setup, with two candidates recorded: **(a)** the existing **staging** environment — already fake-data, but it wipe-reseeds profiles/images on every deploy (`STAGING_AUTOSEED`, N18), so a UAT window there needs autoseed disabled and deploys **frozen** so testers' edits survive; or **(b)** a **dedicated, stably-seeded test environment** (a clone of staging's IaC seeded once, no autoseed, torn down after — in the spirit of the D102 ephemeral-environment tooling), which isolates testers from staging's deploy churn at a modest one-time setup cost. Forrest chose to **record the policy now and pick the mechanism when UAT is provisioned in Phase 8** (the app's cost floors to ~$0 either way, so cost is not the deciding factor). Access is role-switchable via the `DevIdentityProvider` (D72) regardless of platform.

## Phase 5b-1 design decisions (2026-07-08, the Book→Ghost write path — pre-implementation)

Settled in the 5b-1 scoping discussion **before** implementation (the reverse of the usual post-build implementation-notes pattern, because the choices reshape D96 rather than concretize it); Forrest's calls throughout. Phase 5's remaining scope splits into **5b-1** (the write path + the Linter roster stub) and **5b-2** (the reconciliation audit + the Sync-with-Ghost card) — see N67. Live testing targets **ghost-staging only**, never production Ghost (D72); Forrest confirmed a Ghost Admin API key is provisioned on ghost-staging.

### N65 — The Ghost update push is Ghost-first-gated: Ghost accepts the change before Book commits; `pendingPriorEmail` is dropped (Forrest's call, amends D96/D97)
*Later updated by: N68 (2026-07-08 — the pushed set drops from four fields to three: `allowCommentReplyEmail` is not settable via the Ghost Admin API and was removed from Book entirely, so it is no longer a pushed field).*

D96 specified the update path as write-Firestore-then-push, with an email change "commit-gated on Ghost" and a transient `pendingPriorEmail` alias tolerating the disagreement window. Re-examined at build time, Forrest reversed the ordering: **every Ghost-synced write now shares one rule — Ghost confirms before Book commits.** A `PATCH` that changes any pushed field (`email`; a Canonical-Name input — `firstName`/`lastName`/`classYear`; `allowNewsletterEmail`) calls the Ghost Admin API first and proceeds to the Firestore write only on success; a clear Ghost failure fails the whole save (`502 ghost_update_failed`, Book untouched) with an honest "couldn't save — try again later." A save touching none of the pushed fields makes **no** Ghost call and is unaffected by a Ghost outage — as are headshots, stars, and every other non-pushed surface. The same gate applies to `PUT …/deceased` (its forced unsubscribes — and, on reversal, the snapshot restore — push diff-based, Ghost-first-gated). A profile with **no `ghostMemberId`** skips the push (there is no member to update; the reconciliation audit reports it as `missingGhostMember`) — which also keeps fake-data staging profiles editable. **Race handling:** the `If-Match` token is preflighted before the Ghost call and same-record writes are serialized in-process (a keyed promise chain — sound at `max-instances=1`), so a concurrent edit cannot commit between the Ghost `PUT` and the Firestore write; residual cross-system races fall to the 5b-2 audit as `fieldDrift`. **Accepted residual:** Ghost-accepted-then-Firestore-failed (requires a Firestore write failure — assumed rare) leaves Ghost briefly ahead of Book; the failure is loud, the editor's session is still live, and an idempotent retry converges (re-`PUT` by id is a no-op) — an abandoned case surfaces in the audit for an admin re-push. **`pendingPriorEmail` is dropped entirely** (the D96 tolerance and D97's index-alias clause): Book never commits an email Ghost has not accepted, so sign-in and Ghost's magic-link delivery can never disagree about the current address — the tolerance has nothing left to tolerate.
**Why:** (1) **Uniformity** — create, delete, and de-brother were already Ghost-first-abort-clean (D96/D98/D115); update was the lone exception, and the exception was where all the compensating machinery lived. One ordering rule ("Ghost confirms before Book commits, everywhere") is far easier to hold correct in the subsystem Forrest judges most likely to cause operational headaches. (2) **Simplicity** — kills `pendingPriorEmail` (the dual-email index alias, the set-on-uncertainty logic, and a clear-on-reconcile mechanism that was never built), eliminates the silent-desync class for the pushed fields, and removes any "saved-but-didn't-reach-Ghost" partial-success UX. (3) **Loud failure + idempotent retry self-heals**, where Firestore-first produced a "successful" save with silent drift and no user incentive to retry. (4) **Rarity math** — Ghost failures are expected to be rare and post-launch edits to email/name/consent are the rarest edits in the system; blocking that doubly-rare intersection with "try again later" costs far less than the machinery to hide it. Records to `ENGINEERING-DESIGN §5.1`, `API-SPEC §3` (PATCH + deceased), `PRD §6.1`.

### N66 — Photos are not in the Ghost pushed set — a platform limitation, not a choice (byline automation backlogged as OFC-213)
Forrest wants a brother's Book headshot to propagate to Ghost so his photo is the same everywhere (Ghost's avatar surfaces, article bylines). Verified against the live Admin API docs plus testing on ghost-staging and prod (2026-07-08): **Ghost members cannot have photos** — the member `avatar_image` is read-only, Gravatar-derived-or-`null`, with no upload path — so a Book→member-avatar push is **impossible on stock Ghost** (and production is Ghost Pro: auto-upgraded, no server customization, so no hack path exists). **Byline photos belong to Ghost *staff users*** — a separate identity type; today a handful of article authors whom Forrest adds as staff manually, uploading their photos in Ghost Admin. Staff `profile_image` *is* settable — but only via endpoints **outside the documented stable Admin API** (the docs' endpoint table grants `/users/` Browse + Read only; "the endpoints listed on this page are those stable enough to document"), i.e. surfaces Ghost may change in any release without notice — a silent-break risk under Ghost Pro's continuous auto-upgrade, plus an auth wrinkle to verify (user-management endpoints have historically required session/staff auth, not integration keys). **Decision:** the member-avatar half is recorded as a platform limitation (revisit only if Ghost ships member profile images); the byline/staff-photo automation is a backlog feature — **Linear OFC-213** holds the findings and the design questions. The manual workflow remains viable indefinitely at a few authors per bi-annual issue.

**A second platform limitation surfaced at 5b-1 build time (2026-07-08): the comment-reply notification preference is not pushable either.** The `enable_comment_notifications` member field — Book's `allowCommentReplyEmail` — is **not settable via the documented Admin API**: the member serializer never returns it, Ghost silently drops it on write (a junk field also returns `201`), and a live cross-check via the member portal confirmed a `PUT` setting it `false` had **no effect** (the toggle stayed on). Unlike the avatar, this preference *does* exist and *is* editable in the member's own portal, so it reads as a Ghost UI/serializer inconsistency, filed for research-and-report as **Linear OFC-216** (PBE-Ghost). Because Book cannot make the setting take effect, `allowCommentReplyEmail` was **removed from Book entirely** rather than shipped as non-functional UI (see N68). The Ghost pushed set is therefore **three fields** (email, name, newsletter subscription), not four; re-adding the control is tracked as **OFC-215** for if/when Ghost supports it.

### N67 — Phase 5b splits into 5b-1 (the write path + the roster stub) and 5b-2 (the reconciliation audit + the Sync card)
The same §8 session-splitting discipline that produced 5a-1/5a-2. **5b-1** — the write path: the real Ghost Admin-API client behind the `GhostLifecycle` seam (config `GHOST_ADMIN_API_URL` + `GHOST_ADMIN_API_KEY`, the key in Secret Manager and never in the public tree; live-tested against ghost-staging only, D72); the seam grows **`updateMember`**, and **`createMember` now returns the fresh `ghostMemberId`**, which the de-brother reversal folds into its write (a re-created member gets a new id — the stale one must not survive); the N65 Ghost-first-gated diff push wired into `PATCH` and `PUT …/deceased`; and the **Linter roster stub** (`GET /api/roster` → `{ contractVersion: 1, roster: [] }` behind the D58/D78 subject-pinned Google-OIDC verification, mirroring the Ghost-JWKS verify pattern). The **new-brother create-Ghost-first wiring waits for `POST /api/profiles`** (never built; Phase 5.5a, OFC-201) — recorded here so it is a visible gap, not a silent one. **Build-time must-verify (resolved 2026-07-08 against ghost-staging):** newsletter subscription is the `newsletters[]` relation (`[{ id }]` to subscribe, `[]` to unsubscribe), **not** the read-only derived `subscribed` boolean — verified end-to-end (create/update/delete); the newsletter id is pinned via `GHOST_NEWSLETTER_ID`. The comment-notification field turned out **not settable via the Admin API** and was removed from Book (N66/N68), so only the newsletter preference is pushed. **5b-2** — the reconciliation audit (the read pass + the D103 newsletter most-recent-change-wins apply-and-log, whose member-activity-timestamp dependency is that session's own must-verify), the Sync-with-Ghost Admin card's real backend, the D120 email-bounce report riding the audit's outputs, and the D118 maintenance/outage mechanism (the remaining unassigned Phase-5 goal item — placement to be confirmed at 5b-2 kickoff).

### N68 — `allowCommentReplyEmail` is removed from Book entirely (it cannot be pushed to Ghost, so a UI control for it would be non-functional; Forrest's call, 2026-07-08)
Book carried `allowCommentReplyEmail` — a per-brother preference ("email me when someone replies to my article comment") — as one of the Ghost-coupled consent flags (added in D55 so Book could fully replace Ghost's redirected email-preferences modal). Phase 5b-1's live verification against ghost-staging (N66) established that **Ghost's Admin API cannot set this preference**: `enable_comment_notifications` is never serialized back, is silently dropped on write, and a portal cross-check confirmed no effect. Since Book is the single master and edits are redirected away from Ghost's own UI (§5.1), a Book control the brother flips would change nothing in Ghost — a non-functional setting. **Forrest's decision: remove the field from Book altogether** rather than present a dead toggle. Removed across the stack — the shared `Profile` type and `ConsentSnapshot`; the `restricted` visibility class (`visibility.ts`); the `consent` write class (`capabilities.ts`); the shared validation list; the CSV export column; the fake-data generator; the profile-edit consent switch (the *Emails from PBE News* group now holds only the newsletter switch); the manager/admin directory **column and filter**; and every delivered doc. The deceased force-off and its D80 snapshot/restore now touch only `allowNewsletterEmail`, and the Ghost pushed set is **three fields** (email, name, newsletter). Consequences: the privacy/consent toggle set drops from **eight to seven** (five share + **two** consent — `allowNewsletterEmail`, `allowShareWithMITAA`), and the visibility taxonomy is unchanged (the field simply leaves the `restricted` class). **Reversibility:** if Ghost ever exposes the preference through a supported Admin-API path, the control is re-added per **OFC-215** (PBE-Book), using the 5b-1 removal commit as the reference; the upstream Ghost bug is tracked for research-and-file as **OFC-216** (PBE-Ghost). Amends D55 (the field it added is retired), D80 (snapshot is newsletter-only), D89/D93/D113 (toggle count 8→7), and N65/N66 (pushed set 4→3). Records to `DATABASE-SCHEMA §3/§8/§9`, `ENGINEERING-DESIGN §5.1`, `API-SPEC §3`, `PRD §4/§5.7.3/§6.1`, `USER-MANUAL`, `CODING-PROJECT-PLAN`, `PRE-LAUNCH-TOOLS`.

## Phase 5b-1 code-review remediation (2026-07-08)

`/code-review` (high-effort) on PR #37 filed nine findings under **OFC-218** (children OFC-219–227); all remediated on the branch. No finding was a signature-bypass / fail-open — the crypto verify path was sound; these are a concurrency correctness set plus robustness/reuse cleanups.

- **OFC-219 (High) — silent newsletter unsubscribe when `GHOST_NEWSLETTER_ID` unset.** With the Admin key set but the newsletter id missing, enabling the newsletter emitted `newsletters: []` (the *unsubscribe* payload) with no error, inverting consent. `GhostAdminLifecycle` now **requires** a non-empty `newsletterId` (constructor throws), and `index.ts` **fails fast at startup** if the Admin key is present without it — a misconfig crashes rather than silently corrupting consent.
- **OFC-220 (High) — `RecordLock` excluded verify/headshot → Ghost-ahead-of-Book divergence.** A concurrent verify/headshot commit could advance the concurrency token *during* a PATCH's awaited Ghost push, 412-ing that PATCH **after** Ghost was mutated (the exact window N65 closes). Fix: a single shared wrapper `runRecordWrite` (`routes/record-write.ts`) now fronts **every** token-advancing write — PATCH, verify, deceased, debrother, and the headshot pointer write — so they all serialize on the record id. (Stars are excluded by design: they write the `users` doc, not the profile, so they never advance the profile token.)
- **OFC-221 (High) — stale consent snapshot from a pre-lock read.** Deceased/de-brother captured the D80 consent snapshot from a read taken *before* the lock; a concurrent PATCH consent change left it stale, so a later reverse re-subscribed a brother who had opted out. Fix: the snapshot (and the pushed diff) are now built **inside** the lock from a fresh `currentOr404` read, reflecting any write that committed before this task acquired the lock.
- **OFC-222 (Med) — dangling `ghostMemberId` after de-brother raise.** The raise deleted the Ghost member but left the id, so a later pushed-field PATCH pushed to a deleted member → hard 502 (record un-editable). Fix: the raise `remove`s `ghostMemberId`; the reverse re-mints it via `createMember`.
- **OFC-223 (Med) — transient JWKS failure surfaced as 401.** A key-resolution/transport blip returned the Linter a permanent-looking 401 instead of a retryable error. Fix: the shared verifier distinguishes `JwtKeyResolutionError` (transient) from `JwtVerifyError` (bad token); the roster route maps the former to **503**.
- **OFC-224 (Low) — case-sensitive bearer scheme.** `bearerToken` now matches `Bearer` case-insensitively per RFC 6750/7235.
- **OFC-225 (Low) — duplicated JWT-verify skeleton.** The Ghost and roster verifiers shared a copy-pasted alg-pin-and-verify body that could drift. Extracted to one `verifyRsJwt` (`identity/jwt-verify.ts`) used by both; each caller keeps its own registered-claim checks and error mapping. The Ghost auth path's behavior (and its 14-test forge/replay suite) is unchanged.
- **OFC-226 (Low) — no shared Ghost-first wrapper.** The lock→push→commit envelope was re-implemented per handler. `runRecordWrite` + `replyWriteError` now own the ordering and the error→status mapping in one place, so a future write can't silently reopen the window.
- **OFC-227 (Nit) — stale "four pushed fields" comment** in `ghost-push.ts` → three.

Regression locks added: a deterministic serialization test (a blocking Ghost client holds the record lock across a PATCH's in-flight push while a concurrent verify is forced to wait — OFC-220) and an in-lock-snapshot test (a concurrent unsubscribe committing first is reflected in the deceased snapshot — OFC-221), plus targeted tests for OFC-219/222/223/224. Gate green: 563 unit + 42 emulator + 111 e2e.

## Phase 5b-1 write-path test harness — ghost-staging mirror (2026-07-08)
