To exercise the Book→Ghost write path against a real Ghost (ghost-staging only, D72), the fake-data seed can mirror the seeded profiles into ghost-staging as real members. Design (Forrest's call — a delta reconcile in preference to a DB backup/restore):

- **Delta reconcile, not a load.** `tools/fake-data/src/mirror-ghost-staging.ts` (pure planner in `ghost-reconcile.ts`, unit-tested) brings ghost-staging's seed-owned members into correspondence with the current fake profiles — create missing, update drifted (name/subscription), delete orphans — matching by normalized email, then writes each real `ghostMemberId` back into Firestore. **Re-running it is the reset** after a testing session mutated Ghost; it only touches what changed, so the recurring cost is trivial (the one-time cost is the initial ~1k creates). This is why no Ghost DB backup/restore is needed.
- **Safety scoping (by fake-email domain).** The reconcile lists/updates/**deletes** only Ghost members whose email is a fake `@example.test` address — the fake-data domain. Real accounts (the tester-linked profile, the operator's own, the linter's) have real emails and are never touched. The domain scope is deliberate over a `book-seed` label (which an interim version used): members the **real write path** creates during a testing session — a de-brother reversal, a future new-brother create — carry no test-only label, so a label-scoped reconcile could never see or clean them up and they'd orphan on every reset. Verified live 2026-07-08: a de-brother-reversal member was left as an orphan by the label-scoped version and correctly deleted by the domain-scoped one.
- **The generator no longer mints a fake `ghostMemberId`.** A fake id would `502` the Ghost-first push against a nonexistent member once the real Admin client is configured; with no id a profile cleanly skips the push (N65). The mirror is the sole source of real ids.
- **Opt-in.** Gated by the repo var `STAGING_GHOST_MIRROR` (default off): the seed mirrors only when it is `true` (and autoseed is on), so ordinary deploys neither hit ghost-staging nor depend on it. The Admin key rides from Secret Manager (`ghost-admin-api-key`) into both Cloud Run (runtime) and the deploy's mirror step; it is never in the tree. Runbook in `infra/README.md`.

---

## Phase 5b-2 implementation notes (2026-07-09)

### N69 — The Book/Ghost alignment audit is read-only into Book in every category (reverting D103's newsletter write-back); the bounce report is a separate CSV download; the maintenance/outage path is one generic screen (simplifying D118)

Phase 5b-2 built the read/reconcile half of the Ghost integration — the reconciliation audit, the email-bounce report, and the down-for-maintenance mechanism — and, in the building, three of the pinned designs were deliberately simplified with Forrest. All three simplifications *reduce* mechanism.

- **The audit writes nothing into Book — every category is report-only (amends D103, reverting its scoped Ghost→Book write).** D103 had the audit *resolve* the newsletter flag by most-recent-change-wins, writing Ghost→Book on a member's own unsubscribe (a scoped exception to D55's read-only-into-Book invariant) and re-pushing Book→Ghost when Book changed later. That write-back is **removed**: the audit reports a newsletter disagreement exactly like every other field and **changes nothing** — a human (or the future "AI system administrator", Linear OFC-214) flips the correct toggle by hand using the controls that already exist. Two reasons made this clean rather than a loss: (1) the Book→Ghost re-push direction was already foreclosed by the 5b-1 **Ghost-first-gated** write (N65) — Book can no longer silently get ahead of Ghost, so that arm defended a case that no longer occurs; and (2) removing the Ghost→Book arm **restores D55's read-only-into-Book invariant in full**, erasing the one exception that made the audit asymmetric and the failed-push-undo hazard it carried. The Ghost-side change timestamp is still *read and reported* (see OFC-230 below) as **advisory context** — it tells the resolver which side changed later — but it is no longer a control input, so if Ghost ever stopped exposing it the report degrades (no `ghostChangedAt`) rather than breaking. Consequence for the `resolution` field pinned in API-SPEC §7: it is **never set** (the audit resolves nothing); the field stays in the shape only as the frozen contract. (Forrest's call.)
- **Rename + read-only HTTP shape.** With no write-back, "Sync with Ghost" is a misnomer — nothing is synced. The Admin card is **"Book / Ghost alignment audit"** and the endpoint is renamed `POST /api/admin/sync-ghost` → **`GET /api/admin/ghost-audit`** (read-only ⇒ `GET`, matching `GET /api/admin/backup`). It is admin-only at effective role (N31), rate-limited, `no-store`, and audited as `ghost.audit` (a whole-database action, count = discrepancies).
- **Both reports are download-only; the bounce report is its own endpoint + CSV (amends D120).** Neither report renders in Book's UI. Each is a button that runs the job and downloads a file: the **audit → Markdown** (`book-ghost-audit-YYYY-MM-DD.md`; heterogeneous, meant to be read), the **bounce report → CSV** (`book-bounce-report-YYYY-MM-DD.csv`; tabular, opens in a spreadsheet). D120 had the bounce report *ride each audit run* and be "logged and/or a CSV"; it is instead its **own** `GET /api/admin/bounce-report` (audited `bounce.report`) behind its own card — a different job (email-address maintenance, not drift) — and the artifact is a **CSV download**, not a Cloud Logging line (logging is *less* accessible to the one admin who needs it; Forrest's call). The endpoints return the pinned JSON (API-SPEC §7); the SPA formats the download client-side, so the JSON stays the machine-readable contract the future scheduled job / OFC-214 sysadmin consumes directly.
- **The consolidated scheduled job stays Phase 7.** 5b-2 builds the audit *endpoint*, triggered manually from the Admin card. The D99 Cloud-Scheduler health-check job (which will call this same endpoint on a timer, alongside the login canary and the contract test) is Phase 7 — there is one audit implementation, two triggers (manual now, scheduled later).
- **Maintenance / outage is one generic screen; no backend maintenance flag (simplifies D118).** D118 specified a maintenance-flavored `503` so a cached SPA could distinguish *planned* downtime from an *unplanned* outage. That distinction is dropped: a cached, already-loaded SPA that cannot reach the backend **for any reason** shows one calm "Book is temporarily unavailable" screen with a manual retry (Forrest's call). So 5b-2 ships (1) the **edge static `maintenance.html`** + operator swap scripts (`infra/maintenance-on.sh` / `-off.sh` deploy the alternate `firebase.maintenance.json` that rewrites every path to the static page, served by Firebase Hosting independently of Cloud Run — the planned-downtime, fresh-visitor case, Forrest's script-swap mechanism over an admin toggle), and (2) the **SPA fallback**: the session gate's `error` state renders the maintenance/outage screen. A load-bearing fix rode along: `SessionContext` treated *any* `ApiError` as "signed out", so a `5xx`/`503` during an outage bounced the member to the Ghost sign-in flow — now **only `401`/`403`** means signed-out, and every other failure (network, cold-start timeout, `5xx`) lands on the retryable outage screen (a `503` reads as unavailable, not as re-login).

**Build mechanics.** A read seam `GhostReader` (`listMembers` / `listNewsletterEvents` / `listBounceEvents` / best-effort `listNewsletterEmails`) is the read-side sibling of the write-only `GhostLifecycle`; both the write client and the new reader share one `GhostAdminHttp` (auth + pagination) so they can never drift on how they authenticate to Ghost. The reader is **optional** — unconfigured (local dev, no Admin key) the two routes fail closed with `503` (mirroring the roster verifier), unlike the write lifecycle's succeed-and-log stub, because a read has nothing to stub. The audit + bounce engines are pure functions over already-fetched inputs (unit-tested with fixtures); the report wire shapes (`GhostAuditReport`/`Discrepancy`, `BounceReport`/`BounceRow`) live in `@pbe/shared` so producer and download-formatter can't drift (D3). `AdminUserStore` grew `listUserIds()` for the `bookInternalOrphan` users-with-no-profile check (D98). The bounce join is ported from the proven `ghost-member-export/export-bounces.js`.

**OFC-230 resolved (the D103 must-verify).** A throwaway probe against ghost-staging's Admin API confirmed both reads the audit needs: `GET /members/?include=newsletters` returns each member's `subscribed` state, and `GET /members/events/?filter=type:newsletter_event` returns subscribe/unsubscribe events shaped `{ member_id, subscribed, created_at, source }` — i.e. Ghost **does** expose the unsubscribe timestamp programmatically. Because the audit no longer *acts* on it, this moved from a load-bearing dependency to advisory enrichment, so OFC-230 is closed either way.

*Amends D103 (audit is now read-only into Book — the newsletter reconcile is report-only, not applied), D120 (a separate CSV-download bounce report, not a log line riding the audit), and D118 (one generic outage screen; no maintenance-`503` backend flag). Records to `ENGINEERING-DESIGN §5.1`, `API-SPEC §1.5`/`§7`/`§10`, `PRD §5.8.3`/`§6.1`; builds on D55/D99/D96/N65.*

### Phase 5b-2 code-review remediation (2026-07-09)

A high-effort `/code-review` (8 finder angles) ran in-session on the 5b-2 branch; findings were remediated before merge. The substantive ones:

- **CSV formula-injection hardening reunified.** The bounce report's hand-rolled `csvEscape` only guarded the four `= + - @` sigils, silently weaker than the shared `@pbe/shared` neutralizer, which also treats stripped line-break/whitespace leaders (the OFC-99/S9 case). Replaced it with a new exported `formatCsvCell` (neutralize + RFC-4180 escape) from `csv.ts` — now the single cell formatter for **all** Book CSV exports (directory/MITAA + bounce), so the hardening can't drift.
- **`skipped` bounces surfaced.** `planBounceReport` counts bounce events dropped because their member was hard-deleted from Ghost, but the CSV/card ignored it — so an all-skipped run read as "no bounces on record." The card now appends a "N events skipped" note and the CSV a trailing comment row.
- **A leftover Ghost member for a de-brothered profile now surfaces.** `referencedGhostIds` had included de-brothered profiles' (stale) `ghostMemberId`s, which suppressed a *still-live* member (a failed Ghost delete) from `unmatchedGhostMember` — reported in no category. De-brothered ids are now excluded, so the leftover surfaces.
- **Fewer false positives / more robust reads:** name-drift compares NFC-normalized on both sides (matching the email comparison), so a Unicode-form difference isn't permanent drift; `subscribed` is derived from the authoritative `newsletters` **relation** first (the global boolean can disagree); the newsletter-event timestamp gained the same event-level `created_at` fallback bounce events already had; and the "latest event" is chosen by parsed epoch millis, not a lexical string compare.
- **Loud over silent:** `GhostAdminHttp.getAll` now **throws** on hitting its page cap rather than returning a partial (silently-undercounted) list — the audit fails `502` instead of lying. The unbounded event-history fetch that motivates a real bound is **OFC-231** (Phase 7).
- **Cleanups:** dropped the unused `labels` include on the members fetch; removed the now-orphaned `ComingLaterBadge`; reused `formatTimestamp` in the audit-report Markdown; fixed the in-memory `AdminUserStore.listUserIds` double to union role+star doc ids (test fidelity); and gave the `maintenance-on/off.sh` scripts `--help` + `--dry-run` (CLAUDE.md CLI convention). New tests cover each behavior change.

*Post-merge report-UX follow-ups (2026-07-09, from live testing): the alignment-audit Markdown groups each category into a **collapsible `<details open>` section with an `<h2>` title** (open by default — an audit never hides a finding — so a long section can be folded to scan past it; PRs #42/#43). Presentation only.*

## Phase 5.5a implementation notes (2026-07-10, the server write path)

Phase 5.5a cleared the two `5.5a`-tagged Linear tickets — a manager-write privacy leak and the never-built create path — both in the `apps/api` profile-routes / capabilities slice.

### N70 — A manager may not *write* a toggle field the record's privacy hides from them (OFC-206)

OFC-206: a manager, on another brother's record, cannot *see* a contact / spouse / emergency field whose owner set the governing share-flag off (the read projection hides it — only admins see through an off toggle, D19), yet the write path let them *overwrite* it — a blind clobber of data they were never shown. The cause was an asymmetry between Book's two access-control tables: the read side (`visibility.ts`) gates a `toggle` field on the record's privacy flags, but the write side (`capabilities.ts` `WRITE_RULE`) marked those fields `editable`, which is privacy-independent. **Fix: the write gate now mirrors the read gate** — a new shared `canWriteFieldOnRecord(role, isOwner, field, privacy)` is the static `canWriteField` **narrowed by** whether the caller can read that field on that record (`fieldVisibleToRole`). The principle is "you cannot write what you cannot read": only a **non-owner manager** is ever blind (the owner reads their whole record; an admin reads through every toggle), and only on a privacy-gated `toggle` field, so those are the only writes newly rejected — every other field is unchanged. `partitionWritableFields` now takes the record's `privacy`, and the PATCH route passes `stored.privacy` (authoritative — the only gated role, manager, cannot write `privacy` itself, so no in-flight change can widen its own powers within the request). The client mirrors it in two places: the edit form drops a hidden toggle field from its diff (`patch.ts`), and renders the existing "🔒 this field is private" marker in place of an editable input for those fields (`ProfileEdit.tsx`), so a manager is never shown an empty box to type a blind value into. Server-side reject stays the single enforcement point (D82); the client is courtesy. *Records to API-SPEC §3 (PATCH field-level rule); builds on D19/D82/D106/N10.*

### N71 — Add Brother is a two-step create — an essentials form, then the regular edit page (replaces API-SPEC §3's "no empty-then-fill")

OFC-201: "Add Brother" errored because `POST /api/profiles` was never built and `/brother/new` fell through to the `/brother/:id` fetch (id `"new"` → "couldn't load this profile"). Building it reopened the create UX. The delivered API-SPEC §3 had specified a **single atomic POST of a complete Profile body** — "there is no empty-then-fill step" — which would have meant a second full-page form parallel to the edit form. **Forrest's call: do the minimum instead.** Add Brother is now two steps: (1) a small **essentials form** (`/brother/new`, `NewProfile.tsx`) collecting only the identity fields a new record and its Ghost member need — Constitution id, first / last name, class year, email; (2) `POST /api/profiles` creates the record **and** the Ghost member, then the admin is handed to the **regular `/brother/:id/edit` page** to fill in everything else. No bespoke create form — once the record exists, editing it is the ordinary path, nothing new to maintain. This is deliberately the "empty-then-fill" step §3 ruled out; the trade is accepted because the created record is always **valid** (the always-required fields — first/last name, class year — are exactly the essentials collected), never a junk skeleton, and the reuse removes a whole parallel form. **(Corrected by N72: email is *optional*, not required — a brother with no email is created Book-only, and Ghost is not gated on email; the "and its Ghost member" / "creates the record **and** the Ghost member" phrasing above is the always-email happy path, not a universal.)** **Backend contract** (`POST /api/profiles`, admin-only): a partial body is accepted; the server strips any client-sent protected/server-managed fields, fills the schema privacy defaults + status flags (`deceased`/`debrothered` off, `hasHeadshot:false`) + housekeeping stamps, and assembles a **well-formed** record (so this one un-hydrated insert can't seed a record the projection later 500s on); validation in create mode (`requireRequired`) plus the dataset structural checks (email uniqueness, big-brother existence/cycle); a **Ghost-first-gated create** (`createMember` mints the member and its fresh id folds into the write; a brother with no email is created **Book-only**, mirroring the PATCH path's no-`ghostMemberId` skip — `502 ghost_create_failed` aborts clean on a Ghost failure, nothing written); an **atomic Firestore `create()`** for the `409` duplicate (with a fast in-memory pre-check); a cache insert (`applyCreate`, read-your-writes); a `profile.create` audit entry (names, never values); `201` + `ETag`. *Replaces API-SPEC §3's single-complete-body / no-empty-then-fill create; records to API-SPEC §3, PRD §5.5/§5.6.8; builds on D96/N41/N65 (Ghost-first), D25/D28/D82.*

### N72 — Email is optional; a new brother defaults to subscribed; Ghost operations tolerate a Ghost-less brother (OFC-201 follow-up; corrects N71)

Phase 5.5a live testing surfaced a wrong assumption that had crept into the code: that **every Book record has a matching Ghost record**. It does not. Book is the fraternity's system-of-record, gated on the solemn "did they physically sign the constitution" — **not** on the trivial "do they have an email." A large fraction of brothers (historically ~1/3) legitimately have no email and no Ghost record: brothers who died before email existed, and living brothers who have chosen not to share an address. This was already the design (D20's "no-email/unidentified" case; D115 reusing "the existing tolerance for a Book profile with no Ghost member, C15/D20"); the *implementation* had drifted from it in three places. (Forrest caught it in testing.)

- **Add Brother: email is optional.** `NewProfile.tsx` no longer requires email. When it is blank the client omits the field entirely and `POST /api/profiles` creates a **Book-only** record — no Ghost member — exactly as the backend already supported. Only the form was over-strict; the API was already correct.
- **A new brother defaults to *subscribed* to PBE News.** `assembleNewProfile` defaults `allowNewsletterEmail` to **`true`** (was `false`) — the D45 pro-sharing/opt-out default, and what an admin adding a member expects; a brother created with an email is therefore subscribed in Ghost from the start. `allowShareWithMITAA` stays opt-out `false` (D56/D93).
- **Ghost operations tolerate a Ghost-less brother (production correctness).** `DELETE /api/profiles/{id}` (`admin.ts`) and the de-brother **raise** (`status.ts`) now call `deleteMember` **only when `ghostMemberId` is set**; the de-brother **reverse** calls `createMember` **only when the brother has an email** (mirroring the create path). Without these guards the real `GhostAdminLifecycle` throws (`deleteMember`/`createMember` require an id/email), which would `502` every email-less brother out of ever being deleted or de-brothered. These were **masked on staging** by the default `StubGhostLifecycle` (which never throws), so they were latent, production-only bugs — the reason live staging testing didn't catch them. The read paths were already correct: the Book/Ghost audit only reports `missingGhostMember` for a brother who *has* an email (`ghost-audit.ts`, C15/D20), and the PATCH Ghost push already skips a record with no `ghostMemberId`.

**Deferred as its own MVP-critical ticket (OFC-232):** there is currently **no path** to create a Ghost record for an *existing* Book-only brother who later provides an email — `PATCH` only *updates* an existing member. That is a new capability needing its own design decision (auto-on-email-add vs. an explicit affordance; deceased/de-brothered/collision edge cases) and is not in this follow-up.

*Corrects N71 (email optional, not required); records to API-SPEC §3, PRD §5.6.8; builds on D20/D115/C15 (Ghost-less brothers), D45 (opt-out default), D96/N65 (Ghost-first).*

### N73 — Verification status is public; the verifier's name is shown, resolved client-side (OFC-207 / OFC-208; Phase 5.5b)

Two Profile-page live-test tickets, taken together as one change. **Forrest's call on both.**

- **OFC-207 — verification is public (amends D28).** `lastVerifiedDate` and `verifiedBy` were `restricted` (owner/manager/admin read); they are now **`public`**, so every brother sees whether — and when — another brother's record was last verified. Rationale (Forrest): verification is an accuracy signal useful to all readers and a **public administrative act**, not PII. The change is one line each in `FIELD_VISIBILITY`; because the projection, the client render-gates, and the CSV export all read that one table (D5/D50), brothers now receive the two fields on profiles, in the bulk payload, and as export columns, with no other server change. The **right to mark verified** is unaffected — it lives on the write side (`capabilities.ts`) and stays owner/manager/admin. The Directory's **verification filters** ("not verified since," etc.) stay a manager/admin affordance: "filterable ⟺ visible" gates those controls by role, not by the field's read class, so they did not follow the field to public. The verification read-out moved out of the Profile page's owner/staff-only "restricted" block into an all-viewer element; the Verify button, the last-updated line, the consent digest, and the admin note remain owner/staff.

- **OFC-208 — show *who* verified, resolved client-side with a date-only fallback.** The UI showed only the date though `verifiedBy` was already stored and stamped by both write paths. It now reads "Verified 2026-07-06 by Alain Smithee '81" — "(self)" for an owner self-confirm — resolving the verifier's Constitution id to his Canonical Name from the **same in-memory roster** the Big/Little-Brother links use, no server or wire change (**D3/D82 kept pure**). Consequence, and **Forrest's explicit choice** over a server-supplied name: a brother's roster omits unlisted/de-brothered records (D124/D115), so when the verifier is hidden from *this* viewer the name can't be resolved — the line then shows **date only** rather than inventing or leaking a name. Managers and admins hold the whole roster, so they always see the verifier's name; only a brother ever hits the date-only fallback, and only for a hidden verifier (a rare case — verifiers are staff or self). The attribution is a small pure helper (`verifierAttribution`, unit-tested); the read-out degrades to a bare date, never a blank "by". **Accepted consequence (Forrest's call, from the 5.5b code review):** because `verifiedBy` is public, a brother receives the verifier's Constitution id on the wire (and as a CSV column) even when that verifier is an unlisted/de-brothered brother otherwise whole-record-hidden from him (D124/D115) — the date-only fallback hides the *name*, not the *id*. This is **knowingly accepted**: verification is a manager/admin acting in a staff capacity, and disclosing which staff member took that public administrative action is not treated as a privacy problem. The name is still not resolvable client-side for such a verifier, so nothing beyond the id leaks.

*Records to DATABASE-SCHEMA §3.3/§9/§10 (visibility class + export note), amends D28; builds on D3/D5/D50/D82, D124/D115. The sibling 5.5b tickets — OFC-203 (relationship thumbnails), OFC-198 (← Directory link styling), and OFC-204 (closed as report-in-error: admin note already shows on the view page for staff; it is absent only on one's **own** record, where `projectSelf` strips it by design) — are display-only and need no decision entry.*

### N74 — Dependabot #7 (uuid CVE-2026-41907): fixed by a root npm `override` to uuid ^11.1.1; the vulnerable API is confirmed unreachable here

GitHub Dependabot alert #7 (GHSA-w5hq-g745-h8pq, moderate): `uuid` < 11.1.1 performs **silent out-of-bounds partial writes** in `v3()`/`v5()`/`v6()` when the caller supplies an output buffer with a bad offset — those three functions lack the `RangeError` bounds check that `v1()`/`v4()`/`v7()` have. Book never depends on `uuid` directly; the flagged `uuid@9.0.1` arrived through three transitive chains — two **runtime** (apps/api: `firebase-admin` → `@google-cloud/firestore` → `google-gax`, and → `@google-cloud/storage` → `teeny-request`) and one **dev-only** (`firebase-tools` → `gaxios`). **Reachability assessment: not exploitable in Book.** Every one of those dependents calls only `uuid.v4()` (request/stream ids and multipart boundaries — verified by grepping each package's shipped build), and `v4()` has the bounds check; nothing in or under Book ever calls `v3`/`v5`/`v6`, with or without a buffer. The fix is therefore hygiene — clearing the alert and the class of risk — not an urgent hole.

**Fix: a root `overrides: { "uuid": "^11.1.1" }`**, because no patched 9.x exists (first patched versions are 11.1.1 / 12.0.1 / 13.0.1 / 14.0.0) and every parent pins `^9` with no fixed release in range — google-gax 4.x is capped at `uuid ^9.0.1` even at its latest (firestore 7 pins gax 4), and `@google-cloud/storage` pins `teeny-request ^9` whose only uuid-free release is 10.x; even firebase-admin 14 (a major bump) still resolves the same vulnerable chains, so waiting on upstream or upgrading firebase-admin would not have cleared it. uuid 11 is drop-in for these consumers: same `v4()` named export, dual CJS/ESM (`main: dist/cjs`), Node ≥ 16 (repo requires ≥ 24). The override intentionally covers *all* uuid instances — a version-scoped key (`"uuid@<11.1.1"`) applied inconsistently in testing — so the one other copy (dev-only `universal-analytics`'s already-patched 14.0.1) is pinned down to 11.1.1 too; harmless, since it also only calls `v4()`.

Two npm mechanics worth remembering (the *why* of the diff shape): **(1) root overrides only apply to workspace-reached edges on a from-scratch resolution** — with the existing `package-lock.json` in place, `npm install` and `npm update uuid` both kept re-materializing nested `uuid@9.0.1` under the firestore/teeny-request chains (they enter via the `apps/api` / `tools/fake-data` workspaces; the root-dev `firebase-tools` chain overrode fine). The lockfile was therefore **regenerated** (delete lock + `node_modules`, fresh `npm install`), which is why the PR carries ~150 incidental in-range patch/minor bumps alongside the uuid change — a routine-`npm update`-sized drift, validated by the full gate. After regeneration the tree holds **exactly one** uuid entry, 11.1.1, deduped everywhere, and `npm ci` reproduces it. **(2) `npm ls uuid` will report the workspace-side edges as "invalid"** (`^9.0.1` vs 11.1.1) — cosmetic; reification is correct, `npm audit` no longer reports the advisory. **Remove the override** when the Google chains move to uuid ≥ 11 on their own (check `npm ls uuid --all` after future firebase-admin/firebase-tools bumps). The one remaining `npm audit` finding (dev-only `@opentelemetry/core` unbounded-memory advisory via firebase-tools → pubsub, GHSA-8988-4f7v-96qf) predates this change, has no non-breaking fix, and is not flagged by Dependabot; left alone deliberately.

## Phase 5.5c implementation notes (2026-07-11, the app shell & session error handling)

Phase 5.5c cleared the four `5.5c`-tagged Linear tickets — all in the SPA's app-shell / session-error slice: OFC-192 (an unlisted record vanishing for an admin), OFC-193 (misleading session-expiry messaging + an unauthenticated Admin-page exposure), OFC-202 (unknown URLs falling through to the Directory), and OFC-63 (the long-lived-tab new-version toast).

### N75 — A per-role `404` on `GET /api/profiles/:id` must be `no-store`: Firebase Hosting caches header-less `/api` responses for 10 minutes (OFC-192)

OFC-192: an admin views an **unlisted** record (visible to staff, D124), steps down to "View as brother" (the record is correctly `404` — the whole-record hide), then stops impersonating — and the record stays **"Brother not found"** even as an admin, persisting across a hard reload and a fresh tab. The persistence across a new tab is the tell: it rules out per-tab and per-session state, pointing at a **shared, URL-keyed cache**. Client, route logic, and the real Firestore-backed session store were each exonerated by test (the impersonation round-trip clears the effective role correctly at every layer — N31 holds), which left the one layer none of those tests exercise: **the CDN in front of Cloud Run.**

**Root cause (confirmed live on staging):** the single-record read set `Cache-Control: no-store` on its **success** path (D95) but on **none of its error branches**. The `404` therefore left Cloud Run with *no* `Cache-Control`, and **Firebase Hosting injects a default `Cache-Control: max-age=600` on `/api/**` rewrite responses that don't set their own** — so the brother-projection `404` was cached for 10 minutes and replayed to the admin's later `GET /api/profiles/<id>` for the same URL (DevTools showed `404 Not Found (from disk cache)`, `max-age=600`). The record "disappears" for the admin until the cache lapses; the Directory still shows it because that is a different URL (`GET /api/profiles`, already `no-store`). This also explains why no local layer reproduced it: `app.inject`, the emulator, and Playwright's mocked responses all bypass the Hosting cache.

**Fix:** hoist `reply.header("Cache-Control", "no-store")` to the **top** of the `GET /api/profiles/:id` handler so **every** branch (400/401/404/200) is uncacheable — a read whose visibility is per-role must never let one role's response be replayed to another. Regression tests assert the unlisted `404` and the invalid-id `400` both carry `no-store`. **Principle:** any per-role/per-session `/api` response is uncacheable on *all* branches, not just the happy path.

**Two confirmed facts about the Hosting header layer** (they answer half of OFC-212, empirically): (a) an **explicit** backend `no-store` **is** honored end-to-end — the success `200` was not cached, so the PII success paths look safe for D95; (b) the firebase.json `**` `headers` rule (`no-cache, must-revalidate`) does **not** reach `/api/**` **rewrites** — the delivered header on the header-less `404` was `max-age=600`, Hosting's rewrite default, not the `**` value. The broader risk this exposes — *any* `/api` response that omits `Cache-Control` silently inherits `max-age=600` — is logged as an overlap note on **OFC-212**, whose systematic audit (every endpoint, every branch) and belt-and-suspenders Hosting `source:"/api/**"` → `no-store` rule remain its Phase-7 scope. This N75 fix is the targeted close of the one path that manifested as a bug. *Records to API-SPEC §3; builds on D95/D124/D126, N31; overlaps OFC-212.*

### N76 — One central 401 interceptor flips the whole SPA to signed-out, *except* the edit-form Save path (OFC-193; honors D109)

OFC-193: when a session lapsed under an open tab (the 4-hour cap, D22), the SPA still believed it was authenticated, so each subsequent call's `401` was mistaken by that page for a transient failure — the Directory and Profile pages said "couldn't load, please refresh" (misleading — a refresh never helps a logged-out user), and worse, an already-open **Admin page kept rendering**, letting a logged-out admin sit on it and get false "something went wrong" errors from backup/banner actions. **Fix (one mechanism, not per-page):** a module-level unauthorized handler in the SPA's `api.ts` fetch layer fires whenever any response is a **401**; `SessionProvider` registers it to transition the app to `unauthenticated` and drop the cached roster (D95). Because the whole tree is gated on session state, one `401` anywhere bounces Directory, Profile, **and** Admin to the sign-in screen at once — the "unauthenticated user lingering on Admin" problem falls out of the gate rather than needing an Admin-specific guard. Keyed strictly on **401**: a `403` is an in-session authorization decision (a field the role may not write, N70) and must **not** read as "logged out," so it is left to the caller.

**The one carve-out — the edit-form Save path — preserves D109 (Forrest's call, Option A).** A blanket bounce would collide with **D109**'s non-destructive-recovery contract: a mid-edit `401` must *keep the in-progress form*, never yank the user to the sign-in screen and silently discard unsaved work. So the writes that carry unsaved form input — `PATCH /api/profiles/:id`, the headshot `PUT`/`DELETE` (staged crop), and `POST /api/profiles` (Add-Brother) — **opt out** of the app-wide bounce (an `asError(response, { silent: true })` flag in `api.ts`) and handle their own `401` locally: the container stays mounted, the form and staged photo survive, and the Save surfaces a new **`expired` `SubmitResult`** rendered as "Your session has expired. Please sign in again to save your changes." The **full** D109 flow (child-window re-auth + resume the same Save with its original `If-Match`) remains unbuilt and is filed as its own ticket — this batch's carve-out is the minimal step that stops the regression (no lost work + an honest message), not the full recovery. Every *other* write (banner set, stars, bug-report, the verify/deceased/de-brother status actions) has no unsaved long-form input and still bounces, so OFC-193's Admin-action cases are fully covered.

The sign-in screen gains an "expired" variant — when the transition came from a live session it shows a calm `<output>` status region, distinct from a first-time visitor. The copy is deliberately **cause-agnostic — "You've been signed out. Please sign in again."** — because a mid-session `401` is not only inactivity: **N53** active revocation (a de-brothered / demoted brother's next call `401`s) reaches the same path, for which "due to inactivity" would be wrong. Chosen (Forrest's call) over the ticket's literal "refresh to log in" wording because the sign-in screen already offers the sign-in affordance directly. *Records to API-SPEC §2/§1.2, ENGINEERING-DESIGN §2.3; builds on D22/D109/D125/N53, D95; the full D109 child-window recovery is deferred to its own ticket.*

*Live-test follow-up (2026-07-11): the interim `expired` message has **no in-page re-auth affordance** — to recover, the user signs in on another tab (the shared per-origin `__session` cookie then lets the held Save commit on the untouched editor tab) or navigates away and loses the edit. The other-tab recovery was confirmed working. Adding an in-page "Sign in" button that opens the handshake in a **new tab/window** (never navigating the editor tab) would collapse that into one click, but **Forrest's call: skip the interim button and wait for the seamless OFC-236 child-window recovery** — no users yet, so the friction is acceptable and not worth a throwaway affordance.*

### N77 — Unknown URLs render a client-side "Page not found", not a real HTTP 404 (OFC-202, Forrest's call)

OFC-202: a random URL (`/xyzzy`) silently showed the Directory. **Forrest's call:** render an honest **client-side** "Page not found" screen (in the app shell, with a link back to the Directory) rather than pursue a true HTTP `404`. Book is an SPA behind Firebase Hosting's `** → /index.html` rewrite (D126), so Hosting has no route table and serves the shell at `200` for every unknown path; a real `404` would mean teaching a backend layer the full set of valid routes — disproportionate for an internal members app. The trade is explicit and accepted: the HTTP status stays `200`, but the user sees a real not-found UI. The route sits inside the session gate, so an unknown URL opened while signed out still lands on sign-in. *Records to PRD §5 (shell); builds on D126.*

### N78 — Long-lived-tab version toast: a build-stamped `version.json` polled frugally (OFC-63, implements N25's follow-up)

OFC-63 (the follow-up N25 flagged): the `no-cache` SPA shell means a returning visitor picks up a new bundle on the next reload/navigation, but a tab left **open** runs the old bundle forever. **Fix:** the build emits a tiny un-hashed `version.json` carrying the build id (a Vite plugin reusing the existing `__APP_VERSION__`/`BOOK_APP_VERSION` stamp — DATABASE-SCHEMA §6.4); because it isn't content-hashed it is served `no-cache` and needs **no** Hosting header change. A shell-mounted watcher records the id the tab booted with and polls `version.json` **frugally** — on window refocus and tab-visibility plus a generous 30-minute interval, backing off entirely while hidden (bytes + battery for the slow-link, 60+ audience) — and raises **one** calm, dismissible `<output>` toast with a Refresh button when the deployed id has moved on; the user chooses when to reload. Deliberately not a service worker (a whole caching layer to own; overkill and riskier for this audience). *Records to PRD §5 (shell); builds on N25, D79 (a11y).*

*Live-test confirmed (2026-07-11): across a real staging deploy, an open tab's toast fires on refocus, Refresh reloads onto the new build, dismiss clears it, and an ignored update leaves the toast as a persistent reminder while the old bundle keeps working (until an API-incompatible call). Two live-test polish items landed: the toast sits **20% from the top** (the bottom edge was easy to miss) and uses the **external brand — "A new version of PBE Address Book is available"** ("Book" is the internal codename). **Behavior worth knowing (surfaced during live testing):** a given tab announces **at most one** update — the poll tears down once a newer build is found, and a dismiss is per-tab-permanent — so a long-lived tab does not re-nag for a *second* later deploy; a reload re-arms it. This is the intended "one quiet toast, never a nag" posture, and it is why, across several rapid test deploys, a tab already on the newest build (or one that already dismissed) shows nothing.*

### N79 — Directory row selection persists across search / filter / sort / navigation; a per-instance in-memory bucket (OFC-196; amends D41, extends D31)

OFC-196: manager/admin row selections (the Select column feeding Export) evaporated on any search/filter change and on navigating away and back — so a user could not build a **disjoint set across filters** (select the class of 1970, then the class of 1980, export both), which is the main thing selection is now for. **This reverses D41's "selection clears on any search/filter change."** D41's sole rationale was to scope a *destructive bulk delete* to visible rows ("no deleting rows I can't see"); **D100 removed Directory bulk-delete**, leaving CSV **Export** (D90/D92) as the only consumer — a benign, consent-gated read — so keeping out-of-view ids is no longer hazardous and is exactly what the disjoint-set workflow needs (**Forrest's call**, 2026-07-12).

**Where it lives — a fourth state bucket beyond D31's three.** D31 partitions view state into the URL (the shareable view), History-API state (per-*entry* transient context: the Starred-only flag and scroll), and localStorage (the column lens). Selection fits none: it is **private** (never in a shared link — like the stars it feeds), **transient** (dropped on a full reload or in a new tab), and **session-scoped** — it must outlive the Directory's remount as the user round-trips to a Profile, which is broader than any single history entry. So it lives in a **per-instance in-memory React context** (`SelectionProvider`) mounted on the authenticated layout route **above** the Directory outlet: it survives the child remount, and because it sits inside the session gate a sign-out unmounts it and clears the selection for free. Keyed by stable Constitution ID (unchanged from D41).

**Consequent behavior.** Header **select-all** now **unions** the current view's rows into the selection and its inverse **removes just those rows** — never touching off-view picks; its tri-state reflects the *visible* rows only. **Export** serializes the whole selected set resolved over the **entire** dataset (sorted by the active sort), so a disjoint selection exports in full rather than being silently clipped to the current filter. Because a persistent selection can be entirely off-screen, the action bar carries an always-visible **count** and an explicit **Clear selection** control, so the selection never invisibly drives an export. *Records to PRD §5.6.8; amends D41 (supersedes its clear-on-view-change), extends D31.*

### N80 — The masthead logo is a clean-slate reset, distinct from the "← Directory" back-navigation (OFC-194)

OFC-194: clicking the masthead crest/wordmark (a plain link to `/`) was meant to return to a *clean* Directory but left the **"Starred only"** filter on. Root cause is the D31 state split: a bare `/` clears the URL-held view (search, filters, sort, deceased) but has no effect on the **History-held** Starred-only flag (D39) or — now — the persisted **selection** (N79), so those two survived. **Fix:** the masthead link carries an explicit one-shot **`reset` intent** (`<Link to="/" state={{ reset: true }}>`); the Directory consumes it once (guarded by the history entry's `key`, and stripped via a `replace` navigation so a later Back never re-fires it) and clears the Starred-only flag and the selection. This gives Book **two deliberately different return-to-Directory affordances**: the **masthead = "home, fresh"** — a full clean slate (**Forrest's call**, 2026-07-12) — while the **"← Directory" back-links preserve the working view** (scroll, filters, selection) exactly as before. *Records to PRD §5.6.6; builds on D31/D39/N79.*

### N81 — The Class-Year / Constitution-ID numeric grammar gains one-sided (open-bound) ranges (OFC-195; extends D38)

OFC-195: D38's numeric-grammar filter accepted single years, comma lists, and closed `lo-hi` ranges but **not** a range bounded on one side — `1985-` ("that year and later") or `-1990` ("that year and earlier"), a natural way to filter by class year. **Fix:** the parser accepts an open bound on either side, carried as a `null` in the range tuple, and the matcher treats `null` as unbounded; a bare `-` (no bound at all) stays an error, consistent with the "flag bad tokens inline, never silently drop" rule (§5.6.4). Applies to both grammar fields (Class Year and Constitution ID); the field placeholder and the inline error hint now advertise the open-ended form. *Records to PRD §5.6.4; extends D38.*

### N82 — Docs-only merges to `main` skip the post-merge CI re-run, and therefore the staging deploy (Forrest's call)

Every merge to `main` re-ran the full CI gate and, on green, auto-deployed staging — even for changes that cannot affect the shipped artifact (design docs, the decision log and its index, the vendored dev-workflow skill). Docs-only merges have become routine (the decision-log-index and skill-sync PRs of 2026-07-11/12), and each cost a full deploy plus the N18 wipe-reseed. **Fix:** `ci.yml`'s **push** trigger gains a scoped `paths-ignore` — `docs/**`, root `*.md`, `.claude/**` — so a docs-only push to `main` starts no CI run; `deploy-staging.yml` fires only on a successful CI `workflow_run` from a push to `main`, so no CI run means no deploy, with zero new machinery in the deploy workflow. The **`pull_request` trigger stays unfiltered**: every PR, docs included, still runs the full gate before merge — what a docs-only merge skips is only the redundant post-merge re-run. Deliberately scoped, **not** a blanket `**/*.md`: `packages/help-content` ships Markdown into the app bundle (D111), so Markdown outside the three ignored paths still triggers CI and a deploy. Trades accepted (Forrest's call): a docs-only `main` commit carries no CI check of its own (the merged PR's green run is the evidence), and docs riding along on the *next* code merge deploy as usual. *Records in `ci.yml`'s trigger comment; builds on N18 (deploy = reseed), D111.*

*Later updated by: **D143** — the post-merge CI re-run this note is built around no longer exists (`ci.yml` has no `push` trigger). The docs-only skip itself survives with its outcome unchanged: the same `paths-ignore` list now sits on `deploy-staging.yml`'s own `push` trigger, so a docs-only merge still deploys nothing. The `pull_request`-stays-unfiltered rule is likewise unchanged, and is now the whole of the gate.*

### N83 — Name Search: fold the atomic Latin letters NFKD can't, and make the worker result a superset of the substring match (OFC-200; extends D35)

OFC-200: searching the Directory for "sor" returned an **empty** list while both "so" and "sore" matched many — including the intended hit, "Søren". Two independent, compounding causes:

1. **The diacritic fold was incomplete.** `normalizeToken` folded accents via Unicode `NFKD` + strip-combining-marks — which handles *decomposable* accents ("José" → `jose`, é = e + combining acute) but **not atomic Latin letters**: ø, æ, œ, ß, ł, ð, þ, ı are single indivisible code points with the diacritic baked in, so NFKD leaves them untouched. "Søren" tokenized to `søren`, so "sor" was not a clean substring, the fuzzy path scored the ø≠o miss at 1/3 ≈ 0.333 (just over Fuse's 0.30 threshold), and Beider-Morse didn't bridge it — he vanished. **Fix:** an explicit `ATOMIC_LATIN_FOLD` map (ø→o, æ→ae, œ→oe, ß→ss, ł→l, ð/đ→d, þ→th, …) applied after lowercasing, symmetrically to indexed names and queries. The highlighter already folds character-by-character through `normalizeToken` with an offset map, so length-changing folds (ß→ss) mark the original glyph correctly with no extra work.

2. **Fuse's error/length quantization is non-monotonic in query length.** A single edit costs `1/len`: it is tolerated at 4 chars (0.25 < 0.30) but not at 3 (0.333 > 0.30), so a 3-char query uniquely rejects near-misses that both shorter (substring) and longer (1-edit) queries accept — which is why the list emptied at exactly "sor". Rather than re-tune the deliberately A/B-chosen threshold (D66/N19) and trade precision (the fuzzy near-misses like "Wilsone" are best-effort noise), **`searchDetailed` now unions the deterministic substring match into its result** — guaranteeing the documented invariant that the worker's richer answer is always a **superset** of the instant main-thread substring set (D110). A hit the user already saw as they typed can no longer disappear when the worker answers; this also covers 1-char queries, which Fuse drops entirely (`minMatchCharLength: 2`) but the substring pass matches.

**Forrest's call (A + B, 2026-07-12):** fold + substring-superset, but **not** loosening Fuse for short queries (the fuzzy-noise inconsistency is acceptable; the exact/substring layer is now deterministic and monotonic, matching the user's "anything matching *sore* must also match *sor*" mental model). *Records to PRD §5.6.3 / D35; guarded by repro tests in `tokenize`, `index-build`, `highlight`.*

### N84 — The Directory's horizontal scrollbar is forced always-visible (classic, non-overlay) so it stays discoverable (OFC-205)

OFC-205: the Directory's horizontal scrollbar — present when the columns overflow the window — had become impossible to summon. It is **not a layout regression**: the scroll container clips and scrolls correctly (`overflow-x: auto`, content 1392px vs. a narrower viewport), unchanged since Phase 3a, and the app ships **zero** scrollbar CSS. The cause is the browser/OS default: **overlay scrollbars** (Windows 11's "Always show scrollbars" is off by default, and modern Chrome honors it with auto-hiding Fluent scrollbars), which fade out and are especially hard to reach horizontally with a mouse wheel — effectively invisible for the 60+ audience, and the reason it read as a regression with no app change. **Fix (Forrest's call, 2026-07-12):** an `.always-scrollbars` utility on the scroll panel. Defining `::-webkit-scrollbar` opts Chrome out of overlay into the legacy always-present scrollbar; `scrollbar-width`/`scrollbar-color` do the same for Firefox. The 14px track is generous on purpose; the thumb is `--muted-foreground` over the `--card` track (≥5.8:1 light, ≥7:1 dark — past the 3:1 WCAG 1.4.11 non-text floor) in both themes. Overlay-vs-classic rendering is a visual property headless Chromium doesn't reproduce, so the e2e guard locks the *substrate* (the panel overflows, owns the overflow rather than the page, and scrolls) and the visible-scrollbar outcome is live-confirmed. *Records to PRD §5.6 (Directory); CSS in `apps/web/src/index.css`, applied in `DirectoryGrid.tsx`.*

*Later updated by: N85 — live testing showed this diagnosis was wrong (or at most secondary): the real cause was the scroll container overrunning the viewport, so the horizontal scrollbar sat below the fold. The `.always-scrollbars` styling is kept as a complementary always-visible-scrollbar improvement, but N85 is the actual OFC-205 fix.*

### N85 — The Directory grid fills to the viewport bottom so its horizontal scrollbar is on-screen (OFC-205 follow-up; corrects N84's root cause)

Live testing after N84 shipped: the horizontal scrollbar was **still** missing, while the (now classic, always-visible) *vertical* scrollbar rendered fine. That combination disproved the overlay-scrollbar theory and revealed the real bug — a **layout** one N84 had explicitly ruled out. The horizontal scrollbar lives at the **bottom edge** of the scroll container, and the container was capped at a fixed `maxHeight: calc(100dvh − 13rem)`. That `13rem` was tuned in Phase 3a when little sat above the grid; the system banner (D117), the Filters panel (D38), and the manager/admin action bar (D41/D90) have since grown the chrome above the grid to ~28rem, so the container's bottom — and its scrollbar — was pushed **below the viewport fold**, unreachable. (Measured with a banner at 1200×900: container bottom y=961 vs. viewport 900 — 61px past the fold, page body overflowing.) The vertical scrollbar stayed usable because only its *top* need be visible; the horizontal one is entirely at the bottom.

**Fix (Forrest's call, 2026-07-12 — "measure & fill to viewport"):** a small `useLayoutEffect` in `DirectoryGrid` measures the grid's live top (`getBoundingClientRect().top`) and sets `max-height` to `innerHeight − top − 24px`, re-measuring on window `resize` and — via a `ResizeObserver` on `<body>` — whenever the chrome above changes height (banner appears, Filters expands). Recomputing from the grid's *top* (which the grid's own height never moves) keeps it idempotent, so no feedback loop. A fixed constant was rejected as a bandaid (it re-breaks whenever the chrome height changes); a shell-wide flex-fill refactor was rejected as too broad (it would change page-scroll/footer behavior for Profile/Admin/SignIn). The measured approach is correct for any chrome height and viewport without touching the shared shell. Consequence: the privacy footer now sits below the grid rather than after it — already effectively below the fold before this. *Records to PRD §5.6; `apps/web/src/pages/directory/DirectoryGrid.tsx`; supersedes N84's root-cause claim, keeps its `.always-scrollbars` styling.*

### D127 — The repository is licensed MIT (code only); the Phi Beta Epsilon names, marks, and brand-artwork files are reserved to Phi Beta Epsilon Corporation

The public repository gains a root `LICENSE` — the SPDX-canonical **MIT License**, kept verbatim so GitHub's license detector reports "MIT" — copyright **Forrest Thiessen**, and `package.json`'s `license` field changes from the intent-contradicting **`"UNLICENSED"`** (the npm "no rights granted" default that shipped with the scaffold) to **`"MIT"`**. A sibling `TRADEMARKS.md` and a README **License** section carve the brand out of the grant on two axes: (1) the **names and marks** — "Phi Beta Epsilon", "PBE", the crest, the triangle device, the gold leaf — are trademarks of **Phi Beta Epsilon Corporation** and are reserved; (2) the **brand-artwork asset files** (`apps/web/public/crest.svg` and the derived `favicon.ico` / `apple-touch-icon.png` / `icon-192.png` / `icon-512.png`, plus their generated `dist/` copies) are **all rights reserved — not covered by MIT**. `private: true` stays: it only bars an accidental `npm publish` of the workspace root and is orthogonal to the repo's license.

**Why:** the repo was already public with the stated intent that others may reuse the code, yet `"UNLICENSED"` granted nobody any rights — the exact opposite. Permissive-over-copyleft is Forrest's call: he wants maximal reuse freedom with attribution preserved, and nothing in the dependency tree (uniformly MIT/BSD/Apache) forces copyleft. MIT over Apache-2.0 for brevity and ubiquity; the one Apache feature that would matter here — its explicit "no trademark rights" clause — is reproduced by `TRADEMARKS.md`, and MIT, a *copyright* license, conveys no trademark rights regardless. The real exposure an unqualified MIT would create is **copyright in the artwork**: MIT covers *every file in the repo*, so as-written it would license the crest/triangle image files for free reuse — and that artwork's copyright belongs to the Corporation, not to Forrest to grant. Hence the explicit file-level carve-out, kept *out* of the verbatim `LICENSE` body (so detection stays clean) and placed in `TRADEMARKS.md`. Code license and trademark are distinct legal regimes; the docs keep them distinct. **(Forrest's call, 2026-07-12: MIT, permissive, copyright Forrest Thiessen; names, marks, and brand artwork reserved to Phi Beta Epsilon Corporation.)**

### D128 — `role` moves onto the `Profile`, read-public / write-protected; the change-role write re-paths to `PUT /api/profiles/{id}/role` (OFC-139 + OFC-199; reverses OFC-139's staff-only visibility, supersedes N50, amends N44/D51/D106)

A brother's Book `role` moves out of the private `users` collection and onto the `Profile` document, and its read visibility is **reversed to public**. Concretely: `Profile` gains `role`, classified **`public`** in `FIELD_VISIBILITY` (every authenticated brother sees anyone's role) and **`protected`** in `WRITE_RULE` (settable only by the change-role action, never via PATCH); `UserRecord` shrinks to `{ id, stars }`. The change-role write re-paths from `PUT /api/users/{id}/role` to **`PUT /api/profiles/{id}/role`** and becomes a protected-field profile write committed through `commitStatusWrite` (advancing the cache token in lock-step, exactly like mark-deceased / de-brother). `GET /api/users/{id}/role` is **removed**: the profile-page Role control reads the current role straight off the projected record it already holds (`record.role`). The **last-admin invariant** for both change-role and delete moves from a Firestore `users where role==admin` query to an in-memory `ProfileCache.adminCount()`. The caller's own role is snapshotted onto the session from the resolved profile at sign-in, not from `ensureUser`. The Directory gains an all-brothers **Staff** filter (Any / Managers and Administrators) and an optional, off-by-default **Role** column (any role; ordinary brothers render as an em-dash so the column reads as "who's staff").

`role` is stored **optionally**: a Firestore document that omits it is a `brother`, and the single Firestore→`Profile` hydration boundary (`normalizeHydratedProfile`) normalizes a missing *or unrecognized* value to `"brother"`, so every in-memory record carries a concrete role and no authorization path ever sees `undefined`. Because only brothers omit `role`, an "absent" role is unambiguous — a reader that ever forgot to normalize could only ever *under*-privilege (read a brother as a brother), never over-privilege; the design fails safe. This is what lets the eventual production data load write `role` only for the handful of non-brothers rather than stamping ~1,800 explicit `"brother"` fields.

**Why the visibility reversal (the crux).** OFC-139 recorded role as staff-only ("Forrest, confirmed"); the newer OFC-199 argued for all-brothers. **Forrest's call:** the staff roles — Manager and Administrator — are **official, not secret**. They are the people a brother contacts for help with Book, or to report that another brother is perpetually offline or has died; their names would have to be published somewhere on the site regardless, so there is no privacy to protect and making the field public actually eases those communication paths. Public read, with the write still locked to the dedicated action, gives "who is staff" to everyone while keeping "who may change a role" to admins. This **reverses OFC-139's staff-only decision**; OFC-139's stale "confirmed" text is corrected and the resolution is recorded on both tickets.

**Why role-on-profile.** A role is a property *of the brother* (like class year), not per-viewer state — only `stars` is genuinely per-viewer, so only `stars` stays in `users`. With `role` in the profile projection (public), the Directory filter and column are almost free, and the profile-page control reads the role it already holds — deleting the `GET …/role` round-trip that N50 added only because role wasn't on the profile.

**Why no migration script.** OFC-139 assumed an existing `users.role` to move, but there is nothing to migrate: **staging** wipe-reseeds on every deploy (N18), so updating the fake-data generator is the whole story there; **production** has never held role in Book at all — roles are assigned for the first time when Forrest's prepared spreadsheet loads into Firestore at cutover. That load writes `role` only for the sole initial admin (Forrest); every other brother is a `brother` by omission, and further managers/admins are granted by hand after launch. This requirement is captured for the forthcoming **CUTOVER-PLAN** document (OFC ticket filed), not PRE-LAUNCH-TOOLS.

**Why an in-memory count for the invariant (accepted trade-off).** The old `setRole` enforced the last-admin invariant inside a Firestore transaction. With role on the profile and the single authoritative in-memory instance (D83), the count is read from `ProfileCache.adminCount()` before the write — which regresses the strict transactional guarantee to the same narrow check-then-write race the **delete** path already documents and accepts as negligible (two admins acting on the last two within one event-loop await gap — a concurrent pair of demotions, or a demotion of one and a delete of the other, since both endpoints now read the same in-memory count). Given admin actions are rare and manual for a ~700-member directory with a handful of admins, and the model is single-instance, this is the pragmatic and consistent choice. **(Forrest's call, 2026-07-13.)**

**Why the simplified filter.** Rather than OFC-199's separate manager/admin options, the Staff filter is a single Any / "Managers and Administrators" toggle: with only ~6–8 staff, splitting them adds UI for no practical gain. **(Forrest's call, 2026-07-13.)**

*Supersedes N50 (the `GET …/role` endpoint and its premise); amends N44 (no create-if-absent for role — the profile always exists), D51/D106 (last-admin now cache-based), D19 (role now a public projected field). Records to DATABASE-SCHEMA §3.1/§6.1/§9, API-SPEC §5, ENGINEERING-DESIGN §2.1/§2.4, PRD §5.6, USER-MANUAL; guarded by the re-pathed admin route tests, the cache `adminCount`/role-normalization tests, and the shared visibility/capabilities table tests.*

*Later updated by: D129 — `adminCount()` counts only **usable** admins (living, non-de-brothered, with a usable email), not every profile holding the `admin` role; counting nominal-only admins was an org-lockout hole found in 5.5f live testing (OFC-241).*

### D129 — The last-admin invariant counts *usable* admins, not nominal ones (amends D128; OFC-241)

The last-admin invariant — which blocks the change-role and delete actions from removing the org's final administrator (D51/D106) — must count only **usable** admins: a brother who is `role === "admin"` **and can actually sign in and administer**. A shared predicate `isUsableAdmin(profile)` (`packages/shared/capabilities.ts`) defines this: role `admin`, **not deceased**, **not de-brothered** (sign-in is denied for a de-brothered member, D115), and **has a usable email** (`hasUsableEmail` — Book authenticates through the Ghost bridge, which resolves a member by email, so an email-less brother can never sign in; Book deliberately tolerates email-less brothers, ~1/3 of the roster). `ProfileCache.adminCount()` counts `isUsableAdmin`, and both guards key on `isUsableAdmin(stored)` for the target. `unlisted` is deliberately **not** disqualifying — an unlisted admin can still sign in and act.

**Why:** D128's `adminCount()` counted every profile with `role === "admin"`, including admins who hold the role but can never exercise it. This was a real org-lockout hole: the sole *usable* admin could demote (or delete) themselves while a *nominal-only* admin (deceased / email-less / de-brothered) silently satisfied the "one admin remains" check — leaving **zero usable admins** and no way to run backup/restore, add/delete, role changes, or Ghost sync. It surfaced in **5.5f live testing**: the staging fake data seeded a **deceased admin** (#5003, Budi Brownell), which the Directory hides by default, so the operator saw two admins, demoted the one visible other, then self-demoted — and the server, counting the hidden deceased admin, allowed it. The real-world path is identical and not hypothetical: an admin **dies** (is marked deceased) or a promoted admin **loses their email**, either leaving a nominal-only admin that the invariant must not count. Repro-test-first (a living admin plus deceased/email-less/de-brothered co-admins → the sole usable admin's self-demotion is now refused `409 last_admin`). **(Forrest's call, 2026-07-13: usable admin = living, not de-brothered, has a usable email; unlisted still counts.)**

*Amends D128 (the `adminCount()` definition). Records to ENGINEERING-DESIGN §2.4, API-SPEC §5, DATABASE-SCHEMA §6.1; guarded by the `isUsableAdmin` shared-table tests and the admin-route live-repro test.*

*Later updated by: D130 — the usable-admin invariant is enforced across **all five** removal/transition paths (adds mark-deceased, de-brother, PATCH email-clear to role/delete), plus a promote-guard and a gate role-downgrade re-check (OFC-239).*

### D130 — Enforce "the org always retains a usable admin" across *every* removal/transition path; a promote-guard; and a gate role-downgrade re-check (extends D129; OFC-241/OFC-239)

D129 fixed the *count* (usable admins only) but wired it into only two actions (role demotion, delete). Live testing (Forrest) showed the invariant must hold across **every** action that can drop the usable-admin count to zero. So:

1. **Uniform last-admin guard.** A shared `ProfileCache.isSoleUsableAdmin(profile)` (`isUsableAdmin && adminCount() === 1`) now gates **all five** paths that could remove the last usable admin — **role demotion** and **delete** (D129), plus **mark-deceased** (raise), **de-brother** (raise), and the **PATCH email-clear** (the resulting record's `next.email`). Each refuses with `409 last_admin`. Note mark-deceased is **manager-or-admin** tier, so without this a *manager* could lock the org out by marking the sole admin deceased.

2. **Promote-guard.** Promoting a brother who can't sign in — deceased, de-brothered, or with no usable email (`!isRoleEligible`) — to `admin` is rejected `422`: it would only mint a nominal, unusable admin. This stops dangling admin roles at the source. (Cleaning up an *existing* nominal admin — e.g. auto-demoting an admin the moment they're marked deceased or lose their email — is deferred to **OFC-242**, the D129/Q2 "auto-handle on transition" half.)

3. **Gate role-downgrade re-check (OFC-239).** The session snapshots the caller's real role at sign-in; the role-change route actively revokes on demotion (N53), but that revocation is best-effort. Now that `role` lives on the profile cache (D128), the session gate adds a **free per-request** comparison: if the caller's live cache role ranks **below** their snapshot (`isRoleDowngrade`), the session is stale — destroy it and `401` (force re-auth at the new role). Only a downgrade is caught; an upgrade merely under-privileges the stale session, harmlessly. This is the defense-in-depth backstop to active revocation, exactly as the gate's present-and-de-brothered check backs the de-brother route.

**Why:** the last-admin invariant protects a *property of the org* ("someone can always administer"), so it has to be enforced wherever that property could be violated — not just on the two actions that first motivated it. Enforcing it on only role/delete left mark-deceased, de-brother, and email-removal as open lockout paths (and a manager-reachable one at that). The promote-guard and the gate re-check close the two adjacent holes the same session surfaced: creating unusable admins, and a demotion failing to take effect on a live session. **(Forrest's call, 2026-07-13.)**

*Extends D129 (same `isUsableAdmin`/`adminCount` machinery). Records to API-SPEC §3/§5 (409 last_admin on deceased/debrothered/patch; 422 promote-guard), ENGINEERING-DESIGN §2.3 (gate role-downgrade). Guarded by repro tests on each of the five paths, the promote-guard, and the gate downgrade/upgrade cases; OFC-239 closed by this, OFC-242 carries the auto-demote follow-up.*

*Later updated by: N86 — the promote-guard covers **any** staff role (manager too, not just admin), and the last-admin/promote refusals are now surfaced in the mark-deceased/de-brother/role UIs (they were silently swallowed).*

### N86 — 5.5f live-test remediation of D130: the promote-guard covers *any* staff role, and the last-admin/promote refusals are surfaced in the UI

Two fixes from Forrest's re-test of the D130 guards, both merged as a follow-up:

1. **Promote-guard now covers manager too, not just admin.** D130 scoped it to `role === "admin"`; a **manager** who can't sign in (deceased / de-brothered / emailless) is equally useless, so the guard is now `role !== "brother" && !isRoleEligible` — promoting an ineligible brother to **any** staff role is rejected `422`. (You can always still demote them to `brother`.)

2. **The refusals now show in the UI.** The server was correctly refusing (`409 last_admin` on mark-deceased / de-brother / PATCH-email; `422` promote-guard), but three client controls **silently swallowed** it: `putDeceased`/`putDebrothered`/`changeRole` (api.ts) mapped only success/validation/ghost outcomes, so a `409`/`422` fell through to `throw`, which the control's handler didn't catch — the `await` rejected mid-handler and the confirm dialog just sat there ("nothing happens", not even a close). Fixed by mapping `409 → { status: "last_admin" }` and the promote `422 → { status: "ineligible", message }` (server message passed through) as **data**, and surfacing each: the mark-deceased dialog shows the error inline and **stays open**; de-brother shows it below the button; the Role control shows it as its status message. (Delete already did this — hence it was the one that worked in the first live test.) Guarded by e2e tests that mock the refusal and assert the message.

*Extends D130. Records to API-SPEC §5 (422 promote-guard covers manager). (Forrest's live-test call, 2026-07-13.)*

### N87 — Bump all GitHub Actions pins to their latest Node-24 majors (OFC-62)

GitHub runners are retiring the Node 20 action runtime, so every CI/deploy run annotated "Node.js 20 is deprecated … forced to run on Node.js 24." Bumped every action `uses:` pin to the current major whose runtime is Node 24: `actions/checkout@v4→v7`, `actions/setup-node@v4→v7`, `actions/setup-java@v4→v5`, `actions/upload-artifact@v4→v7` (ci.yml); `actions/checkout@v4→v7`, `actions/setup-node@v4→v7` (both build- and Firebase-CLI steps), `google-github-actions/auth@v2→v3`, `google-github-actions/setup-gcloud@v2→v3` (deploy-staging.yml). Latest majors verified live against each repo's release API on 2026-07-14; the only breaking changes across the crossed majors are the Node-24 runtime bump (runner ≥ 2.327.1, satisfied on `ubuntu-latest`) and ESM migration — none touch the inputs we use. `auth@v3` additionally removed the `retries`/`backoff`/`backoff_limit` inputs (unused here); `project_id`/`workload_identity_provider`/`service_account` are unchanged.

**Load-bearing distinction (do not "fix"):** the Firebase-CLI deploy step now uses `actions/setup-node@v7` (the action's own Node-24 runtime) but keeps `node-version: "20"` (the Node it *installs* for the CLI run) — these are orthogonal. The `20` is the deliberate pin that dodges the google-auth-library/undici STS "Premature close" bug (infra/README.md); the action-pin bump does not disturb it.

**Why:** pre-emptive maintenance — the forced-to-Node-24 shim will eventually stop, and clearing the annotation keeps the "new problem in this run" signal trustworthy. Kept the repo's existing floating-major pin convention (`@v7`, not a pinned SHA) rather than switching to SHA-pinning, which is a separate supply-chain-hardening decision not in scope here.

*Records to `.github/workflows/ci.yml`, `.github/workflows/deploy-staging.yml`. Verified by a green CI run and a green staging deploy with no Node-20 annotation (OFC-62 acceptance criteria).*

### N88 — Triage the CodeQL alerts on `main`: three fixes, five dismiss-with-reason (OFC-152)

The repo runs CodeQL (GitHub default setup — no committed workflow), but its alerts had never been triaged; an unreviewed alert queue erodes the "new alert in this PR" signal. The ticket named six alerts open on 2026-07-04, but two more had accrued by the time this landed (**8 total**) — the newer ones are triaged the same way. Resolved all eight — three fixed in code, five dismissed with a documented reason:

**Fixed**

1. **`js/polynomial-redos` (high) — `packages/shared/validation.ts` `EMAIL_RE`.** The email regex `/^[^\s@]+@[^\s@]+\.[^\s@]+$/u` is ambiguous — `[^\s@]` also matches `.`, so `[^\s@]+\.[^\s@]+` backtracks quadratically on a long input whose tail defeats the anchoring `$`. The reachable vector is a `@`-terminated string (`a@` + `x.`×N + `@`): `isValidEmail` trims first, so a *trailing space* is stripped and harmless, but a trailing `@` survives and drives the blowup — **measured 4.7 s on one ~160 KB `email`/`alternateEmail` PATCH value**, which stalls the single Cloud Run instance (D83) for every other caller. **Fix:** a `MAX_EMAIL_LENGTH = 254` guard (RFC 5321 §4.5.3.1.3, the real address cap) *before* the regex — semantically correct (a longer string is not a valid address) and it bounds the regex to constant work. Zero change to the accept-set for valid-length addresses. Repro-first: a timing regression test on the `@`-terminated input (result unchanged either way — rejection — so timing is what proves it, and it uniquely catches a length-check-after-regex ordering regression) plus a 255-vs-254 boundary test that pins the guard against removal. `MAX_EMAIL_LENGTH` is exported and now caps the two web email inputs' `maxLength` off the one authoritative value (the review-finding consistency fix, matching the `MAX_LINKS` pattern).

2. **`actions/missing-workflow-permissions` (medium) — `.github/workflows/ci.yml`.** The `verify` job declared no `permissions:` and inherited the workflow default token scope. Added `permissions: { contents: read }` (least privilege — the gate only reads the repo).

3. **`js/incomplete-sanitization` (high) — `apps/web/src/pages/admin/ghostAuditFormat.ts` `cell()`.** The Ghost-audit Markdown-table escaper escaped pipes (`|` → `\|`) but never escaped **backslashes first**, so a value containing `\|` rendered as an escaped-backslash + a *live* pipe and broke the table row (and a bare `\b` silently vanished as a Markdown escape). Reachable via Ghost member names/emails (some self-signup) surfaced in the admin-downloaded `.md`. **Fix:** escape `\`→`\\` before `|`→`\|`, and flatten a lone CR too (`[\r\n]+`); repro test on `\|` and a bare backslash. (Not in the ticket's original six — accrued 2026-07-09 from the 5b-2 audit-formatter work; a real defect, so fixed, not dismissed.)

**Dismissed (won't-fix, reason recorded)**

4. **`actions/untrusted-checkout` (critical) — `deploy-staging.yml`.** The privileged deploy job (WIF `id-token: write`) checks out `workflow_run.head_sha`, but its **job-level `if` gates on `workflow_run.head_branch == 'main' && workflow_run.event == 'push'`**, and a public-fork PR is a `pull_request` event that can never push to `main` — so fork code never runs with deploy credentials. The whole job is gated (nothing runs before the `if`). Dismissed **won't-fix / mitigated**.

5. **`js/insufficient-key-size` (high) — `ghost-provider.test.ts`.** A **test** deliberately generates a 1024-bit RSA key to reproduce Ghost's real 1024-bit member-JWT key (the regression that motivated verifying via Node `crypto`, not jose — N54). Not production key material. Dismissed **used-in-tests / by-design**.

6–8. **`js/missing-rate-limiting` (high) ×3 — `headshot.ts` PUT and DELETE, and `admin.ts` `PUT …/role`.** All three routes carry `config: writeRateLimit()`; CodeQL doesn't model `@fastify/rate-limit`'s per-route `config`, so it reads them as unprotected. Dismissed **false-positive**. (The role-route one accrued 2026-07-13 from the 5.5f role work — same pattern.)

**Why:** an alert queue is only useful if it's clean — a triaged baseline makes the next genuinely-new finding trustworthy. Fixed the three real (if low-severity) issues and recorded the reasoning for the five non-issues so a future session seeing a dismissed alert understands the call rather than re-litigating it. **CodeQL is now promoted to a required status check** on `main` so the clean baseline is enforced going forward (Forrest's call, 2026-07-14). Eight alerts open → **0 open**.

*Records to `packages/shared/validation.ts` (+ `validation.test.ts`, `index.ts`), `apps/web/src/pages/admin/ghostAuditFormat.ts` (+ test), `apps/web/src/pages/profile/{fields,ProfileEdit}.tsx`, `.github/workflows/ci.yml`; dismissals recorded in the repo's code-scanning UI with these reasons. Guarded by the new email + escaper tests and the green CI/CodeQL gate.*

*Later updated by: the "promoted to a required status check" line got ahead of reality — `main` had **no branch protection at all**, so making CodeQL required means **creating** a protection ruleset from scratch (a policy decision: require PRs? require the Verify gate too? strict / admin-enforcement?). Deferred to **OFC-246** (Forrest's call). Also, the untrusted-checkout critical **re-raises under a new alert number** whenever the flagged `deploy-staging.yml` checkout line changes — it did (#1 → #19 after the N87 pin bump); re-dismiss with the same mitigation. Both still net to 0 open. **Now resolved — see N91**: branch protection was created on `main` 2026-07-14, with CodeQL and the Verify gate as required status checks (OFC-246).*

*Later updated by: **D143** — item 4's untrusted-checkout dismissal reasons from the deploy job's job-level `if` (gating on `workflow_run.head_branch == 'main' && …event == 'push'`). That guard, and the `workflow_run` trigger it interrogated, are **both gone**: `deploy-staging.yml` now triggers on `push: branches:[main]` and its checkout takes **no `ref:` at all**. The mitigation is therefore *stronger* than the one recorded — there is no longer an attacker-influencable ref being checked out, and a fork still cannot push to `main` — but the recorded rationale no longer describes the code. ⚠ If the alert re-raises under a new number, dismiss it on the **new** basis, not by copying the old wording.*

### N89 — Accept the `@opentelemetry/core` advisory as a documented dev-only residual (OFC-234)

`npm audit` reports a **moderate, dev-only** advisory — **GHSA-8988-4f7v-96qf** (`@opentelemetry/core` < 2.8.0, unbounded memory in W3C Baggage propagation), reached via `firebase-tools → @google-cloud/pubsub@5.3.1 → @opentelemetry/core@1.30.1` (three findings for the one package + two dependents). **Accepted as a residual, not fixed**, on this evidence gathered 2026-07-14:

- **Not runtime-reachable.** `firebase-tools` is a root **devDependency** (emulators, deploy CLI); it is not in the `apps/api` or `apps/web` bundles. The vulnerable code runs only on the developer's / CI machine, never in the deployed service. Correspondingly, GitHub Dependabot did **not** raise it (only the uuid alert #7 was, N74).
- **No clean upstream fix.** `firebase-tools@latest` (15.23.0) **is already the installed version** and still resolves `@opentelemetry/core@1.30.1` via `pubsub@5.3.1` — upstream has not moved off the 1.x line.
- **An `overrides` pin to `^2.8.0` is unsafe here.** `pubsub@5.3.1` declares `@opentelemetry/core: ^1.30.1`; forcing the 2.x **major** would violate that range and risk breaking the Firebase CLI (emulators/deploy) at runtime — not worth it for a dev-only baggage-propagation advisory. `npm audit fix --force` "resolves" it only by **downgrading** `firebase-tools` 15 → 14 (a breaking major downgrade), also rejected.

**Why:** the fix carries more risk (a broken dev/deploy CLI) than the advisory carries exposure (dev-only, not runtime-reachable, not Dependabot-flagged). Re-evaluate when `firebase-tools`/`pubsub` move onto `@opentelemetry/core` ≥ 2.8; the override becomes safe then. **(Forrest's call, 2026-07-14.)**

*Records to `docs/initial-build/DECISIONS.md` only (no code change). Sibling of N88 (same security-hygiene batch, 5.5g). Ref N74's closing paragraph.*

### N90 — Staging reseed wipes `users` (stars) too, for a deterministic deploy; column prefs are a documented localStorage residual (OFC-197)

Staging is meant to land in a known, repeatable configuration on every deploy — its data a pure function of the deployed code (N18). But the reseed wiped only `profiles`, not the private `users` collection, so **stars** (per-viewer, `users/{id}.stars`, DATABASE-SCHEMA §6.1) survived across deploys and could skew test state (a brother starred under an earlier deploy stayed starred). **Fixed:** `seed-staging.ts` now wipes **both** `profiles` and `users` via a shared batched `wipeCollection` helper; `users` is recreated lazily, empty, on the tester's next sign-in / first star. Gated by the same `STAGING_AUTOSEED` toggle, so Phase-8 UAT (autoseed off) still preserves in-progress tester state.

**Column preferences are a documented residual, not fixed (Option A — Forrest's call, 2026-07-14).** The column lens (visible columns, order, widths — D30/N15) persists in the **browser's localStorage** (`pbe.book.directory.columns.v1`), which no server-side reseed can reach, and a force-reload does *not* clear it. Rather than a build-flag hack to namespace/auto-reset the key — which would also wipe every real brother's saved columns on each production release (user-hostile) — the guidance is: reset columns **in-app** via the column picker's "Reset to default columns" (`ColumnPicker.tsx`, `lens.reset()`), or clear site data. The server-side stars wipe removes the part that could actually skew test *data*; columns are display-only.

**Why:** "staging = a pure function of the deploy" must cover per-viewer state, not just profiles, or a test can be misled by stale stars. localStorage is genuinely unreachable from a deploy, so the honest split is a server-side fix for stars + a documented manual reset for columns — not a client hack that would degrade production to serve a staging convenience.
