*Records to `tools/fake-data/src/seed-staging.ts`, `CLAUDE.md` (staging landmine). Verified by the next staging deploy resetting the tester's stars (live-test).*

### N91 — Branch protection created on `main`; CodeQL + Verify gate required, PRs required, admin bypass allowed (OFC-246)

`main` had **no branch protection at all** (`GET …/branches/main/protection` → 404); the repo had been relying solely on the `workflow_run` deploy gate (deploy fires only on a green CI for a push to `main`). N88's "CodeQL is now a required status check" line got ahead of that reality, so OFC-246 split the policy decision off from the N88 triage. This note records the policy Forrest chose and the ruleset created.

**Policy (Forrest's call, 2026-07-14):**

- **Require a pull request before merging** to `main`, with **0 required approvals** — solo repo, so the PR-and-checks flow *is* the discipline, not a second reviewer.
- **Required status checks, `strict` (branch must be up to date before merge):** the **Verify gate** (CI) and **CodeQL**. The exact contexts were taken from what actually reports-and-completes on a PR head — a docs-only PR was used as the probe first, so we never require a check that doesn't run on a given PR and silently deadlocks the merge. `Deploy to staging` is deliberately **not** required: it runs post-merge on the `main` push and never reports on a PR.
- **Force-pushes and branch deletion disabled** on `main`.
- **Admin bypass allowed** (`enforce_admins: false`): the PR-and-checks path is the default (a direct push must be *deliberately* bypassed), but the sole maintainer keeps an escape hatch if a required check ever hangs. The stricter `enforce_admins: true` was rejected as able to wedge a solo operator with no second admin to unblock them.

**Why:** mechanically enforce the "never commit directly to `main`" gate and the clean-CodeQL-baseline goal N88 aimed at, without the deadlock and lock-out failure modes a naive "make CodeQL required" would carry. Branch protection is a GitHub-config action (not a git push), run under Forrest's explicit authorization this session (per the "config changes affecting merges are Forrest's" landmine).

*Records to `docs/initial-build/DECISIONS.md` (this note) + `DECISIONS-INDEX.md`; the ruleset itself lives in GitHub branch-protection config, not a file in-tree. Resolves the N88 forward-trailer and OFC-246. Verified by `GET …/branches/main/protection` returning the configured ruleset.*

*Later updated by: **D141** — the required checks now attest the full verification gate (`assert:gate-in-sync`), activating tiered Gate 4 merge-on-green; the admin-bypass question is re-raised (not overridden) there, tracked on OFC-297.*

### D131 — Font-size + theme toggles moved from the inline masthead into the avatar menu; PBE News top-bar link restored (OFC-210, OFC-243)

The masthead packed two 3-button segmented pills (font size, theme) plus Report-a-bug, the role badge, and the avatar into the right of the bar. On a phone the cluster overflowed the viewport — the font-size pill overlapped the wordmark, the avatar was clipped, and the name was pushed off-screen (OFC-210). Restoring the always-specified **PBE News** top-bar link (ASSETS.md — the single sibling-newsletter entry point, silently dropped in the build: OFC-243) would only have made a full bar worse.

**Decision (Forrest's call, 2026-07-14):** relocate the font-size and theme toggles out of the inline bar and **into the avatar menu, on every screen** — not a mobile-only branch. They are set-once display preferences that belong in a menu, and pulling them out leaves a simpler, calmer masthead at all widths. The inline bar becomes `crest + wordmark · PBE News · Report a bug · role badge · avatar menu`. The wordmark link gains `min-w-0` + `truncate` and the control cluster `shrink-0`, so under width pressure the wordmark shortens ("PBE Address…") instead of shoving controls off the edge — the structural fix for the cutoff. PBE News opens `pbe400.org` in a new tab (`rel="noopener noreferrer"`, an external-link glyph, an "opens in a new tab" accessible name).

**Why:** one change fixes both the overflow (fewer, narrower inline elements plus a yielding wordmark) and the visual clutter, and does it uniformly rather than forking mobile vs. desktop layout. The toggles keep working from inside the native `<details>` menu — the auto-close ignores clicks within it (`useDetailsAutoClose`), so adjusting size/theme doesn't dismiss the menu. This diverges from the delivered visual-design shell (toggles inline in the top bar); the divergence is deliberate and recorded here as the authoritative source. Amends **N24** (masthead font-size control is now menu-resident).

*Records to `apps/web/src/components/AppShell.tsx` + `DECISIONS-INDEX.md` (UI shell) + `USER-MANUAL.md` §9. Verified by the browser check at 360/390/412/768/1280px (no cutoff; toggles operable from the menu) and the a11y pass.*

### N92 — Mobile "Options" fold: the Directory chrome collapses on a phone (OFC-211)

On a phone the Directory's chrome — Name Search, the Starred-only / Include-deceased toggles, the column picker, the filter panel, and the staff action bar — stacked vertically and consumed more than half the screen before a single brother row appeared (OFC-211).

**Decision (Forrest's call, 2026-07-14):** below the `md` breakpoint (`min-width: 768px`, the same line that already switches the grid to cards), keep the Directory heading, result count, and **Name Search** always visible, and fold everything else — the two view toggles, the column picker, the `FilterPanel`, and the staff `ActionBar` — into a single **"Options"** disclosure, **closed by default** on every mount. (Labelled **"Options"**, not "Filters & options": live-testing found that the longer label read as a promise of filter fields directly inside, when in fact the nested `FilterPanel` keeps its own "Filters" toggle — two filter-named disclosures confused the reader.) Desktop is unchanged: at `md`+ the toggles and column picker sit beside the search and the filter panel + action bar render inline, exactly as before.

Built as a `<button aria-expanded>` + conditionally-rendered region (mirroring the `FilterPanel` disclosure, D38) rather than a native `<details>` — for a state-driven chevron and to sidestep a nested-`group` collision with the ColumnPicker's own `group` chevron. The open state is **not persisted**, like the FilterPanel (the Directory remounts on a Back-navigation, so always-closed is the consistent return state); a summary badge counts the active folded options (typed filters + the two view toggles) so an applied narrowing is visible while the fold is closed. The reusable chrome elements are built once in `Directory` and placed in whichever width-branch renders, so filters/columns/export keep a single source of behaviour across both widths.

**Why:** the ticket's goal is reclaiming vertical space for the actual data on a phone without disturbing the desktop layout. Keeping search always-visible — rather than folding it too (the ticket's literal suggestion) — preserves the primary tool one glance away while still collapsing the four bulky control blocks into one bar (Forrest's call among the fold-scope options).

*Records to `apps/web/src/pages/Directory.tsx` + `DECISIONS-INDEX.md` (Directory behavior) + `e2e/directory.spec.ts` (mobile-fold coverage). Verified by the new mobile-viewport e2e (fold closed by default, search visible, opening reveals the controls, badge counts) + the a11y gate.*

### N93 — Icon-only masthead controls keep their label in the a11y tree on mobile (`sr-only`, not `hidden`) — fixes a WCAG 4.1.2 gap surfaced by OFC-211's mobile axe pass

Adding the first mobile-viewport axe pass (the OFC-211 fold test at 390px) surfaced two pre-existing **WCAG 4.1.2** violations no desktop axe test could catch: below `sm`, the **Report a bug** button collapses to its icon and the **avatar menu `<summary>`** collapses to just the avatar, and both labelled their text with `hidden sm:inline` — which removes the text from the accessibility tree, leaving the control with **no discernible name** on a phone.

**Fix:** the responsive label now uses `sr-only sm:not-sr-only` instead of `hidden sm:inline` — visually identical (collapsed on a phone, a visible inline label from `sm` up) but the text stays in the accessibility tree at every width, so the button/summary always has a name.

**Why / landmine:** `hidden` (`display:none`) drops content from *both* the visual and the accessibility tree; `sr-only` hides it visually while keeping it for assistive tech. Any control that becomes icon-only on a phone and whose only label is a text span must use `sr-only`, not `hidden`, or it fails 4.1.2 on the phones most of Book's audience uses. Guarded by the mobile-viewport axe pass added with N92.

*Records to `apps/web/src/components/AppShell.tsx` + `ReportBug.tsx`. Found and fixed while building OFC-211 (PR stacked on the masthead PR); verified by the mobile-fold axe e2e.*

### N94 — The masthead PBE News link is environment-specific (build-time `BOOK_PBE_NEWS_URL`); warning-banner rule given real contrast (OFC-243 / OFC-240 live-test)

Live-testing the OFC-243 link found it hardcoded to production `pbe400.org` — so on staging it jumped to the live newsletter instead of ghost-staging. The masthead link must point at the PBE News site **for the environment the SPA was built for**.

**Fix (mirrors the `BOOK_APP_VERSION` build-stamp pattern):** `vite.config` reads `process.env.BOOK_PBE_NEWS_URL` and injects it via `define` as `__PBE_NEWS_URL__`; `apps/web/src/lib/externalLinks.ts` exposes it with a guarded fallback (→ `pbe400.org` for dev / tests, where the global is undefined). The value **defaults to production**, and each environment's deploy overrides it: `infra/environments/staging.env` sets `BOOK_PBE_NEWS_URL=https://staging.pbe400.org`, which the deploy workflow appends to `$GITHUB_ENV` before the SPA build (so `process.env` carries it). A future `prod.env` sets the pbe400.org value (or omits it — the default is already prod), so a prod build can never accidentally link to staging.

**Also (OFC-240 live-test):** the first warning-banner hairline was too close in colour to the saturated red fill to be seen; `--destructive-border` moved to a distinctly darker red (`#6a0f07` light / `#7d271e` dark) for real contrast against the fill.

**Why:** an environment-specific external URL belongs in the same per-environment build config as the other staging/prod values (the `*.env` files, OFC-84), defaulting to the safe production value — not hardcoded in a component. And a rule you can't see isn't a rule: the warning banner's frame has to read against its own fill.

*Records to `apps/web/vite.config.ts`, `apps/web/src/lib/externalLinks.ts`, `apps/web/src/components/AppShell.tsx`, `apps/web/src/vite-env.d.ts`, `infra/environments/staging.env`, and the `--destructive-border` tokens (both copies). Live-test remediation of the 5.5h batch; verified on staging.*

## UAT restructure (2026-07-14, the Phase 7.7 planning session)

### D132 — UAT becomes its own Phase 7.7, run on staging in a frozen-autoseed window, with real-named testers on fake data; a small Phase 7.6 carries the Ghost↔Book theme integration (resolves N64's deferred fork; supersedes §9's UAT placement; plan: `UAT-PLAN.md`; Forrest's calls throughout)

UAT was originally a Phase-8 activity with its platform deliberately undecided (N64). This session restructured it; the full plan is **`UAT-PLAN.md`**, and a stub **`CUTOVER-PLAN.md`** was created as the recorded home for cutover-scope items discovered early. The decisions and their reasoning:

- **UAT is pulled out of Phase 8 into a new Phase 7.7**, strictly after Phases 6/7/7.5 (help must exist to be tested, hardening precedes a 15-person cohort, 7.5's byte-efficiency serves exactly this audience). **Why:** feedback and bugs from real users are incorporated *before* final launch prep begins, instead of mid-cutover-cluster; Phase 8 becomes purely migration + cutover.
- **Platform: staging — N64's option (a), refined.** The fork's framing missed that *code* deploys and *data* reseeds are separable steps: with `STAGING_AUTOSEED=false` for the UAT window, merges still auto-deploy code (testers see fixes immediately — remediation runs concurrently with testing) while tester accounts, edits, role upgrades, and photos survive every deploy. Deploys are therefore **not** frozen — only the data layer is. A manual full reseed (fakes → Ghost mirror → tester roster → photo corpus) stays available and reproduces complete UAT state; a mid-window reseed wiping testers' in-progress edits is an accepted cost. Post-UAT, autoseed returns and the roster keeps running inside the reseed step, giving selected brothers **standing staging access** deterministically recreated on every deploy.
- **Testers are provisioned under their real names and emails** (the one real datum in an otherwise fake environment). **Why:** a tester recognizes his own account, and bug reports arrive attributed to a real name (the `submitterName` snapshot) instead of a fake identity to look up. Cohort: ~30 brothers invited (the specific groups deliberately not named in this public repo), 10–15 expected; volunteers only. No signed releases — the invitation notifies testers their names/emails are visible to the other testers (Forrest's call).
- **The roster lives as a private GCS object in `pbe-book-staging`** (CSV: profileId, name, classYear, email, role). **Why not the repo:** it is public and the roster is real PII. **Why GCS over a GitHub secret or local-only file:** the deploy workflow already authenticates to the project via WIF (no new secrets), it's editable with one `gsutil cp`, and the same object serves CI and local runs. A new `seed:staging-testers` tool (OFC-248) generalizes and subsumes the single-tester `STAGING_TESTER_EMAIL`/`link:staging-tester` mechanism, and also delta-reconciles the testers' Ghost-staging members so the real bridge and the Ghost-first write path both work.
- **Tester profiles are blanked beyond identity** (name/classYear/email/role kept; address, professional, links, big brother, etc. cleared). **Why:** "fill in your profile" becomes the first UAT task — account setup doubles as end-to-end coverage of the edit path, the highest-value flow to watch real users attempt.
- **~200 realistic AI-generated fake headshots** (Forrest-supplied, 1024² PNG) seed the directory for UAT from a private GCS fixture prefix, encoded through the same sharp pipeline as real uploads (OFC-249). **Why:** testers should see a directory that looks alive, not eight recycled placeholders; 1024² downscales cleanly to the 512²/96² derivatives.
- **UAT must exercise the real magic-link sign-in — the DevIdentityProvider bypass was rejected for testers.** **Why:** the email flow is precisely where the 60+ audience will stumble at launch; testing around it would skip the riskiest UX in the system. This makes outbound email from Ghost-staging a hard prerequisite (Mailgun sandbox caps at ~5 authorized recipients): Forrest owns the fix (baseline: a short-term paid Mailgun account for 30–40 recipients; alternatives under investigation) — OFC-252, a della2/Ghost-side change outside this repo.
- **Roles:** testers start as **brother** (what nearly all real users will be); filing a bug report through the in-app control earns a **manager** upgrade (a normal admin role change + a roster edit so it survives reseeds). **Why:** an incentive that both drives use of the bug-report path and recruits testers for the manager-layer features.
- **A new Phase 7.6 (Ghost↔Book theme integration)** precedes UAT: the `pbe-news-ghost-theme` account-management links repoint to Book and light article↔Book test content lands on Ghost-staging (OFC-250/OFC-251), deployed to Ghost-staging only — `pbe400.org` stays on the pre-Book theme until cutover, making the theme diff a cutover artifact. **Why its own phase:** different repo, its own manual deploy motion, and zero dependency on Phases 6/7/7.5, so it can run early in parallel.
- **Out of scope, parked in the `CUTOVER-PLAN.md` stub:** the manual production deploy workflow (OFC-253) and everything else cutover — nothing in UAT needs a production environment to exist.

Records to `UAT-PLAN.md` (new), `CUTOVER-PLAN.md` (new stub), `CODING-PROJECT-PLAN.md` §7/§8/§9, and the N64 trailer. Tickets: OFC-248–OFC-253.

## Backlog triage & scheduling (2026-07-14, the ticket-scheduling session)

### D133 — A Ghost-less brother who gains an email gets his Ghost member auto-created on that PATCH: the email↔Ghost-record invariant (Forrest's call; the OFC-232 pre-session ruling)

OFC-232's open design fork — auto-create the Ghost member on the PATCH that first adds an email to a Ghost-less brother, vs. an explicit "Enable sign-in / add to PBE News" affordance — is ruled **auto-create on the PATCH**.

**Why:** Forrest holds a standing invariant that **a Book record with an email always has a corresponding Ghost record, and vice versa — never a lingering email-but-Ghost-less state.** An explicit affordance permits exactly that state (an admin adds the email but never clicks the second control); the automatic trigger makes the invariant structural. The legibility/typo argument for the explicit affordance loses to the invariant: a mistyped email is corrected by a follow-up edit (the ordinary Ghost-first-gated update path), whereas a silently missing Ghost record is invisible until a brother can't sign in.

The edge cases stay with the 5.5i session's design pass, resolved *under the invariant*: **deceased** (D80) and **de-brothered** (D115) brothers are excluded from auto-create; an email added and removed in the same edit nets no creation; an email colliding with an existing Ghost member resolves via the D20 unidentified-address handling (link vs. reject — settle in-session); creation honors `allowNewsletterEmail` at that moment, uses `send_email=false`, and follows the Ghost-first-gated write ordering (D98).

*Records to OFC-232 and `CODING-PROJECT-PLAN.md` §Phase 5.5 (session 5.5i). Implementation lands in 5.5i, which appends its own N-entry.*

### N95 — Second Todo-backlog triage: sessions 5.5i–5.5l appended; the remaining backlog scheduled onto Phases 6–8 by Linear label

With 5.5a–5.5h all closed, Forrest promoted the surviving backlog to Todo under a pre-launch tech-debt discipline — *"if something will ever be worth fixing, we should do it now"* — and this session scheduled all 23 open Todo tickets (22 PBE-Book + OFC-191 from PBE-Ghost). Nothing was cancelled; three tickets were deliberately *sequenced* rather than deferred (see 7.5 below). The placements:

- **New 5.5 batches** (same code-locality discipline as N59): **5.5i** OFC-232 + OFC-231 (`apps/api/src/identity/`; pre-session ruling D133), **5.5j** OFC-236 + OFC-153 (the SPA 401-recovery seam; Opus-class, elevated effort), **5.5k** OFC-235 + OFC-64 + OFC-120 (small client-side polish), **5.5l** OFC-217 (Ghost 6.0 breaking-change investigation; findings only). **Order: 5.5k → 5.5l → 5.5i → 5.5j** (quick wins first — Forrest's call).
- **Phase 6:** OFC-244 (About page — user-guidance surface, authored alongside the manual; Forrest's call over batching it into 5.5k).
- **Phase 7:** OFC-212 + OFC-209 → session 7b (ops); OFC-228 → 7c (test infrastructure; splits off as 7d if 7c runs long).
- **Phase 7.5:** OFC-179 (*is* the unified store), OFC-68, OFC-119 — sequenced here because both build derived structures on the unified store; building them earlier would be re-done. OFC-179 is blocked-by OFC-212 (the plan's stated precondition, now a Linear relation).
- **Phase 7.6:** OFC-191 joins OFC-250/OFC-251 (same repo, same staging-only deploy, same cutover theme-diff artifact).
- **Phase 7.7 / 8:** unchanged (OFC-248/249/252; OFC-229/253) — already placed by D132.

**Linear conventions set here:** phase/session labels (`5.5i`–`5.5l`, `6`, `7b`, `7c`, `7.5`, `8`, joining the existing `7.6`/`7.7`) are the session index — one label pulls up a session's tickets; each scheduled ticket carries a triage comment with the reasoning; the served-purpose `5.5a`–`5.5h` labels were stripped from their (all-closed) tickets and retired.

*Records to `CODING-PROJECT-PLAN.md` (§Phase 5.5 batches 5.5i–5.5l, §Phase 6, §Phase 7 sessions, §Phase 7.5, §Phase 7.6, the phase-summary table) and the Linear tickets named above.*

### D134 — Marking a brother deceased deletes his Ghost member (and un-marking re-creates it); the email↔Ghost invariant extends to the deceased state (Forrest's call; amends D80, extends D133)

D80 made mark-deceased force `allowNewsletterEmail` off and push that unsubscribe to Ghost, leaving the Ghost **member** in place. Under D133's email↔Ghost-record invariant a deceased brother should have **no Ghost member at all** — the same posture de-brothering already takes (D115). So mark-deceased now **deletes the Ghost member** (Ghost-first, like the de-brother raise) and drops the `ghostMemberId`; un-marking **re-creates** it when the brother is once again Ghost-eligible (living + not-de-brothered + usable email), folding in the fresh id and creating the member with the brother's **restored** newsletter consent so Ghost and Book agree from the first moment.

**Why:** with the member merely unsubscribed (D80's old behavior), every brother who died holding an email would sit as permanent `missingGhostMember`/newsletter drift the audit flags forever, and each death would generate a manual Ghost chore. Deleting the member makes the invariant structural instead of an audit nag — routine deaths need no Ghost surgery — and it removes the deceased brother's address from Ghost entirely (a small privacy win). The D80 Book-side coordination is **unchanged**: the first raise still snapshots consent/verification and forces the newsletter flag off, and the reverse still restores that snapshot; only the Ghost side moved from *unsubscribe* to *delete/re-create*. The reconciliation audit gains a matching exemption (a deceased brother is expected to be Ghost-less; a lingering member surfaces as `unmatchedGhostMember`, exactly as for a de-brothered brother — N96). **Forrest's call** (2026-07-15): "make marking a brother deceased so it automatically deletes their Ghost record at the same time."

*Records to OFC-232, `API-SPEC.md` §3 (`PUT …/deceased`), `ENGINEERING-DESIGN.md` §5.1; amends D80; extends D133/D115; implemented in N96. Log-tail order: D133 → N95 → D134 → N96.*

### N96 — 5.5i implementation: the email↔Ghost-record lifecycle (create/delete on PATCH), email off the create surface, collision rejected (Option B), the shared invariant predicate, and the audit exemption

Session 5.5i implements D133 (the forward auto-create) and D134 (the deceased delete/re-create), and closes the open edge-case forks D133 left to the session — all against one invariant, made a single named predicate.

- **The invariant is a shared predicate.** `shouldHaveGhostMember(profile)` (`@pbe/shared` capabilities) = living + not-de-brothered + has a usable email — i.e. *has a Ghost member iff this holds*. It coincides with `isRoleEligible` (both are "can this brother use the Ghost bridge to sign in") and delegates to it, but is named separately because the two answer distinct questions and could diverge. Every Ghost create/delete gate reads this predicate.
- **The PATCH is the one email→Ghost surface.** A new `runEmailGhostLifecycle` (ghost-push.ts), run Ghost-first inside the per-record lock, resolves `stored → next` into: **create** (email added to an eligible Ghost-less brother — mint the member `send_email=false`, honoring the current `allowNewsletterEmail`, fold the fresh id into the same write), **delete** (email cleared on a brother who had a member — delete it, drop the id), **update** (an eligible brother keeps his member — the existing N65 pushed-field diff), or **none**. Both create and delete are gated on the **email actually changing**, so an unrelated edit (a phone change) never mints or deletes a member as a side effect — matching D133's "the PATCH that *adds* the email". Deceased/de-brothered can't ride a PATCH (`protected`), so `next`'s eligibility differs from `stored`'s only by the email.
- **Email is removed from the create surface entirely (Forrest's call).** Email was an *optional* field wrongly collected on the Add Brother mini-form and wrongly minting a Ghost member at create time (N71/N72). It is now **off the Add Brother form**, and `POST /api/profiles` **`422`s** a body carrying an email (rather than silently dropping it) — a create is always **Book-only**, and the Ghost member is minted later on the profile-edit PATCH. This concentrates *all* Ghost create/delete logic on the one PATCH surface (Forrest: "email should never have been on the Add Brother page in the first place"), and keeps the invariant from being even briefly violated by a Book record that has an email but no member.
- **A collision is rejected, not linked (Forrest's Option B).** If Ghost rejects the create because a member with that email already exists (it answers `422 ValidationError` — verified against the Admin API docs), `createMember` throws a typed `GhostDuplicateEmailError`, which the write path maps to a **`422` on `email`** ("already exists in PBE News under an account not linked to Book — an administrator must reconcile it"), distinct from the generic `502 ghost_create_failed` a transient outage yields. Option A (auto-adopt/link the member) was rejected: the ~70 historical unidentified Ghost addresses are purged from both Book and Ghost before launch (the mystery-email project), so a collision means *something is wrong* — the right response is a loud, specific error, not a silent link (Forrest's call).
- **The deceased delete/re-create (D134).** `PUT …/deceased` raise deletes the member (Ghost-first) and drops the id; reverse re-creates it via `shouldHaveGhostMember` evaluated on the post-reverse state, creating it with the **restored** consent (the snapshot value the commit will write) so no transient `newsletterDrift` appears. The de-brother reverse predicate was unified onto the same `shouldHaveGhostMember` call (previously a bare `hasUsableEmail`), so a brother who is *both* deceased and de-brothered is correctly reinstated Book-only.
- **The audit exemption.** The Book/Ghost alignment audit now treats a **deceased** brother exactly like a de-brothered one: excluded from the "legitimately referenced" member ids and skipped in the per-profile comparison. So a deceased brother with an email but no member is **not** flagged as `missingGhostMember`, while a still-live member for a deceased (or de-brothered) brother surfaces as `unmatchedGhostMember`. (`computeConsentDiff` became dead with the deceased consent-push gone and was removed.)

**Verified:** all 71 unit test files / 710 tests green; typecheck + Biome clean; prove-it test written first (a PATCH adding an email to a Ghost-less brother minted no member — watched fail, then pass). **Must-verify at live-test:** the exact Ghost duplicate-email status/shape against ghost-staging (built to the documented `422`; a mismatch degrades gracefully to a generic `502`, still safe).

*Records to `API-SPEC.md` §3 (`POST` no-email + `PATCH` email lifecycle), `ENGINEERING-DESIGN.md` §5.1, `USER-MANUAL.md` (Add Brother), `DATABASE-SCHEMA.md` §8 (email is not a create-settable field); implements D133/D134; builds on D98/N65/N72/D115/D80. Log-tail order: D134 → N96.*

### N97 — Bound the audit/bounce member-events fetch to a 24-month window (OFC-231)

`GhostAdminReader.listNewsletterEvents` and `listBounceEvents` fetched `type:…` from Ghost's **append-only** member-event feed with **no date bound**, so every alignment-audit / bounce-report run pulled the entire history for that type — over the years, hundreds of sequential paginated round-trips on a synchronous admin request, trending toward multi-second latency and a Cloud Run `502` on the very report meant to diagnose Ghost health (5b-2 had mitigated the *silent* failure — `getAll` throws at its 1000-page cap rather than undercounting — but not the growth). Both event fetches now carry an NQL `created_at:>'<cutoff>'` bound, `EVENT_LOOKBACK_MONTHS = 24` before now (day-granular UTC, single-quoted — Ghost parses a bare `'YYYY-MM-DD'` unambiguously; `+` is NQL's AND).

**Why 24 months, and why a bound degrades gracefully:** the alignment audit needs only the **latest** newsletter event per member (and that timestamp is *advisory* since N69 — the audit acts on nothing), and bounces matter only for **recent** sends; PBE News is bi-annual, so 24 months spans ~4 sends and keeps every useful event while capping the fetch. Omitting older events loses nothing the reports act on. A larger page `limit` was the other floated lever (OFC-231) but is **foreclosed by Ghost 6.0** (`limit` capped at 100 — OFC-217), leaving the date bound as the real fix. The cutoff clock is injectable for deterministic tests. `listMembers` / `listNewsletterEmails` are **not** bounded — they read the member and post collections (sized by membership / post count), not the unbounded event feed.

*Records to OFC-231; builds on N69 (advisory newsletter timestamp) and the 5b-2 `getAll` page-cap throw; relates to OFC-217 (Ghost 6.0 `limit` cap). Log-tail order: N96 → N97 (OFC-231 merges after OFC-232).*

### N98 — 5.5j implementation: the full D109 non-destructive recovery (child-window re-auth that resumes the held request), seamless read recovery, and two amendments to D109 (OFC-236 / OFC-153)

5.5c (N76) shipped only the *partial* D109 step — the edit-form writes opt out of the app-wide 401 bounce so no work is lost, but there was no re-auth and no resume; the user had to sign in on another tab and re-click Save. 5.5j builds the **full** recovery D109 designed, and reuses the same affordance for the directory read path (OFC-153). It is **entirely Book-side**: the Ghost bridge (`book.hbs`) already drives whatever window it is in and lands on Book's own `/auth/callback`, and Hosting sets **no `Cross-Origin-Opener-Policy`**, so `window.opener` survives the cross-origin hop and the `postMessage` handoff works — the bridge needs no change (verified against `firebase.json`).

**The mechanism.** A module-level re-auth **coordinator** in `SessionContext` (`requestReauth`, registered with the fetch layer via `setReauthHandler`, mirroring N76's `setUnauthorizedHandler`): gated on *was-authenticated* (a first-load 401 is left to `refresh`, never spawns a popup) and **deduped to a single child window** so concurrent 401s — a held Save, the roster read, the images that failed with them — all ride one re-auth. It opens the child window **synchronously first** (a blank `window.open("", "pbe-reauth", …)`) *before* `startSignIn()` mints the fresh nonce, then navigates it to the relay URL — because the popup fires after the Save's fetch, spending `startSignIn`'s round-trip before the open would eat more of the browser's transient-user-activation budget and get it blocked on the slow links this audience skews toward. The popup runs the existing bridge → Book's `/auth/callback`, which — seeing it has an opener and the `pbe-reauth` window name — re-establishes the shared `__session` cookie, `postMessage`s a typed `pbe-reauth-success`/`pbe-reauth-failed` back (same-origin checked, D104), and `window.close()`s (AuthCallback **popup mode**). The editor tab never navigates; nothing lands on disk. In `api.ts`, `fetchWithReauth` gives a mid-session 401 **one** transparent retry on success, **re-sending the original request `init`** — so the resumed PATCH echoes its original `If-Match` and a genuine concurrent edit still `412`s for D25 reconcile. The edit writes stay `silent` (a failed re-auth keeps the form); the reads are non-silent (a failed re-auth bounces — nothing to preserve).

**Amends D109 in two places (Forrest's calls, 5.5j):**
1. **R18 image retry → a lightweight "re-arm", not status-aware per-image re-auth.** An `<img>` element cannot read HTTP status (a 401, a 404, and a network blip all collapse to one `onError`), so images do **not** drive re-auth; instead a successful re-auth bumps a module-level signal (`reauthSignal.ts`, a `useSyncExternalStore` counter) and each thumbnail/headshot resets its failed state and re-fetches under the restored cookie. This honors D109's "one cap-lapse, one re-auth, images resume" without rearchitecting the byte-frugal, slow-link image path (D42) into `fetch`+blob-URL. In practice a roster/self read 401s and drives the re-auth first; the images ride it.
2. **The `sessionStorage` draft stash is dropped.** D109 named a tab-scoped `sessionStorage` stash as the popup-blocked fallback. With the child-window design the editor tab never navigates, so the in-memory form already survives unless the user *manually* reloads; the stash would guard only that, at the cost of writing PII (including the staged headshot **`Blob`**, which doesn't serialize cleanly) to disk against D95's spirit. The blocked-popup fallback is instead **in-memory + an honest recover-here message** ("Your session expired. Click Save again to sign in, or sign in on another tab") — a re-click is a fresh user gesture, so the popup reopens reliably.

**A known limit, accepted:** the popup fires *after* the Save's network round-trip, so on a slow link the round-trip can outrun the browser's transient-activation window and `window.open` is blocked — then the fallback above applies. The auto-popup is the seamless primary; the fallback is graceful, not lossy. (Forrest weighed a blocked-popup in-page "Sign in to save" button and chose to keep the approved "other tab" message.)

*Records to `ENGINEERING-DESIGN §2.3`/`§2.5`/`§2.6`; implements and amends **D109** (which gains a forward-trailer); supersedes N76's interim `expired` message + manual-copy affordance; reuses D104 (same-origin/allowlist), D107 (child window not iframe), D125 (rare-cap-lapse frequency), D95 (no-disk-PII), D25 (If-Match reconcile). Client seams: `apps/web/src/lib/api.ts` (`fetchWithReauth`/`setReauthHandler`), `auth/SessionContext.tsx` (`requestReauth`/`runReauth`), `pages/AuthCallback.tsx` (popup mode), `lib/reauthSignal.ts`, the edit/create/read/image consumers. Tests: `api.test.ts` (retry seam) + `e2e/app-shell-session-5.5j.spec.ts` (real popup handoff, blocked fallback, read recovery, first-load gate). Log-tail order: N97 → N98.*

### N99 — 5.5k implementation: the personal Star on the Profile page (set hoisted to a shell provider), the brother-role verification read-out narrowed, and a Select/Star divider (OFC-256 / OFC-235 / OFC-64; OFC-120 was already fixed)

A small-polish batch. The one structural change is OFC-256; the other two are presentation, and OFC-120 turned out already done.

- **OFC-256 — Star on the Profile page (the substantive change).** Stars were Directory-local state (`useStars` called inside the Directory page), so the Profile page — a sibling route under the gate, not a Directory child — had no access to the set. The set is now hoisted into a **shell-level provider** (`StarsContext` / `StarsProvider`), mounted on `GateLayout` beside the `SelectionProvider` and seeded once from the session's `/api/me` stars. The Directory consumes it via a no-arg `useStars()` context hook (the optimistic implementation hook was renamed `useStarsState` and now runs once inside the provider); the Profile's `IdentityHeader` renders the existing `StarButton` to the right of the Canonical Name. Because one set now backs both surfaces, a star toggled on a Profile is reflected on the Directory (and vice versa) **the moment the user navigates back — no reload** (e2e proves the round-trip both directions). The star is **uniform for all brothers**, exactly as on the Directory — including one's own record and deceased brothers (**Forrest's call**, 2026-07-15: "implement stars on profiles uniformly for all brothers, just as on the Directory page"; a gold toggle in a memorial header was weighed and judged tonally fine).
- **OFC-235 — the brother-role "Record status" narrowed.** A brother viewing another brother saw the public "Verified {date}" badge rendered **full-bleed** (its own full-width block), the only field on the page to do so. It now renders inside the two-up `Row` (a single grid column), so the badge is the width of an Identity/Contact field at `md`+ and collapses to full width below `md` like every other field — the staff view was already Row-nested, so this just aligns the brother view to it.
- **OFC-64 — Select/Star divider (staff grid).** Managers/admins saw the **Select** checkbox and the universal **Star** as two small adjacent controls easy to misclick (reported Phase 3c). A **subtle vertical rule** (a right `border-border` on the Select column, header + body cells, matching the grid's own cell borders) now separates them; the controls sit centered in their 44px cells, so there is whitespace on either side of the rule for breathing room. **Forrest's call** (option 1 of the ticket's three — divider + spacing, "least visual change"; the tint and reorder options were declined). Brothers are unaffected (no Select column, D33).
- **OFC-120 — no code needed.** The repeatable-editor row caps were already importing `MAX_LINKS` / `MAX_EMERGENCY_CONTACTS` from `@pbe/shared` (the shared constants exported, the local copies deleted) as of commit `28c6662` (Phase-4 PR #10 review remediation, OFC-107–OFC-121). The ticket had simply not been closed; verified and closed with evidence.

**Why the hoist rather than a second star hook on the Profile.** Two independent `useStars` instances would each reconcile to the server on toggle but would not update **each other** within a session — star on the Profile, go Back, and the Directory would still show unstarred until a reload. Hoisting to one per-instance in-memory context is the same pattern N79 used for selection (D31's fourth state bucket: private — never in a shared link; transient — dropped on reload / new tab; session-scoped — outlives the Directory's remount), and it sits inside the gate so a sign-out clears it for free. The existing optimistic-toggle logic (generation guard, revert-on-failure, reconcile-to-server-list — OFC-103) is reused untouched; only its host moved.

**Live-test refinements (2026-07-15).** Two things from Forrest's staging test. (1) The Profile star is rendered `prominent` — a 22px glyph sized to the class-year type beside it (`--text-h3`, 21px) in a roomier 40px target — because the Directory/card 18px star read too small next to the profile's larger name. (2) **Cross-window star sync is an accepted non-goal:** the set is per-tab in-memory, seeded from `/api/me` at load (the same transient/per-instance nature as the row selection, N79), so a star set in one window shows up in a *second* already-open window only after that window reloads. Forrest confirmed a real-time cross-tab channel (pub/sub, `BroadcastChannel`, storage events) isn't worth building for a private bookmark — the persisted `users.stars` is always authoritative on the next load.

*Records to `USER-MANUAL.md` §5 (already described starring another brother from his page — now implemented), `ENGINEERING-DESIGN` §5.7 (Profile identity header); extends **D39** (stars — gains a forward-trailer) and the D31/N79 shared-context pattern; relates to D41 (Select column) and D33 (`canSelectRows`). Client seams: `apps/web/src/pages/directory/StarsContext.tsx` (new provider), `useStars.ts` (`useStarsState`), `App.tsx` (`GateLayout` mount), `Directory.tsx` (consumes context), `pages/profile/ProfileView.tsx` (header star + Record-status Row), `directory/DirectoryGrid.tsx` (Select divider). Tests: `e2e/profile-star-5.5k.spec.ts` (cross-surface round-trip + mobile-viewport axe). Log-tail order: N98 → N99.*

### N100 — Architecture overview diagrams (`docs/architecture/`) and the README embed

Four hand-authored SVGs render the system architecture in the visual-design token palette (`tokens.css`, D29): a plain-English **slide** pair (light/dark, 16:9, built for the September 2026 Annual Reunion presentation — audience skews 60+, so 15px-minimum near-black text and strong borders, using the darker `--input` border token) and an annotated **readme** pair (identical layout plus a monospace technical layer: routes, cache directives, the `__session` cookie, the projection point). The repo README embeds the readme pair via `<picture prefers-color-scheme>`, so GitHub follows the reader's theme.

Composition: Firebase Hosting is drawn as a literal wall — "the front door" — with door openings; flow ② (the app shell) originates *at* the wall (edge-cached, D73), while flows ③/④ pass *through* the openings (member data is `no-store`, never cached at the edge — D95/D126). Ghost carries the crest-gold identity accent; everything Google-side sits in one labeled group; the numbered chips ①–④ order the flows for live narration. Fonts follow the app's own stack (Inter → system fallback, **not** embedded — the app itself doesn't ship Inter, and the diagrams honor the same byte-frugality; each SVG is ~11 KB). Deck PNGs are generated, not committed (`npx playwright screenshot --viewport-size=3200,1800 "file://$PWD/book-arch-slide-light.svg" out.png`; command in `docs/architecture/README.md`).

**Forrest's calls (2026-07-15):** two detail levels sharing one layout rather than a single compromise diagram; the wall metaphor and the ①–④ narration kept; no CDN box (the diagram matches D126, not the folklore); legibility over palette fidelity where they conflicted ("legibility has to win over beauty"); the house glyph on the wall dropped as more confusing than helpful.

*Records to `docs/architecture/README.md` (conventions + regeneration); renders D73/D82/D83/D85/D95/D104/D126 for readers; relates to D74 (byte-frugality). Log-tail order: N99 → N100.*

## Phase 6a (2026-07-16, the Lucide icon sweep + two live-test polish fixes)

### N101 — `lucide-react` adopted as the app's icon set in one sweep; the last emoji-as-icons retired; the consent "off" ring given real light-mode contrast

Phase 6a, the foundation for Phase 6's `CircleHelp` toggle-tips (which need a Lucide glyph). Three related changes landed across three PRs (#86 the sweep, #87 the emoji cleanup, #88 the contrast fix), all live-confirmed on staging.

**The icon sweep (PR #86).** `lucide-react` (`^1.24.0`, verified current against npm — not from training memory — and React-19-compatible) is added to `apps/web`, and ~17 hand-inlined chrome SVGs become Lucide glyphs: the four hand-authored Admin-card icons (`Download`/`RefreshCw`/`Bug`/`MailWarning`/`Megaphone`, kept behind thin sized-alias wrappers so the six consuming cards don't churn), the masthead `ExternalLink` and Report-a-bug `Bug`, `ThemeToggle` `Sun`/`Monitor`/`Moon`, the Directory `Columns3` / Filter `ChevronRight` (rotate-on-open preserved) / column-grip `GripVertical` / brother `Star` (brand-gold fill + 18/22px sizes preserved) / Unlisted-badge `EyeOff` / `ClearButton` `X`, and the Profile `Plus` and `Search` adornments. This realizes the 2026-07-07 Admin-session plan (recorded then as an aside) to adopt Lucide in one sweep. **Byte cost: +0.6 KB brotli** (220.0 vs 219.4 KB) — per-icon tree-shaking plus deleting ~221 lines of inline SVG nets to nearly free, which matters for the slow-connection 60+ audience (D74).

**Icon conventions established (the standing rule this sets).** Every Book icon is now a **monochrome Lucide line glyph that inherits `currentColor` and is `aria-hidden`** — so it adapts to light/dark and to the colour of the text beside it, and meaning never rides on the icon (D32). *Do not introduce emoji-as-icons or multicolour/raster glyphs.*

**Kept bespoke (Forrest's call).** `DebrotheredMark` (the crossed-out expelled-record mark) and the `Avatar` default person-silhouette stay hand-authored — meaning-bearing illustrations, not icon-library chrome.

**Forrest's live-test calls (2026-07-16), folded in as follow-ups:**
- **Report-a-bug glyph moved to the *right* of its label**, mirroring the neighbouring "PBE News ↗" link's trailing external-link icon, so the two masthead links read consistently (PR #86).
- **The lock/warning emoji retired (PR #87).** The `🔒` on locked/system-controlled Profile fields (Constitution ID, Little Brothers, `PrivateMarker`, `LockedField`, the locked `ConsentSwitch` — five sites) was the OS **colour emoji**: multicolour and theme-blind where every other glyph is monochrome and quiets down in dark mode. → Lucide `Lock`. A sibling `⚠` on the manager restricted-block eyebrow → `TriangleAlert`. Both inherit `currentColor` (teal in the read-only eyebrow, muted in the field rows, gold in the warn eyebrow) and keep their hover-tooltip spans and `aria-hidden`.
- **The consent "off" status ring given real light-mode contrast (PR #88).** The view-mode "Preferences & consent" list (`ProfileView`) marks each line with a filled green dot (on) / hollow ring (off). The ring's `border-[var(--track)]` on the white light-mode card (`--card #ffffff`) was only **~1.5:1** — "almost invisible." → `--muted-foreground` (the same tone as the "off" label text beside it; the calibrated visible-muted colour in both themes, ~5.9:1 light). One token fixes both modes; the ring still reads lighter than the solid green on-dot, so the on/off *shape* distinction (D32) is intact. Not a strict WCAG failure (state is redundantly carried in the label text + consequence wording, so the ring is defensibly decorative under 1.4.11's "required to identify" wording) — which is precisely **why neither the automated axe pass nor the manual reviews flagged it**: axe's `color-contrast` rule checks text (1.4.3), not **1.4.11 non-text contrast** of custom indicators (un-automatable), and a conformance review would reasonably pass a redundantly-encoded state. Filed **OFC-261** (Phase 7 / 7c a11y audit) to add a **token-pairing contrast matrix** (every foreground/border token × every surface it lands on, both themes, checked mechanically against 3:1/4.5:1) plus a manual "scan each state indicator in both themes at low vision" checklist step — the net axe structurally can't provide.

*Records to `CODING-PROJECT-PLAN §Phase 6` (6a done; 6b/6c remain); establishes the Lucide icon convention; cites D32/D74/D79/D111; files OFC-261. Log-tail order: N100 → N101.*

## Phase 6b-1 (2026-07-16, the in-context help enrichment) — renamed from "6b" on 2026-07-16 when Forrest chose to add more help sessions (6b-2, …) before 6c

### N102 — The `CircleHelp` toggle-tips wired across every page; the privacy/consent switch copy and the admin-card descriptions folded into the help-content registry; the interim `HelpTip` retired

Phase 6b-1 (originally "6b") delivers the above-baseline help layer the WCAG split (D111) deferred out of Phases 3–5: the richer `?` "what is this / how do I use it" explanations, provided **only where a control isn't self-evident** (the plan's Phase 6 discipline — most controls keep just a label and, where needed, a helper line). The member-facing copy was reviewed by Forrest before wiring, via a CSV round-trip (per-control coverage list + draft copy → his edits → the registry).

**The toggle-tip component.** `HelpToggleTip` (`apps/web/src/components/HelpToggleTip.tsx`) is the app's one help affordance: a click/tap-toggle Radix Popover (the 4b-1 headless landing, N36) triggered by the Lucide `CircleHelp` glyph (6a enabled it). Radix supplies keyboard operability, focus management, and Escape / outside-click dismissal; the trigger carries an accessible name (`Help: <label>`) and a 24px target (WCAG 2.2 AA 2.5.8). A toggle-tip, **not** a hover tooltip — it never depends on a pointer the 60+ audience may not hover with. `ControlHelp` (`components/ControlHelp.tsx`) is the registry-driven drop-in: it looks an entry up by id and renders the tip **iff** a `toggleTip` is authored, so a call site can wire it unconditionally. The interim native-`<details>` `HelpTip` is deleted (`useDetailsAutoClose` stays — the avatar menu and Columns picker still use it).

**Switch copy into the registry (Option A — Forrest's call).** `HelpEntry` gains optional `whenOn`/`whenOff` (populated only by switch entries), so the eight privacy/consent switches source their inline consequence and their `?` counterfactual from the shared registry, not the local `consent.ts` module (D53 — the 6c USER-MANUAL now reads the same strings; the two cannot drift). `consent.ts` shrinks to a `switchCopy(key)` resolver (throws on an unknown or non-switch key — a drift guard) plus the `activeConsequence`/`counterfactual` helpers; `ConsentSwitch` takes an `entryKey` and `ProfileEdit`/`ProfileView` reference `SWITCH_KEYS`. A switch may also carry a `toggleTip` (richer context shown beneath the counterfactual in the same popover) — **MITAA** and **Listed** do; the other six are counterfactual-only.

**Coverage (Forrest-approved).** New `?` tips: Directory **Name Search** (name-only scope + pointer to Filters), the staff **Staff** / **Verification** / **Not verified since** filters, staff **Export CSV** (whole-selection-across-the-dataset scope; role + photos excluded); Profile **Full name**, **Class year**, **Email**, **Links**, **Courses**, **Big Brother**, **Verification**, and richer context on the **MITAA** / **Listed** switches. Declined: the Class Year / Constitution ID **filter** grammar (placeholder + inline error suffice) and every self-evident field. The Profile field helper texts (fullLegalName/classYear/mugName/alternateEmail/adminNote) also moved into the registry as their single source; the alternate-email *disabled-state* instruction stays inline (a UI state, not manual material).

**Admin-card descriptions folded in (Forrest's note "existing but missing here").** The three cards whose blurbs were hardcoded — Ghost audit, Bounce report, Bug reports — now read `title`/`description` from the registry via `getHelpEntry`, matching the Backup/Banner cards, so all admin help is one source for the manual. No `?` tips there (an admin card's description already is its explanation).

**The Email tip pre-empts part of OFC-254.** Forrest's copy warns that clearing the email address makes login impossible (accurate — clearing email deletes the Ghost member, D134, and login is the Ghost magic-link), makes the brother hard to reach, and unsubscribes them from PBE News — the create/delete side effect OFC-254 was filed to surface, now stated in-context. **Two minor editorial edits pending his live-test eyeball:** a redundant "…PBE News … will be sent to, and that PBE News will be sent to" clause was de-duplicated, and the verb "login" → "log in".

**Landmines.** (1) `@pbe/help-content` builds to `dist/` (`tsc -b`) — rebuild it after editing the registry or the web typecheck/tests see stale types (the gate rebuilds libs first, so CI is fine). (2) A switch entry MUST carry `whenOn`/`whenOff`; `switchCopy` throws otherwise, and a new switch that forgets them fails the `consent.test.ts` drift check. (3) The `?` trigger's accessible name is `Help: <label>` (fields) or `Help: What changes if you flip "<label>"` (switches) — e2e selects on these.

*Records to `CODING-PROJECT-PLAN §Phase 6` (6b-1 done; 6c remains) and the registry doc-comment; extends D53/D111/D113/D45; partially pre-empts OFC-254. Log-tail order: N101 → N102.*

### N103 — 6b-1 live-test polish: the switch `?` drops the counterfactual (keeps only static context); Email/Courses copy; Export `?` binding

Forrest's staging live-test of N102 (2026-07-16). Changes, all his calls:

**The switch `?` no longer carries the counterfactual (amends D113).** D113's model put each switch's inline active consequence on the page and the *counterfactual* ("what flips if you change this") one tap away in the `?`. In practice the counterfactual read as redundant with the inline consequence for the per-field switches — the inline text already implies its own negation — so the counterfactual is **removed from the `?` entirely**. A switch's `?` now shows **only its optional static `toggleTip`**, exactly as a field's does, so `ConsentSwitch` renders the same `ControlHelp` the fields use (the bespoke counterfactual popover and the `counterfactual()` helper are deleted). Net effect: the five per-field share switches (email/address/phone/emergency/spouse) **and** the newsletter switch now have **no `?`**; only **MITAA** and **Listed** keep one, showing just their standing context. The panel intro shrank from "Each switch shows what's true now; the `?` says what changes if you flip it." to **"Each switch shows what's true now."** The inline active consequence (D45/D113's primary transparency) is untouched — this trims only the redundant second layer.

**Copy.** The **Email** tip was reworded to point brothers at the switches instead of enumerating effects: clearing the field makes login impossible (D134) and, "If you just want to unsubscribe from PBE News or hide your email address, turn off the appropriate privacy switch under 'Privacy & consent', below." **Courses**: "substantial work toward a degree" (dropped "study").

**Verification tip — deliberately unchanged.** Forrest asked to add "Verification expires after 1 year"; checking the code showed verification **does not auto-expire** — the only mechanism is D48's **two-year staleness *nudge*** (`TWO_YEARS_MS` in `ProfileControls.tsx`), a banner inviting re-confirmation, not an expiry. Rather than ship inaccurate copy or build an expiry mechanism, **Forrest's call was to leave the tip as-is** (no expiry sentence).

**Directory.** The **Export CSV** `?` is now wrapped with its button in one tight `inline-flex` (gap-1.5) inside a `gap-3` bar, so the tip visibly binds to Export and is clearly separated from Add Brother (it had sat equidistant between them).

*Records to the registry doc-comment; amends D113 (counterfactual dropped from the `?`) and N102; leaves D48's staleness horizon authoritative for verification. Log-tail order: N102 → N103.*

### N104 — The column-lens "foreign shared link" test compares `cols` to the saved value, not mere URL presence (fixes OFC-263; refines D30/D31)

**Bug (OFC-263, High).** After using "View as" impersonation, "Reset to default columns" stopped working: an admin who customised columns, impersonated a brother, then stopped, found Reset had no effect — and further column edits misbehaved for the rest of the session.

**Root cause.** The column lens (D30/D31, N15) persists to localStorage *and* mirrors to the URL (`?cols=`), and it withholds edits from localStorage when the view arrived via a *foreign* shared link, so opening someone else's link and tweaking a column can't clobber your saved setup (OFC-101). But `useColumnLens` decided "foreign shared link" purely by **whether the URL carried `cols` at mount** (`fromSharedLink = cols != null`). "View as" start/stop does a **hard reload** (N31 — so the directory re-downloads at the new projection), and a hard reload preserves the user's *own* URL, including the `?cols=` that `apply()` had reflected there. So after the reload the user's own view was misread as a foreign link, `fromSharedLink` latched true, and from then on edits and Reset only rewrote the URL while localStorage kept the stale custom lens — `reset()`'s `setCols(null)` then fell back to that stale saved value, so Reset appeared to do nothing.

**Decision (Forrest's call, Option A — "the more elegant approach").** Decide "foreign" by **comparing the incoming `cols` against the persisted localStorage value**, not by URL presence: `fromSharedLink = cols != null && cols !== loadSavedRaw()`. `apply()` writes the URL and localStorage from the *same* serialisation, in lock-step, so the user's own view always satisfies `cols === saved` after any reload — including the impersonation reload — while a genuine shared link (a lens the recipient never saved) differs and stays transient. This encodes the actual OFC-101 invariant ("a lens I never saved must not clobber my default") directly, rather than the URL-presence proxy that the reload defeated. The comparison is on the **raw serialised strings**, before role-parsing, so a saved staff-only column (filtered out of a brother's *displayed* lens) can't make the own view look foreign. Bonus: it also fixes the latent sibling case where bookmarking your own reflected view read as foreign.

Rejected — a reload-detection approach (`PerformanceNavigationTiming` + a sessionStorage breadcrumb): a proxy signal with more moving parts that still left the bookmark case broken. Rejected — "don't persist edits while impersonating": it diverges the URL from localStorage and so re-breaks the own-vs-foreign test after impersonation (would need extra URL-clearing machinery) — worse than the disease.

**Known residual (deferred, OFC-274, Low).** Because own-view edits now persist again, editing columns *while impersonating* a lower role persists that role's filtered lens, silently dropping any saved staff-only columns from the default. Narrow trigger (deliberate column edit while in View-as with a staff-only column saved); a correct guard needs its own design pass (see OFC-274), so it's out of scope here to keep the fix to one root cause.

Guarded by `e2e/columns-impersonate-6b-2.spec.ts`: the 8-step repro (customise → View as → stop → Reset restores the default) and an OFC-101 regression guard (a foreign `?cols=` link's edits never touch the recipient's saved default). Change is `apps/web/src/pages/directory/useColumnLens.ts` only.

*Refines D30/D31 (the URL/localStorage lens model); does not change the persisted format or the URL grammar. Log-tail order: N103 → N104.*

### D135 — Clearing a set email is gated behind a client-side confirmation; the sole-usable-admin case stays a server hard-block (OFC-272)

Removing a brother's email address silently locks them out of both the Address Book and PBE News — the Ghost bridge resolves sign-in by email (`hasUsableEmail`; C15/D20/D115), so an email-less brother can never authenticate. It is the second-most-destructive profile edit after outright deletion, yet the edit form saved it with no more friction than fixing a typo. **Forrest's call: gate it.** A Save that removes a previously-usable email now raises an "are you sure — this locks *name* out" confirmation — the same accessible `ConfirmDialog` (destructive tone) the Delete-brother / De-brother controls use, different copy — on all three edit paths (self, manager, admin).

**Two design forks, both Forrest's call:**

- **No new server-side guard for the general case.** The confirmation is a UX affordance, not an invariant: a brother *may* legitimately remove their email (Book deliberately tolerates email-less brothers, ~1/3 of the roster — C15/D115). The only genuine server invariant is the last-admin one, which already exists (D129/D130), so the general email-clear stays a soft, confirmable client warning with no matching hard block.
- **The confirmation composes *in front of* the existing sole-usable-admin hard block.** `profiles.ts` already refuses (`409 last_admin`) a PATCH that would strip the sole usable admin's email (D130). The client cannot know "sole usable admin" ahead of a save (it is server-resident cache state — D128/D83), so the warning fires for that admin too; on confirm the server's 409 is the backstop — now surfaced with a specific message instead of the generic banner (N105). Warning for everyone, hard block preserved for the last admin.

*Continues the write-side chain D106 → D128 → D129 → D130 → N86; implemented in N105. Log-tail order: N104 → D135 → N105.*

### N105 — 6b-3 implementation: the email-clear guard predicate, and the PATCH `409 last_admin` finally mapped on the client (closes N86's gap on this path)

Implements D135 (OFC-272).

**The trip predicate is one pure, unit-tested function.** `wouldClearUsableEmail(original, patch)` in `patch.ts` — `"email" in patch && hasUsableEmail(original.email) && !hasUsableEmail(patch.email)` — reuses the *same* `hasUsableEmail` the server's last-admin check uses, so client and server agree on what "usable" means. `"email" in patch` keys off the field actually changing (an untouched email never trips it); `hasUsableEmail` treats null / undefined / whitespace as not-usable, so a redacted private-email projection (a manager without `shareEmail`, N70 — `original.email` never reached the client) cannot false-trip either. `ProfileEdit.onSave` gained a `confirmedEmailClear` re-entry: the guard sets a `confirmClearEmail` state and bails before the PATCH; the dialog's confirm re-invokes `onSave(true)`, which skips the guard and proceeds.

**The N86 gap on the PATCH-email path is closed.** N86 surfaced the last-admin refusal in the mark-deceased / de-brother / role UIs but left the *PATCH-email* 409 unmapped: `patchProfile` had no `409` branch (it threw → the generic "couldn't save just now"), and `PatchOutcome` / `SubmitResult` had no `last_admin` variant. The `409 → last_admin` outcome is now threaded end to end (`api.ts` → `Profile.tsx` `submit` → `ProfileEdit` banner), guarded on `body.error === "last_admin"` so any other 409 still throws. The sole-usable-admin block now reads "You can't remove the last administrator's email address — … Give another brother the administrator role first."

**Tests.** `patch.test.ts` covers the predicate (clear / whitespace / change / untouched / never-had / redacted / empty-patch); a new `profile-email-guard-6b3.spec.ts` e2e drives the dialog on self / manager / admin, asserts the PATCH is withheld until confirm and that Keep-editing sends nothing, covers the 409 banner, and gates the open dialog on WCAG 2.2 AA (D79).

*Implements D135; extends N86 (its last-admin-surfacing thread now covers the PATCH-email path). Log-tail order: D135 → N105.*

### D136 — The Directory shows all of a brother's courses, not only the primary (amends D33)

D33 chose to show only the **primary** course in the Directory's Course column, to give the brother a single-line directory identity they control. In practice the limit bought nothing: almost every brother has one course, a handful have two, and the column — once it is wide enough to show its own "Course" heading — easily holds two or three chips. The single-course rule simply hid real data. **The Directory (both the wide-screen grid and the small-screen cards) now renders the full `majors` array as course chips**, in the brother's chosen order (primary first). The brother's course ordering stays load-bearing (the same ordering D33 made load-bearing — it now governs the order of the whole list, not just which one shows).

**Overflow — Forrest's call: hard-clip.** When a brother has more courses than the column is wide enough to show, the chips clip at the column's right edge exactly like any too-narrow column (widen the column to see the rest). No `+N` counter and no "…" glyph — a row of chips cannot take a native text ellipsis the way plain text can, and fewer than 1% of brothers have three or more courses, so the simplest behaviour is the right one. No wrapping and no row-height change.

**No behavioural change to sort or filter.** The Course column still **sorts** on the primary course (`primaryMajor` — the grid-model `display`/`sortValue`, also the CSV export value, are unchanged), and the Course **filter** already matched *any* of a brother's courses (§5.6.1), so multi-course display is already consistent with both. **No data-path change either**: `majors` was always the complete array on the wire (the one shared `Profile`, D3); only the rendering changed — the projection and payload were already carrying every course.

*Amends D33 (Directory column model: primary-course-only display → all courses). Implemented in N106. Records to PRD §5.6. Log-tail order: N105 → D136.*

### N106 — 6b-4 implementation: the Directory-page UI batch (OFC-262 / 265 / 266 / 267 / 269)

Five Directory-page tickets, one PR, all on `apps/web/src/pages/directory/` (plus doc propagation).

- **OFC-269 (all courses, implements D136).** A shared **`CourseChips`** component (`Chips.tsx`) renders a brother's course list on a single line — each chip `shrink-0`, the caller's cell (`overflow-hidden whitespace-nowrap`) clipping the overflow. `DirectoryGrid` (the major cell) and `DirectoryCards` (the Course `dd`) both use it, replacing their `majors?.[0]` single-chip render. Empty list → the caller's em-dash placeholder.
- **OFC-265 (chips in the Course filter).** `MultiSelectFilter` gained an optional `renderOption`; only the Course filter passes one, rendering the shared `CourseChip` followed by the course name — visual consistency with the grid/cards/profile, `CourseChip` reused unchanged. The chip already carries the "Course `<code>`, `<name>`" accessible name, so the visible description is `aria-hidden` to avoid a doubled screen-reader announcement. Checkbox + description layout otherwise untouched.
- **OFC-266 / OFC-267 (filter labels).** The Staff filter option "Managers and Administrators" → "**PBE Address Book Managers and Administrators**" (regular brothers may not know Book has roles). The newsletter filter label "Newsletter" → "**Subscribed to PBE News**". *Scope note:* OFC-267 changed the **filter** only; the staff-only **Newsletter column** header still reads "Newsletter" (flagged for Forrest — "Subscribed to PBE News" is long for that narrow column).
- **OFC-262 (header fill past the last column — Forrest's call: fill it).** When the columns are narrower than the viewport, the header strip right of the last column now carries the header background instead of the general grid background. Mechanism: a trailing auto-width **spacer `<col>`** plus a presentational, **`aria-hidden` spacer `<th>`** (`bg-secondary`, sticky, matching `HeaderCell`'s height/border), and the table's width changed from `totalWidth` to `width:100%; min-width:totalWidth` so it fills a wider container while keeping the real column widths and the horizontal scroll (the spacer collapses to zero when the columns overflow). **Body rows get no spacer cell**, so the body keeps the general grid background — only the header fills, which is exactly the ask. Book's grid is a bare HTML `<table>` (TanStack supplies row virtualization, not header rendering), so there was no grid-library option to toggle — the fill is ours.
- **Tests.** `e2e/directory-6b-4.spec.ts`: all-courses in the grid and (mobile) in the cards, the filter chips + description with a WCAG 2.2 AA axe pass, both new labels, and the header spacer. The existing Directory / scroll / column e2e stay green (the table-width change didn't regress column widths or the horizontal scroll).

*Implements D136 (OFC-269) and the four sibling tickets. Log-tail order: D136 → N106.*

### N107 — 6b-5 Profile-surface UI batch: share toggles unified into Privacy & consent (OFC-270), Admin Note promoted to its own section (OFC-271), repeatable spacing/alignment (OFC-260); OFC-268 declined (D93 upheld)

**Share toggles unified into Privacy & consent (OFC-270).** The `shareEmergency` and `shareSpousePartner` switches moved out from beside the Emergency-contacts editor and the Spouse/partner field into the primary switch group of the "Privacy & consent" section, joining `shareEmail`/`shareAddress`/`sharePhone` — one placement philosophy for all five per-field share toggles rather than the split the page carried (Forrest's call). Pure relocation: the switches keep their `entryKey`/`setPrivacy` bindings and `locked` behaviour, and the field editors keep their `managerSeesPrivate` "private" markers. The moved toggles now behave exactly like `shareEmail`'s, which always sat in the privacy section (privacy flags are `restricted`-class, so a manager receives them regardless of the toggle). Their **off-copy was rewritten to name the field** — "Your emergency contacts are visible to administrators only." / "Your spouse / partner is visible to administrators only." (was the bare "Visible to administrators only.") — so each row is self-identifying once it no longer sits next to the field it protects, matching the reachability switches. Copy lives in the help-content registry, the single source read by the UI and the 6c manual (D53/N102).

**Admin Note promoted to its own "Administrative" section (OFC-271).** On the Profile *view*, the staff-internal Admin Note moved out of "Record status" — where it blended into the verification read-out and was repeatedly overlooked — into a new "Administrative" `Section`, stacked in the left column beneath "Preferences & consent" with Record status remaining the right column (Forrest's layout call). Same render guard as before — managers/admins only, and only when a note exists — so the heading never appears for the owner, a non-staff viewer, or an empty note (`adminNote` is `staff-internal`, never in a brother's projection anyway). It reuses the shared `Section` so the document outline stays correct for screen readers.

**Repeatable-editor spacing & alignment (OFC-260).** In the Links + Emergency-contacts editors the Links "Remove" button is now vertically centred against the inputs beside it (it was top-aligned and hung short of their bottom edge); and a single spacing token (`space-y-4`) now separates the field group from "+ Add a link", the contact cards from one another, and the cards from "+ Add an emergency contact" — the previous near-zero `space-y-3` gaps read as cramped against the bordered cards and dashed Add buttons. One alignment treatment, one spacing token, as the ticket asked.

**OFC-268 declined — D93 upheld (Forrest's call).** OFC-268 proposed defaulting emergency-contact and spouse/partner visibility to *on*. Declined at the plan gate: those are third-party data — people who aren't PBE members and never consented — so opt-in stays the correct default. No code change; **D93 stands, unamended.**

**Tests.** New `profile-6b5.spec.ts` locks the two structural changes — the five share switches all resolve *inside* the Privacy & consent section with none stranded beside their fields, the moved switches' self-identifying off-copy, and the Administrative section's staff-only/non-empty guard — plus an axe WCAG 2.2 AA scan of the restructured restricted block. The OFC-260 spacing is visual-only and not asserted.

*Batch of OFC-270/271/260; reaffirms D93 (OFC-268 declined). Extends the Profile-controls polish chain (N35) and the consent-copy chain (N102/N103). Log-tail order: D135 → N105 → D136 → N106 → N107.*
*Later updated by: N109 — the OFC-260 spacing here was inert (`space-y` cancelled by the rows' `m-0`); the real fix is flex `gap`. And the OFC-271 Admin Note "Administrative" section reaches the edit page there too.*

### N108 — 6b-4 follow-up: the course chip + name unified into one aligned component, adopted by the Profile course picker (refines N106/OFC-265)

Forrest's live-test of N106's Course-filter chips surfaced three issues, all fixed here:

1. **Chip codes wrapped.** In a tight flex row beside a long course name, `CourseChip` flex-shrank and its code (e.g. "6-2") broke across two lines. Fixed at the source: `CourseChip` now carries `shrink-0 whitespace-nowrap`, so a chip keeps its full size and its code never wraps anywhere it appears. `CourseChips` (the Directory grid/cards list) drops its now-redundant per-chip `shrink-0` wrappers.
2. **Descriptions didn't line up.** Chip widths vary with the code ("7" vs "6-3"), so the names started at different x. New shared component **`CourseChipName`** (Chips.tsx) puts the chip in a fixed-width slot (`w-11`, wide enough for the widest 3-character code), followed by the name; a long name wraps beneath itself while the chip stays top-aligned (`items-start`). The name is `aria-hidden` (the chip's aria-label already carries "Course <code>, <name>"), so the option's accessible name is unchanged.
3. **The Profile course picker didn't match.** Forrest asked (extending OFC-265) that the Profile edit **course picker** read like the filter — colour chips + aligned names, minus the checkboxes. The picker is the shared `Combobox` (also the Big-Brother typeahead), so it gained an optional **`renderOption`** prop (default unchanged → the typeahead is untouched); `MajorsEditor` passes `CourseChipName`. The Directory Course filter (`MultiSelectFilter` renderOption) and the picker now render through the one component, so the two can't drift again.

**Tests.** `directory-6b-4.spec.ts` gains an alignment assertion (every description shares the same left x across chip-code widths 2 / 6-3 / 18) and a `whitespace-nowrap` guard on the chip; `profile-4b1.spec.ts` asserts the picker option renders the chip (by its "code — name" title). Full gate green.

*Refines N106 (OFC-265); extends the controls chain N36/N37 (`Combobox` gains `renderOption`) and the course-chip presentation (D136/N106). Log-tail order: N107 → N108.*
### N109 — 6b-5 live-test follow-up: the repeatable-editor spacing actually renders now (flex `gap`, not `space-y`), and the Admin Note's "Administrative" section reaches the edit page too (OFC-260 / OFC-271)

**N107's OFC-260 spacing fix was inert — flex `gap` was needed.** The Links and Emergency repeatable rows are `<fieldset>`s carrying `m-0` (the reset of the browser's default fieldset margin), and `m-0` cancels `space-y`'s `margin-top`. So N107's `space-y-3 → space-y-4` changed nothing: the rows, the contact cards, and the "+ Add …" buttons all rendered with **0px** between them — the ticket's literal "zero vertical space." The real fix is **`flex flex-col gap-4`** on both repeatable containers — flex/grid `gap` is immune to child margins. Two riders: a flex column stretches its children on the cross axis by default, which blew the Add button up to the full column width (pinned back with `self-start`); and the gap was tuned to 16px after the first attempt's 20px read "a little too far." A new e2e measures the actual pixel gap between the link rows and before the Add button, so the collapse can't silently return. **Reusable landmine: `space-y-*` silently no-ops on any child carrying `m-0` / a margin reset — use flex or grid `gap` there.**

**OFC-271 completed on the edit page.** N107 promoted the Admin Note into its own "Administrative" section on the *view*; the note also renders on the *edit* page, where it was still sitting inside Record status. The edit page now mirrors the view — a staff-only "Administrative" `Section` (the note's `TextAreaField`) stacked in the left column under Privacy & consent, out of Record status (the input is always shown for staff, empty or not, since they need it to add a note).

*Follow-up to N107 (OFC-260/271); corrects N107's spacing mechanism (`space-y` → flex `gap`). Log-tail order: N107 → N108 → N109.*

### N110 — Directory filter multi-selects dismiss on outside click / Escape (live-test follow-up)

The Directory's Course, Country, and State/Province filters are native `<details>` disclosures (§5.6.4, D38); unlike the Profile course picker's Radix popover they stayed open until the summary was clicked again. Forrest flagged the inconsistency on live-test. Fixed by reusing the app's existing **`useDetailsAutoClose`** hook — already dismissing the Columns picker and the masthead avatar menu — inside `MultiSelectFilter`: an outside pointerdown closes the open disclosure, and Escape closes it and restores focus to the summary. The fix lives in the shared component, so all three multi-selects gain it together (Forrest's call: consistency over singling out Course). Filtering behaviour is unchanged. Test: `directory-3c.spec.ts` opens the Course disclosure and asserts that an outside click and Escape each close it.

*Extends D38 (filter panel) with the disclosure-dismiss hook already used by the Columns picker and the avatar menu. Renumbered from N109 (the 6b-5 session merged first and took N109). Log-tail order: N109 → N110.*

### N111 — Course filter option: the checkbox aligns to the first line of a wrapping course name (refines N106/N108)

Live-test: with a course name long enough to wrap to two lines in the narrow (3-column) filter, the `MultiSelectFilter` row's checkbox centred on the whole two-line block (`items-center`) while the chip — via `CourseChipName`'s `items-start` — sat on the first line, so the two no longer lined up. Fixed by switching the option `<label>` from `items-center` to **`items-start`** and nudging the checkbox **`mt-0.5`** to centre it on the first (20px) line, so the checkbox, the chip, and the first line of the description all align — for both single- and multi-line options. The Country and State/Province multi-selects (single-line) are unaffected. Test: `directory-6b-4.spec.ts` opens the Course filter at a wrapping width and asserts the checkbox's vertical centre tracks the chip's.

*Refines N106/N108 (Course-filter chip layout); extends D38 (filter panel). Log-tail order: N110 → N111.*

### N112 — Course-column auto-fit measures the full course-chip strip, not just the primary course (OFC-277)

OFC-269/D136 made the Directory's Course cell render *all* of a brother's courses as chips, but the double-click auto-fit (N27) still measured only the primary course. The column model's `major.display` returns the primary code alone — kept deliberately as the sort/export value — and the auto-fit handler fed that single string, plus one chip's padding, to `autoFitWidth`. So double-clicking the Course column border sized it to a single chip and clipped the rest for any multi-course brother (the reported symptom).

Fix: the auto-fit now measures the whole chip strip. `autofit.ts` gains **`chipStripWidth(codes, measure)`** — Σ(code width + chip padding) plus the `gap-1` between adjacent chips — and **`autoFitChipStripWidth(header, rowsOfCodes, measure)`**, which fits the widest strip across the display set; the shared header/clamp arithmetic is factored into a private `fitColumn`. `Directory.tsx` routes the `major` key through the chip path (reading `profile.majors` directly, exactly as the cell renderer does); every other column keeps the plain-text path. The primary-only `major.display`/`sortValue` are untouched, so sort and CSV export stay keyed on the primary (D33). The now-unused `extraWidthFor` helper and `autoFitWidth`'s `extraPerValue` parameter are removed — the Course chip was their only user. Two deliberate approximations preserved: chip codes are measured at the 14px grid body font though chips render at 12px `text-xs` (a slight over-estimate that only adds harmless slack, never a clip), and the 640px max-width clamp still applies, so a brother with an extreme course count clips-with-ellipsis exactly as OFC-269 intended.

Tests (repro-first): `autofit.test.ts` gains `chipStripWidth`/`autoFitChipStripWidth` coverage — single chip, multi-chip gaps, empty list, header floor, and the explicit "all courses fit wider than the primary alone" OFC-277 regression. `directory-3c.spec.ts` narrows the Course column to its minimum (a triple-major brother's second/third chips then clipped), double-clicks the separator to auto-fit, and asserts no chip is clipped — guarding the `Directory.tsx` wiring the unit tests can't reach. Full gate green.

*Refines N27 (double-click auto-fit) for the all-courses chip cell (D136/N106/OFC-269). Log-tail order: N111 → N112.*

### N113 — The N97 member-events date bound named the wrong NQL field; correct it to `data.created_at` and make the audit's advisory read failure-safe (OFC-275)
