N97's 24-month bound filtered the member-event fetches on the **bare** `created_at` field, but Ghost's `/members/events` endpoint validates every filter key against a hard allowlist — `['data.created_at', 'data.member_id', 'data.post_id', 'type', 'id']` (Ghost `event-repository.js` `getNQLSubset`) — and rejects anything else with `400 "Cannot filter by created_at"`. The event's timestamp lives at `data.created_at`, so both fetches 400'd against real Ghost. This never showed in CI (unit/e2e inject fake readers, not real Ghost — the same real-vs-fake gap flagged at 5.5i) and surfaced only when the alignment audit was run against ghost-staging during OFC-272 live-test: `listNewsletterEvents` threw inside the audit route's read block, so the whole audit returned `502 ghost_read_failed` (generic error screen), and the bounce report — sharing the bounded events query — 400'd identically. Broken since N97 landed (2026-07-15).

Fix, two parts. **(1) Correct the field** — both filters now read `type:…+data.created_at:>'<cutoff>'` (verified against the Ghost source allowlist; the 24-month window, day-granular UTC cutoff, and injectable clock from N97 are otherwise unchanged). **(2) Make the audit resilient** — `listNewsletterEvents` now swallows a read failure to `[]` with a server-side `WARNING`, mirroring the best-effort `listNewsletterEmails` 403-swallow: the audit's `ghostChangedAt` enrichment is *advisory* (N69 — a missing timestamp degrades the report, it does not break it), so an advisory read must never 502 the whole audit. `listBounceEvents` deliberately does **not** swallow — the bounce report genuinely needs those events, so a failure must surface as 502 rather than produce an empty-and-misleadingly-clean report. A true total Ghost outage still fails loudly via the non-swallowed `listMembers`. Part 2 is the belt (never breaks again on an advisory event read); Part 1 is the fix (the reports work).

Tests (repro-first): `ghost-reader.test.ts` updated to assert the `data.created_at` filter strings (the OFC-231 bound tests are the guard against re-introducing the bare field), plus a new pair — `listNewsletterEvents` degrades to `[]` on a failed events fetch, and `listBounceEvents` throws on one. The exact NQL was verified against the Ghost `event-repository.js` allowlist (source is the Ghost 6-line `main`; the allowlist has carried `data.created_at` since Ghost 4.x, and ghost-staging runs v5); real-Ghost confirmation is Forrest's post-deploy staging live-test (Run audit downloads its report; bounce report succeeds), since the fake-reader tests can't reach real Ghost's NQL validation.

*Amends N97 (which introduced the wrong field name); builds on N69 (advisory newsletter timestamp) and the `listNewsletterEmails` best-effort swallow (D120). Relates to OFC-231 (the bound), OFC-217 (Ghost 6.0 `limit` cap). Log-tail order: N112 → N113.*

### N114 — The Ghost email-change PUT gains the create path's duplicate-email guard: an email *change* that collides now `422`s on `email`, not a generic `502` (OFC-276)

Book rejected a duplicate email on member **create** (N96/D133 — Ghost's `422` → `GhostDuplicateEmailError` → a `422` field issue on `email`, Option B) but **not** on the member **update** PUT that carries a changed email. An email changed from one non-empty value to another on a brother who keeps his member rides `runEmailGhostLifecycle`'s **update** branch — a single PUT carrying `diff.email`, never modelled as delete-old + create-new — so the create path's collision rejection was never exercised for an email *change*. `updateMember` let *every* PUT error become a generic `GhostStepError("ghost_update_failed")` → `502`; there was no duplicate branch. A latent gap found while debugging OFC-272 (not its cause).

**Verified the empirical unknown first (ghost-staging, 2026-07-17).** The fix hinged on what Ghost's member PUT does on an email collision — unknown at ticket-file time (does it `422` like create, silently allow the duplicate, or something else?). A throwaway probe (create two members, PUT A's email := B's already-held email, observe post-state, clean up) showed Ghost **rejects the PUT with the same `422 ValidationError` a duplicate create gets** ("Member already exists. Attempting to edit member with existing email address", `property: email`) and forms **no** duplicate. So the minimal, create-symmetric fix is correct and no proactive pre-check GET is needed. This also retroactively confirms N96's "must-verify at live-test" duplicate-email shape for **both** the create and the update path.

**Fix (symmetric with create — Forrest's call, the minimal option over a belt-and-suspenders pre-check).** `GhostAdminLifecycle.updateMember` now catches a `GhostHttpError` `422` and — **guarded on the diff actually carrying an `email`** (a name/newsletter-only `422` is not a duplicate-email condition and stays a generic failure — the one refinement over create, which always carries email) — rethrows it as `GhostDuplicateEmailError`, exactly as `createMember` does. `pushGhostUpdate` lets that typed error **propagate** rather than wrapping it in `GhostStepError`, so it reaches the shared `replyWriteError` (unchanged) and maps to the same `422`-on-`email` (Option B), distinct from a transient outage's `502 ghost_update_failed`. The deceased/de-brother paths delete+create (never an email-carrying update), so this touches only the PATCH email-change surface.

Tests (repro-first, watched fail then pass): `ghost-admin.test.ts` — an email-carrying `422` update → `GhostDuplicateEmailError`, while a **non-email** `422` update still throws the raw transport error (the generic-abort path preserved). `ghost-push.test.ts` — `pushGhostUpdate` propagates the collision unchanged (not `GhostStepError`), and `runEmailGhostLifecycle`'s **update** branch surfaces it for an email *change* (→ `422`). Full gate green.

*Extends N96/D133 (create-side Option-B collision handling) to the update path; builds on N65 (Ghost-first gate) and the D98/OFC-232 write-error mapping through `replyWriteError`. Relates OFC-275 (the sibling real-Ghost check, N113). Records to `API-SPEC.md` §3 (`PATCH` errors — collision now covers a *changed* email). Log-tail order: N113 → N114.*

### N115 — One canonical order for the eight privacy/consent switches across the Profile view and edit pages (OFC-278)

The Profile view and edit pages built their privacy-switch UI from independent code, so their orders had drifted apart — a small but real inconsistency for the owner/staff who see both. The edit page (`ProfileEdit.tsx`) ordered the reachability switches Email, **Mailing, Telephone**, Emergency, Spouse and the beyond-brotherhood subgroups **MITAA, PBE News**, Directory listing; the view digest (`ProfileView.tsx` `PreferencesSection`) showed only **five** of the eight — Email, Telephone, Mailing, PBE News, MITAA — omitting the Emergency and Spouse toggles entirely and surfacing Directory listing *only when the record was unlisted*.

Fix: both pages now present the same canonical order — **Email, Telephone, Mailing address, Emergency contacts, Spouse/partner, PBE News, MITAA, Directory listing**. On edit this is two swaps (Telephone before Mailing in the reachability box; the "Emails from PBE News" subgroup before "Sharing beyond the brotherhood"). On view the digest gains the Emergency and Spouse lines — read from the same already-projected `record.privacy` object as the existing three, so no new visibility surface — and Directory listing is now shown unconditionally as `!(record.unlisted ?? false)`, a filled marker when listed and a hollow one when not, mirroring the edit page's always-present "Listed" switch. `PreferencesSection` renders only behind `seesRestricted` (owner/manager/admin), so the always-present Directory-listing line never reaches a regular brother — Forrest's call to show staff *all* toggles for consistency, since regular brothers only ever see these as switches on their own profile.

Purely presentational: no field, projection, validation, or write path changed, and the switch copy still resolves from the help-content registry (N102/N103), so the USER-MANUAL — which describes the switches conceptually, not in visual order — needs no change. No strict-order unit/e2e assertion added (the 6b-5 e2e already guards switch presence/count in Privacy & consent; a positional test would be brittle); verified by the full local gate plus Forrest's staging live-test.

*Extends the consent-toggle chain D45 → … → N107 (OFC-270 relocated Emergency/Spouse into the edit page's Privacy & consent group) by standardizing the *order* across both pages and completing the view digest. Log-tail order: N114 → N115. Later updated by: N117 (OFC-282 swapped the final MITAA/Directory-listing pair back the other way one day later).*

### N116 — The About page: Markdown compiled to HTML at build time, and the "Address Book" naming rule (OFC-244)

Phase 6c-1. The app said nowhere what it is, who to tell when it breaks, who owns the code, or what happens to a brother's data — and the Mixpanel disclosure (D62/D88) existed only on the newsletter side. `/about`, reached from the avatar menu, now carries all four. It sits inside `GateLayout` like every other route: About is members-only, not a public marketing page.

**Markdown compiled at build time (Forrest's call — option 2 of the three in the ticket).** The copy lives in `apps/web/src/content/about.md`; `aboutHtmlPlugin` (vite.config.ts) compiles it with `marked` — a **devDependency**, PR #106 — and exposes the finished HTML as the virtual module `virtual:about-html`. So Forrest edits prose without touching code, and **no Markdown parser ships in the bundle**. The alternative of rendering Markdown in the browser was rejected on bytes: the budget is 250 KB brotli (D74), the bundle sits at ~222 KB, and shipping a parser to every reader — on the slow links this audience actually has — to render one static page is a poor trade. The compiled copy itself costs **1.1 KB brotli** (221.8 → 222.9 KB).

**A virtual module, not a `.md` `transform`.** `.md` is not a type Vite knows how to serve as JavaScript, so a bare transform on a `.md` id is the classic "works in `vite build`, MIME-errors under `vite dev`" trap — and the Playwright suite runs against `build:web && preview`, so e2e would never have caught it. The virtual-module shape behaves identically in both, and `addWatchFile` + `handleHotUpdate` give the copy HMR while authoring. Both paths were verified by hand this session: the dev server returns the module `200 text/javascript` with the right HTML, and an edit to `about.md` is picked up without a restart.

**The first `dangerouslySetInnerHTML` in this repo, and what makes it defensible.** The input is a reviewed file in this repo, never user content or a network response — but "trusted" is a claim, so `compileAboutHtml` **enforces** it and fails the *build* on: a `<script>`, an inline `on*=` handler, a `javascript:` URL, or an off-origin `<img>`/`<iframe>`/`<embed>`. The off-origin guard is not theoretical hygiene: Firebase Hosting serves the SPA under `default-src 'self'` while `vite preview` sends **no CSP headers at all**, so an external asset would pass local e2e and break on staging. The compiler **rejects HTML comments outright** — `about.md` may not contain one, which is why it carries no authoring note and the guidance lives in the new `apps/web/src/content/README.md`. That design was forced by CodeQL and is better than what it replaced. The first cut *stripped* comments so the note could sit atop the copy; `js/incomplete-sanitization` objected, correctly: an **unterminated** `<!--` cannot be stripped (there is no `-->` to match, and looping the replace to a fixed point does not help — both verified empirically), and it would reach the browser as raw HTML and comment out the rest of the page. The second cut stripped *and* threw on the residue, which was safe but left CodeQL still flagging the `replace` (it cannot see the later guard). Banning the construct deletes the entire class rather than sanitizing it, and costs only a comment in one Markdown file. **The general lesson, worth carrying: when a sanitizer cannot be made complete, reject the input instead.** Its sibling alert, `js/bad-tag-filter`, was a genuine-but-inert unit-test smell — a `/<script>/` assertion regex that matched only an `Error` *message* yet read as a case-sensitive tag filter; it now asserts on the message wording, with an added upper-case `<SCRIPT>` case proving the real guard is case-insensitive. Both cleared to keep the repo's standing **0 open CodeQL alerts** (OFC-152) and rejects an `<h1>` (the page renders the only one; a second breaks heading order, WCAG 1.3.1) — first against lexed tokens, so a `#` inside a code fence isn't mistaken for a heading and the error message can be a good one, then against the **rendered output**, because the token scan walks only top-level tokens and a heading nested in a blockquote or list item (`> # Title`) otherwise reaches the renderer. **In-session `/code-review` (high effort) caught that gap, plus a sharper one:** "off-origin" was being decided by an `https?:` prefix in three separate places — `isExternal`, the asset guard, and `AboutPage`'s click delegation — and a **protocol-relative URL (`//host/x`) slipped past all three**, so an off-origin image would have passed local e2e and been CSP-blocked on staging, and a protocol-relative *link* would have been handed to the router as though it were an in-app path. Fixed at the root rather than per-site: one `OFF_ORIGIN_URL` pattern with an **optional** scheme (`/^(?:[a-z][a-z0-9+.-]*:)?\/\//i`) is now the single notion, `AboutPage` mirrors it explicitly (`startsWith("/") && !startsWith("//")`), and each hole has a regression test. External links get `target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"` and an "(opens in a new tab)" accessible name, matching the masthead's PBE News link. Biome's recommended `noDangerouslySetInnerHtml` is turned off **for `AboutPage.tsx` only**, via a file-scoped `overrides` entry in `biome.json` beside the existing `Combobox.tsx` one — Biome cannot suppress a diagnostic raised on a JSX *attribute*, so an inline `biome-ignore` above the element has no effect (it reports `suppressions/unused` while the rule still fires). The reasoning lives in a comment at the call site regardless, and the unit tests are what keep the exemption honest.

`compileAboutHtml` lives at `apps/web/src/buildtime/aboutHtml.ts` — under `src/` deliberately, because that is the one path the vitest include glob, `apps/web/tsconfig.json`, and Biome all already cover, so it is unit-tested, typechecked, and linted with **zero config changes**. ⚠ **Landmine, cost us a near-miss:** it was first written to `apps/web/src/**build**/`, which the root `.gitignore`'s line-6 `build/` rule (meant for build *output*) silently swallowed — `git status` stayed clean, the local gate passed because the files existed on disk, and the branch pushed **without the compiler or its tests**, which would have failed CI on an import of a file not in the repo. The rule is unanchored, so it matches a `build/` directory at *any* depth. Hence `buildtime/`. **Never name a source directory `build` anywhere in this tree**, and treat a suspiciously small `git show --stat` as a signal to run `git check-ignore -v`. ⚠ **It must never be imported by application code**, or `marked` lands in the bundle; only `vite.config.ts` imports it. (Related: **OFC-280** — `vite.config.ts` itself is referenced by no typecheck script, which is why the logic lives in `src/` rather than in the plugin.)

Prose styling is a scoped `.about-prose` rule set in `index.css` written **entirely in existing tokens** (a new token would mean editing the canonical `visual-design/tokens.css` and re-copying, which `assert:tokens` enforces); sizes come from the type scale so the block grows with the font-size control (D131), and links are underlined so they are never signalled by colour alone (WCAG 1.4.1). This project deliberately does not pull in the Tailwind typography plugin for one static page.

**The naming rule (Forrest's call, deferred here from 6b-3).** Member-facing copy says **"PBE Address Book" on first use and "the Address Book" thereafter**; bare **"Book" is internal shorthand only** — code, comments, `CLAUDE.md`, this log. Two stray member-facing strings were fixed: `MaintenanceOutage.tsx` ("The Address Book is temporarily unavailable" — its two e2e assertions updated) and `ProfileControls.tsx`'s delete help + confirmation. ⚠ **Deliberate boundary, do not "fix" it later:** the rule stops at member-facing copy. The **Ghost alignment-audit surface keeps "Book"** as a system name contrasted with Ghost — the card title "Book / Ghost alignment audit", the report's "Book value | Ghost value" columns, "Book-internal orphan" — because the whole point of that admin-only operator output is setting two systems side by side, where "Book | Ghost" scans better than "Address Book | Ghost". The rule has no mechanical guard beyond a unit assertion over `about.md`, so this entry is the only place the boundary is recorded.

**About's copy is its own source, not generated from the USER-MANUAL.** D53's no-drift guarantee is scoped to per-control help text, where one string appears in two places; a short standalone statement of what the app is isn't that, and forcing it through the help registry would distort both. Noted explicitly so a later session doesn't read the overlap with manual §1 as a D53 violation.

**`/brother/me` and `/brother/me/edit` — an identity-free URL for one's own record (Forrest's call, folded in here).** The About copy wanted to *link* a brother to his own profile rather than describe a three-step click path, and couldn't: every profile URL carries a Constitution ID, and build-time Markdown has no session. `OwnProfileRedirect` resolves `me.profileId` from the session and `<Navigate replace>`s to the real `/brother/<id>`. They are **static** sibling routes registered above the dynamic `brother/:id` — the `brother/new` shape exactly — so "me" is never parsed as a Constitution ID. It **redirects** rather than rendering in place, so a record keeps one canonical URL and prev/next (D4d), the back-stack, and link-sharing are untouched; `replace` keeps the alias out of history so Back doesn't bounce off it. The avatar menu deliberately still links the concrete id — it already holds one, and a redirect hop would buy nothing. **The wider motive is Phase 7.6:** the Ghost theme's account links know a member's email but nothing about Book's ids, so this is the URL the newsletter side can point at.

That link exposed a hazard worth recording: injected HTML holds **plain `<a href="/…">`, not router `<Link>`s**, so an internal link would have triggered a **full page reload** — refetching the whole bundle and roster on precisely the slow connections this app is built for. `AboutPage` delegates such clicks to the router with a real DOM listener on the prose container (a `ref` + `useEffect`, not a JSX `onClick` — the handler belongs to the injected subtree, and it also keeps the presentational `<div>` clear of `useKeyWithClickEvents`). Deliberately narrow: only a plain left-click on a *relative*, non-`target` href, so Ctrl/Cmd/Shift-click and middle-click still open a new tab and compiler-marked external links are never intercepted. **Any future page that injects HTML containing internal links needs this same interception** — it is not automatic.

Tests: `aboutHtml.test.ts` (19 units — every guard actually throws, including the protocol-relative, nested-heading, upper-case-`<SCRIPT>` and unterminated-comment cases the code review and CodeQL surfaced; external-link treatment, comment stripping, and the shipped `about.md` compiling and obeying the naming rule) and `e2e/about-6c-1.spec.ts` (5: the avatar-menu link navigates *and closes the menu* — the `closeMenu` wiring regresses silently otherwise; a deep link renders the compiled content, proving the whole build-time chain in the real preview build; the profile link routes **in-app**, asserted by a `window` marker surviving the navigation, with Back returning to About rather than looping through the alias; `/brother/me` resolves to the real record; axe WCAG 2.2 AA). Full gate green.

*Extends the help/guidance chain D53 → D111 → N102 → N103 with the app's first standalone guidance *page* (as opposed to per-control help). Records `/about` to `PRD.md` §5.4's route inventory. Filed during: OFC-280 (build-time TS untypechecked), OFC-281 (USER-MANUAL §8 claims a footer privacy link that does not exist — 6c-2). Log-tail order: N115 → N116.*

### N117 — MITAA moves back below Directory listing on both Profile pages (amends N115, OFC-282)

N115 (the day before) set the canonical eight-switch order ending **…PBE News, MITAA, Directory listing** — but that put MITAA, the one toggle governing sharing *beyond* the brotherhood, ahead of Directory listing, a toggle about visibility *within* it. Forrest flagged the resulting read as odd: the beyond-brotherhood switch sitting in the middle of two brotherhood-internal ones. Fix: swap the last two so the order reads **…PBE News, Directory listing, MITAA** — the two internal-sharing switches (PBE News email, Directory listing) now sit together, with the one beyond-brotherhood switch last on both pages.

On edit (`ProfileEdit.tsx`) this is a straight swap of the "Directory listing" and "Sharing beyond the brotherhood" `Subgroup`s. On view (`ProfileView.tsx` `PreferencesSection`) the `listed` line's `lines.push` moves ahead of the `allowShareWithMITAA` push. No field, projection, or copy changed — pure reorder, same as N115. No strict-order assertion added, for the same reason N115 gave.

*Amends N115 in the consent-toggle chain D45 → … → N107 → N115 → **N117** (current). Log-tail order: N116 → N117.*

### N118 — USER-MANUAL §10 is generated from the help registry, and the gate fails on drift (6c-2)

D53 promised the in-page help and the manual's §10 reference are "one source, not two," and §11 told the reader they "cannot drift apart." Until now that was an intention, not a mechanism: §10 was hand-written during planning and the registry moved on without it. By this session the two had visibly separated — §10 still documented a **Majors** control the app calls **Courses**, carried a *Constitution ID filter* entry the registry never had, and was missing a dozen entries the registry had gained (Columns, Export CSV, the whole privacy/consent switch set with its `whenOn`/`whenOff` copy, the four admin-card descriptions). A promise with no enforcement had decayed exactly as one would expect.

**The mechanism.** `scripts/generate-help-manual.ts` (run by `npm run docs:help`) renders the registry into §10 **in place**, between two marker comments in `USER-MANUAL.md`; `npm run assert:help-manual` runs the same generator in `--check` mode and exits non-zero if regenerating would change the file. That check is wired into `verify:gate` immediately after `assert:tokens` **and into `ci.yml` as its own step** — CI runs the gate's steps individually rather than invoking `verify:gate`, so adding it only to the composite would have left every PR unguarded, which the code review caught. It reads the registry's **TypeScript source** directly via `tsx` rather than the built `dist/`, so it needs no prior `build:libs` and can sit early in both.

⚠ **A gate check must never be able to pass by not running.** The first cut kept `main()` behind an "am I the entry point?" comparison (`fileURLToPath(import.meta.url) === resolve(argv[1])`) so the unit tests could import the pure functions. That guard **fails open**: any path-spelling mismatch — Windows drive-letter case, a symlinked checkout, a wrapper that rewrites `argv[1]` — and the process exits 0 having done nothing, so `assert:help-manual` would report success without comparing anything. The rendering therefore moved to `scripts/lib/help-manual.ts` (pure, no I/O, what the tests import) and the CLI now runs unconditionally. The general rule this instance illustrates: **never make a verification step conditional on something that can silently be false.**

**In place, not a separate generated file (Forrest's call at the 6c-2 plan gate).** The alternative — generating a sibling file the manual points at — would keep the checked-in manual entirely hand-written, but it splits one document across two files for the reader. Markers keep the manual a single reviewable artifact, and the diff of a copy change stays legible in review.

**Grouping is mechanical, not curated.** Entries group by key prefix (`directory.` → Directory, `profile.` → Your profile, `profile.privacy.`/`profile.consent.` → Privacy and consent switches, `admin.` → Administration) and keep registry order within a group, which is authored in on-page order. A key matching **no** group throws rather than being silently omitted — the omission would be precisely the drift this script exists to prevent, and it would be invisible in review. A new key prefix therefore requires a deliberate edit to `GROUPS`.

**Two stale code comments fixed in passing**, both contradicting N103: `types.ts` still described the switch counterfactual as appearing in the `?` popover (it was dropped from there), and `registry.ts`'s header didn't mention the generator. Left alone they would have taught the next session the wrong model.

**Generation exposed a coverage gap it did not cause (OFC-283).** The Directory's **Class Year** and **Constitution ID** filters carry hardcoded `label`/`placeholder` props in `FilterPanel.tsx` rather than registry entries — only the staff and verification filters are wired to the registry. The hand-written §10 had documented both, including the range-and-list syntax (`1980-1989, 1992`); generating §10 drops them, because the registry never held them. So the old manual had been documenting in-page help **the app does not have**, and §3's "the page's own help explains this where you type" is currently false. Filed rather than fixed here: it needs member-facing copy (Forrest's review) and possibly `ControlHelp` support in `NumericFilter`, which would blur the generator PR's review. Recorded because it is the general hazard of this kind of work — *generating a document from a source can silently narrow it, and the loss looks like a clean diff.*

Also not addressed here, deliberately: the generated Administration entries still say "Book" in member-facing help copy ("never changes Book", "Book only holds them"), which the N116 naming rule makes "the Address Book." That copy lives in the registry, so fixing it is a registry edit that regenerates §10 — folded into 6c-2's manual-wide naming pass rather than smuggled into the generator PR. And §11's field table lost its claim that `helperText` "may vary by role" (citing Verification): no registry entry does this and the generated §10 cannot express it, so the claim was checkable and false.

*Extends the help chain D53 → D111 → N102 → N103 → N116 → **N118** (current) with the enforcement D53 always implied. Log-tail order: N117 → N118.*

### N119 — The manual's illustrations are generated by a scripted Playwright harness, deterministically, from fake data (6c-2)

The manual has to photograph a finished app, and the plan called for a scripted harness rather than hand-captured shots (Forrest's call at the 6c-1/6c-2 split). `npm run docs:screenshots` drives the **real production bundle** — `vite preview` over a fresh `build:web`, the same arrangement the e2e suite uses — against network-mocked `/api/*` fixtures, and writes five PNGs into `docs/images/`.

**Why generated rather than captured.** Three properties a hand-taken screenshot cannot have. It is *reproducible* — anyone can re-run it and get the same files. It is *safe by construction* — the roster comes from `tools/fake-data` (Constitution IDs above the #5000 fake floor, `example.test` emails) and the app never reaches a real API, so the public-repo PII rule is satisfied structurally rather than by a reviewer remembering to check. And it is *honest over time*: because the output is byte-identical run to run, a non-empty `git status` after a run means the interface actually moved, which makes stale illustrations detectable instead of merely regrettable.

**Determinism took three fixes, each worth recording** — the first two were caught only by running the harness twice and diffing hashes, which is the test this kind of tool needs:

1. **Animation must be frozen before the first interaction, not before the capture.** The initial cut injected the reduced-motion stylesheet inside the capture helper, i.e. *after* the mobile shot clicked the Options fold open. The fold animated, and the screenshot landed at a slightly different point each run. Motion is now killed via `emulateMedia({ reducedMotion: "reduce" })` before first paint plus a stylesheet applied immediately after `goto`.
2. **The footer's build id had to be hidden.** `PrivacyFooter` renders the deployed commit SHA (with `-dirty` in a working tree). Left visible, every shot would change on every commit — turning the "the UI moved" signal into permanent churn — and the manual would ship a build id that means nothing to a member. Only that one line is hidden; the privacy notice stays.
3. **The subject is chosen from the roster, not synthesized.** The first cut copied a record and forced its id to the documentary exemplar #5247, producing a profile headed "#5247" whose email read `…5002@example.test` — a visible contradiction in a page whose whole job is to illustrate. The subject is now picked *from* the roster and used as-is, so his Directory row and his profile page are the same record. `pickSubject()` also skips the generator's deliberately planted canonical-name collision pair (a "William Evan '19 (#5001)" edge case is the wrong thing to present as the ordinary profile) and requires a plain `brother`, so member-facing sections don't carry a staff badge.

**Not in the CI gate, and deliberately so.** The harness writes files rather than asserting; regenerating the manual's illustrations should be a deliberate act, not something a test run does behind your back. It therefore lives in its own `playwright.screenshots.config.ts` (`testDir: tools/screenshots`), invoked by `npm run docs:screenshots`. The cost of that choice is that image staleness is **not** mechanically caught the way §10's text drift now is (N118) — `docs/images/README.md` carries the standing instruction to re-run after UI changes, which is a weaker guarantee, honestly labelled.

**Full-page for the two content pages** (profile view, Admin), viewport-cropped for the Directory and the phone shot: §4/§5 and §7 walk their pages section by section, and a viewport crop cut the later sections off mid-sentence, whereas the Directory's virtualized grid reads correctly as a window onto a longer list.

⚠ **Screenshots are downstream of copy.** Two registry strings still visible in `admin.png` ("never changes Book", "Book only holds them") are on 6c-2's naming-pass list, and the footer gains a privacy link in the same PR (OFC-281). **Re-run `npm run docs:screenshots` after any copy or chrome change lands**, or the illustrations will contradict the text beside them.

*Extends the help/guidance chain D53 → D111 → N102 → N103 → N116 → N118 → **N119** (current). Log-tail order: N118 → N119.*

*Later updated by: **N120**, which corrects this entry's byte-determinism claim — the phone shot proved bistable at about 1 run in 10 (OFC-284).*

### N120 — The USER-MANUAL is finished against the built app: the footer gains a real privacy link, the numeric filters gain help, and the narrative is corrected to what the app does (6c-2; OFC-281, OFC-283; amends N119's determinism claim)

The manual had been written during planning from the settled design and carried a "Status: draft" banner ever since. This entry closes it: the narrative was walked against the running app, every claim checked, and the illustrations placed. The banner is gone.

**The footer's privacy link is now real (OFC-281).** §8 had told brothers for months that "there is a link to it in the footer at the bottom of every page." There was no such link, and no privacy notice to link to. Forrest's call at the plan gate: make the manual true rather than delete the sentence. `PrivacyFooter` gains **"How we handle your information"** → `/about#privacy`, the section 6c-1's About page already carries.

Three things that "add a link" turned out to require, none of them optional:

1. **It cannot be unconditional.** `PrivacyFooter` renders in three places, and `/about` lives inside the session gate — so on `SignIn` and `MaintenanceOutage` the link would bounce off the gate or dead-end in a degraded app. Hence `withAboutLink`, opt-in, passed only by `AppShell`. §8 now describes exactly this: the standing prose shows to everyone including signed-out, the link appears once signed in.
2. **The anchor did not exist.** `marked` has emitted no heading ids since v5, so `#privacy` would have landed nowhere. `compileAboutHtml` gains a `heading` renderer that slugs every heading — generalized rather than special-casing the one section, so every About section is addressable (7.6's Ghost theme will want this). These ids are now a **public surface**: renaming a heading in `about.md` breaks any link to it, so a unit test pins `#privacy` specifically. The code review then added two build-time guards beside the compiler's existing ones: a heading whose text has no alphanumerics would emit `id=""`, and — worse — two headings that slugify alike would emit **duplicate** ids, where a fragment resolves to the first match and would therefore point the privacy link at the wrong section. Both now fail the build rather than ship a page that quietly misbehaves.
3. **A fragment does not scroll on a client-side navigation.** The browser scrolls to a hash on a full page load; React Router does not. Without a hash effect in `AboutPage` the reader would land at the top of About having clicked a link promising a privacy section. The effect also moves **focus** to the heading, so the jump works for keyboard and screen-reader users rather than only visually (WCAG 2.4.3) — and the e2e asserts the landing, not merely the link's presence, because "the link exists" and "the reader arrives" are different claims and only the second is what §8 promises.

**The two numeric filters gain toggle-tips (OFC-283, Forrest's call).** Class Year and Constitution ID carried hardcoded labels and placeholders and no registry entry, so they had no `?` help — and generating §10 (N118) would have silently dropped the range-and-list syntax the hand-written manual used to document. Forrest: the need was borderline, and *the manual being generated from the registry pushed it over*. `NumericFilter` gains the `helpKey` passthrough `Field` and `DateFilter` already had; the copy is Forrest's, revised from 6b-1. Asterisk emphasis was stripped from it deliberately — the same string renders in two surfaces, and `*1985-1989*` would italicise in §10's Markdown while showing literal asterisks in the popover.

**A landmine the decision log caught.** N118 had listed both `admin.ghostAudit`'s "never changes Book" and `admin.bugReports`' "Book only holds them" as naming-pass items. Re-reading N116 before editing showed that wrong: the Ghost alignment-audit surface **deliberately keeps bare "Book"** as a system name set against "Ghost". Only `bugReports` was changed; a comment now sits beside `ghostAudit` saying not to "fix" it. Recorded because the near-miss is the argument for the convention — the boundary existed in exactly one place, and reading it was what prevented undoing a considered decision.

**Narrative drift found and corrected**, each one a claim that had quietly become false: §4 described the switch counterfactual as living under the "?" (removed in N103 — rewritten to describe what the switch actually states); §4 and §8 spoke of marking yourself "Unlisted" when the control is the positive "Listed in the directory" (N35); §3 called courses "majors"; §2 put Sign out "in the top corner beside your profile icon" when D131 moved it into the avatar menu; §7's Ghost bullet was titled "Sync with Ghost", which is not what the card is called. The whole manual moved to the N116 naming rule — bare "Book" survives only where N116 says it should.

**⚠ Amends N119: the harness is not byte-deterministic after all.** Regenerating the illustrations after these copy changes surfaced it. `directory-mobile-options.png` is **bistable at about 1 run in 10** — the same alternate hash recurring, the two renderings visually identical. Freezing animation earlier had fixed a *more frequent* flake on this same shot; a `waitForStableLayout` (images decoded, document height repeating across three frames) did not fix the remainder, and neither did clipping the shot to remove the virtualized card tail — which at least localizes the cause to the top 600px. Filed as **OFC-284** and documented in `docs/images/README.md` as a labelled exception rather than left as an overstated claim: a diff on that file alone with no visible change is noise; a diff anywhere else is real. The other four reproduce byte for byte across every run measured. The general point worth keeping: **an intermittent imperceptible diff is worse than a consistent one**, because it looks like a real change and trains the reader to commit without looking.

*Extends D53 → D111 → N102 → N103 → N116 → N118 → N119 → **N120** (current). Amends N119's determinism claim. Log-tail order: N119 → N120.*

### N121 — Verification may be confirmed by the owner **or** by staff; an edit by another party clears the mark (records the semantics that kept getting mis-stated)

Recorded because the *rationale* for this has now been written wrongly twice and corrected twice, and the Verification chain (D28 → D48 → D68 → D80 → N73) never said who may confirm — so there was nothing to consult and the wrong explanation kept being reinvented from scratch.

**The semantics, as built.** `POST /api/profiles/{id}/verify` is **owner-or-staff** (N40). `ProfileControls` renders "Confirm my details are current" to the owner and **"Mark as verified"** to a manager or administrator — so staff can deliberately attest a record on a brother's behalf. Separately, and independently, an *edit* saved by someone other than the owner **clears** the verified mark (D28's content-edit coupling): the mark records a deliberate confirmation, not an edit. Both halves are true at once, and the second is not evidence for a restriction on the first.

**The false claim.** Successive drafts explained the clearing behaviour as "only the brother himself can confirm his own details" — a plausible-sounding rationale that flatly contradicts the staff confirm button, and which sat in the USER-MANUAL one sentence away from a correct description of that same button. Forrest caught the contradiction reading the finished manual.

**How it survived a correction — the part worth keeping.** The claim had lived in **four** places: the help registry's `profile.verification` copy, two hand-written USER-MANUAL §10 fields (a manager/admin helper text and a toggle-tip), and the §4 and §6 narrative. The registry copy was fixed in an earlier session, which corrected what a brother actually sees in the app — but the manual's §10 was hand-authored prose holding its own independent duplicate, so the stale wording kept reappearing on every read of the manual. **Generating §10 from the registry (N118) deleted both of those instances automatically**, without anyone asking it to; the two survivors were narrative, which nothing generates and nothing ties to the registry. That is precisely the class of drift D53 was written to prevent, and the clearest evidence so far that generating §10 was worth doing — as well as a standing reminder that **the narrative sections carry no such protection** and must be checked against the code by hand.

*Extends the Verification chain D28 → D48 → D68 → D80 → N73 → **N121** (current). Log-tail order: N120 → N121.*

## Phase 7a planning (2026-07-19, the analytics & observability planning session — "7a-0")

*A discussion-only session that opened Phase 7, surveyed what exists against what the plan asks for, and settled the analytics identity key before any code was written. No application code changed.*

### D137 — Book identifies to Mixpanel by the Ghost member `uuid`, fetched at sign-in and held on the session; `ghostMemberUuid` is **not** persisted (amends D62/D88; leaves D81 unreversed)

D62 named the **email** as Book's Mixpanel `distinct_id`, and D88 reaffirmed it. That is no longer the right key, because the other half of the composite system already moved: **the live pbe400.org integration has keyed on the Ghost member `uuid` since 2026-05-27**, calling `identify(uuid)` and carrying the address separately as an `Email` property. Reality moved and this log did not follow it. Book therefore adopts the **Ghost member `uuid`** as its `distinct_id` too — the change-immune upgrade D62 itself reserved (via D70) for exactly this situation.

**Where the uuid comes from: a Ghost Admin-API lookup at session creation**, keyed on the already-verified email, with the value held on the `Session` record alongside the email it already stores and returned to the SPA by `GET /api/me`. It is **not** written to the `Profile`: **D81 stays unreversed**, `ghostMemberUuid` remains absent from the schema, and no backfill of the ~1,199 existing members is required.

**Why the uuid rather than the email.** Mixpanel stitches a person's actions into one timeline by `distinct_id`. With Ghost saying `uuid-…` and Book saying `fred@example.com`, one brother would be **two Mixpanel users**, and the cross-app paths that motivate a shared project — read an article, cross into the Address Book, look someone up — would break at precisely the seam worth measuring. Identity Merge does not close this on its own: it fires only when one side calls `identify()` across both ids, which the Ghost theme does not do today. Keying both halves the same way is the only option in which one brother is one person permanently, and identity mistakes in an analytics store are expensive to correct once history accumulates.

**Why not read it from the JWT (checked, and it is not there).** `ghost-provider.ts` reads five claims and discards the rest unread, so a `uuid` claim would have been free. Verified empirically against ghost-staging on 2026-07-19: `/members/api/session` mints exactly `sub` (the email), `kid`, `iat`, `exp`, `aud`, `iss`. **No `uuid` claim exists**, so the token cannot supply it.

**Why not persist it (considered, rejected).** Persisting confers exactly one capability a sign-in fetch does not: server-side access to the uuid of members who are **not** currently signed in — wanted only by server-side event tracking or a historical push through Mixpanel's import API, neither of which is on the roadmap. It notably does *not* help the Ghost alignment audit, which already joins on `ghostMemberId`; Ghost's `id` is exactly as stable a join key as its `uuid`, so persisting would add a field and a backfill and improve nothing. And one consideration runs decisively the other way: **D134 deletes a brother's Ghost member when he is marked deceased and re-creates it when that is undone — minting a new `uuid`.** A persisted value would go silently stale at exactly that moment and keep attributing events to a dead identifier, whereas a per-sign-in fetch is self-healing and keeps Book's notion of a person identical to Ghost's at all times. The cheaper option is also the more correct one.

**Accepted residuals.** (1) Sign-in acquires its **first Ghost HTTP dependency** — today it makes zero Ghost calls, resolving identity purely from the verified email against the in-memory profile index. Accepted: a member cannot obtain a magic link at all if Ghost is down, so the dependency is already there in practice. (2) If that lookup fails, the session simply carries no uuid and its events go **unidentified** rather than mis-identified; sign-in itself must never be blocked by an analytics concern. (3) Volume is negligible — sessions last four hours (D22/D125) across ~700 members.

**Not a gap:** roughly a third of brothers have no email and therefore no Ghost member, hence no uuid. They also cannot sign in — Book's sign-in *is* a Ghost magic link — so they are records, never users. Every brother who can produce an analytics event necessarily has a uuid.

**Confirmed after the decision: the email key was not merely worse, it was unrecoverable.** Mixpanel-Prod runs the **Simplified ID Merge API** (verified in the project's settings, 2026-07-19). Under it, `identify()` sets `$user_id`, and an anonymous `$device_id` seen in the same event is folded into that user's cluster with prior anonymous events retroactively re-attributed — but per Mixpanel's own documentation, **"It is not possible to merge 2 `$user_id`s together using the Simplified API"**, and the legacy `alias()` / `$merge` escape hatches are gone. This falsifies D62's stated premise that Identity Merge would "absorb the rare, propagated email change": under the API actually in use, an email change would mint a `$user_id` that could **never** be reunited with the old one, and a Book-on-email / Ghost-on-uuid split would have produced two permanently distinct people with **no repair path** — the damage would have been discovered only once enough history existed to notice, and then been uncorrectable. Both halves must emit an **identical `$user_id`**, which is precisely what this decision mandates. The practical consequence for 7a-2: events emitted before `identify()` are harmless (device-to-user merging is retroactive), but calling `identify()` with the *wrong* key is not.

*Amends the analytics-identity chain D62 → D88 → **D137** (current). Interacts with D81 (uuid capture stays deferred) and D134 (the delete/re-create that makes a persisted uuid stale). Log-tail order: N121 → D137.*

### D138 — Two Mixpanel projects, one per tier; Book ships the `mixpanel-browser` **core** build with session replay and autocapture deliberately off

**Project topology.** Analytics reports to **two** Mixpanel projects: the existing **Mixpanel-Prod** (live since 2026-05-27, currently serving pbe400.org only) and a new **Mixpanel-Staging**. Each project spans *both* halves of the composite system at its own tier — Ghost **and** Book. This **preserves D62's intent rather than reversing it**: D62's "one project" was about not splitting Book from Ghost, which still holds within each tier; what it did not contemplate was staging traffic — including a 2–3 week UAT window with 10–15 testers (D132) — landing in the same dataset as real member usage. Forrest's call: keep the tiers apart. **Consequence:** Ghost-staging reports to nothing today, so the Mixpanel snippet must be added to the Ghost-staging theme for the staging project to mirror prod — folded into **Phase 7.6**, which touches that theme anyway.

**The library.** Book imports the **core** build (`mixpanel-browser/dist/mixpanel-core.cjs.js`), not the package's default entry point. Measured at v2.81.0, bundled and brotli'd the way `check-bundle-size.mjs` measures: the default entry costs **81.6 KB** brotli, the core build **31.4 KB**. The default was never viable against the D74 ceiling; the core build is, with a modest raise that lands in 7a-2 alongside the code that consumes it (per OFC-286's argument that each move of that number should be attributable to a specific change).

**Session replay and autocapture are off, and the core build makes that structural rather than a setting.** This is the part most worth remembering, because re-enabling them will look like a free win to a later session and it is not. **Session replay captures the rendered DOM** — so a single recording of a Directory page would ship other brothers' names, email addresses, phone numbers and postal addresses to Mixpanel as replay data. That is a PII egress the public privacy notice does not cover, and it is exactly what the server-side per-role projection (D5/D82) exists to prevent; it would route protected data around the one enforcement point the whole design rests on. Ghost's newsletter side runs `record_sessions_percent: 100`, which is unobjectionable on public article pages and **must not be copied to Book**. Autocapture is declined on separate and much milder grounds: Book wires its events deliberately (D62's taxonomy), so autocapture would buy only the convenience of not doing so, while broadening what leaves the page for no analytical gain. Choosing the core build means neither feature is present to be switched on by accident.

**The token** is a publishable client-side identifier, not a secret, so it lives in the public repo as an env-specific **build-time define** on the `BOOK_APP_VERSION` / `BOOK_PBE_NEWS_URL` pattern (N94) — prod by default, overridden for staging in `infra/environments/staging.env`. **CSP:** `connect-src` is `'self'` today and must gain the Mixpanel ingestion origin; that edit lands in 7a-2 with the code, and note the CSP hash guard (N54) covers inline *scripts*, which this is not.

*New chain — Analytics delivery: **D138** (current), companion to D137 (identity). Interacts with D62 (one project per tier, not one overall), D74/OFC-286 (bundle ceiling), D5/D82 (why replay is refused), N54 (CSP), N94 (env-specific build defines). Log-tail order: D137 → D138.*

*Later updated by: **D140** — the token defaults to **empty** rather than to production (the N94 pattern inverts for an analytics token); the core build is imported as `mixpanel-browser/src/loaders/loader-module-core`, not `dist/mixpanel-core.cjs.js`; and "neither feature is present" is narrowed to what the bundle actually shows — the rrweb recorder is absent, its plumbing is not, so `autocapture: false` / `record_sessions_percent: 0` are set explicitly and `assert-no-session-replay.mjs` enforces the rest. Built out by **N124**.*

### N122 — Phase 7a splits into 7a-1 / 7a-2 / 7a-3; the survey of what the phase actually inherits

Phase 7a as planned bundled four workstreams — Mixpanel, the three structured log streams, log-based alerting, and the log-reader service account. That is too much for one session, and the halves are near-disjoint in both surface and risk, so 7a splits: **7a-1** the identity foundation (D137's sign-in uuid fetch — `apps/api` identity, session, and `/api/me`); **7a-2** the Mixpanel walking skeleton (`apps/web`, CSP, build define); **7a-3** the three log streams, the audit-stream gaps, and the observability infrastructure — the original 7a's logging half, likely to split again once examined. **Phases 7b and 7c are untouched**, so their Linear labels stay valid. Taxonomy is built walking-skeleton style (Forrest's call): minimal wiring proven end-to-end first, events fleshed out once the infrastructure is seen working.

**What the survey found, so 7a-3 does not rediscover it.** The audit stream (D61/N14) is real and well-wired — profile CRUD, role changes, deceased/verify/de-brother, headshots, impersonation, export, backup download, banner, bug reports — but **D61's event list is not fully honored**: sign-in success and denial emit nothing, JWKS failures emit nothing, and **`"ghost.push"` is declared in the `AuditAction` union with zero call sites**, which reads as covered until grepped. Import and restore have no API route to audit yet. The other two streams barely exist: Fastify is constructed `logger: false`, so **there is no app-side HTTP access log at all**, and there is no diagnostic logger module — only an inline `logType: "error"` writer in the 500 handler plus ad-hoc `console.*` and `process.stderr.write` in five files. And **none of the operational plumbing is provisioned**: `infra/` defines no log sink, no retention bucket, no log-based metrics, no alert policies, and no log-reader service account — despite `audit-log.ts` stating that `logType: "audit"` "is the label that routes this stream to its longer-retention bucket." That routing has never existed.

**One docs-outrun-code gap found and left standing until 7a-2:** `about.md` already tells members the Address Book "uses a standard analytics tool (Mixpanel) to track usage and page views." The app ships **no analytics at all**, so that sentence is currently false. Same species as N121, and closed by 7a-2 landing rather than by editing the copy — the disclosure is what we intend to be true.

*Re-plan note, joining N30 → N39 → N59 → N67 → N62 → D132 → N95 → **N122**. Log-tail order: D138 → N122.*

### D139 — Phase 7.6: Ghost's account-management entry points hand off to Book behind a `book_url` theme setting; Ghost-staging shares the production Mixpanel proxy (implements D132/D138; Forrest's calls throughout)

**The hand-off.** Every account-management entry point in the `pbe-news-ghost-theme` now lands on Book's **`/brother/me/edit`**. A brother's account *is* his Book profile — Book is the system of record for membership and already pushes name, email, and newsletter consent into the Ghost member record — so Ghost's member portal manages nothing he should be editing. Three visible links move (`partials/member-menu.hbs`, `partials/menu.hbs`, `partials/content-cta.hbs`) and **both** account routes move with them: `/account/` and `/membership/` render a shared `partials/book-redirect.hbs` instead of Maali's paid-tier UI, so typing the URL lands where clicking does. The redirect is **unconditional** — signed-out visitors go to Book too, rather than being diverted to Ghost's sign-in — because Book's auth bridge already handles arriving without a session (D20/D104) and one rule is easier to reason about than two branches that diverge in a place nobody looks. `book-redirect.hbs` renders a visible link and redirects *from* it, which buys a no-JS fallback, something to read on a slow connection, and one source of truth for the URL rather than interpolating it into a script context. It then **validates that destination before navigating** — http(s) scheme, different host — because `book_url` is free text with two silent failure modes code review confirmed against Ghost's source: cleared to empty (Ghost stores `''` verbatim; `package.json`'s `default` applies only when the setting record is first created, never as a fallback), which would turn every account link into a same-origin 404 with no recovery path; and a `javascript:` value, which `location.replace` executes. Defence in depth rather than a trust boundary — an admin who can set this already has Code Injection — but it converts both misconfigurations into a link that simply does not auto-navigate. An earlier draft of the partial's comment claimed the link indirection made script injection impossible; that was **false** (Handlebars' HTML escaping does not touch a `javascript:` scheme) and is corrected, because a comment asserting safety is worse than none — it discourages the next reader from adding the check.

**Two entry points found by code review, both invisible from the repo.** Code review (two independent passes) caught that the survey had missed `partials/header.hbs`'s **Upgrade** button — `data-portal="account/plans"`, rendering for every signed-in *non-paid* member, which on PBE News is everyone. Forrest's call: **leave it**, because both Ghost instances already hide it with `display: none` from Code Injection, and it is removed for real by the scaffolding-cleanup ticket (OFC-291) rather than repointed here. Verified against Ghost-staging's live `<head>` rather than assumed — staging carries the identical hiding CSS, so UAT testers will not see it.

That verification then surfaced a genuine defect in this change: the same injected rule hides **`.signup-link`** in order to suppress the real Subscribe button (membership is by invitation), and Maali had reused `signup-link` on the slide-out menu's *Account* button — so one of the three repointed links was hidden as collateral and had never in fact been visible. It now carries `account-link`. Both classes are inert in that context (`.btn.signup-link` is scoped inside `.header`, `.account-link` inside `.member-menu`), so the swap changes no styling, only visibility. **The general lesson is the one worth keeping: Ghost's Code Injection CSS can hide theme markup and is not in the repo, so "the template renders it" does not mean "the member sees it" — check the live `<head>`.**

**The mechanism gotcha, recorded because it is invisible and fatal.** Each repointed link **drops its `data-portal` attribute**. That attribute is what makes Ghost's Portal script intercept the click and open its own overlay — leaving it in place would silently defeat the redirect no matter how correct the `href` was. Any account link added later must leave `data-portal` off. (Noted in passing: `menu.hbs` carried `data-portal="signup"` on its *Account* button, an upstream Maali bug that sent members to Portal's signup screen; now moot.)

**One theme, both tiers.** Which Book a Ghost instance points at is a new site-wide theme setting, **`book_url`** — `https://pbe-book-staging.web.app` on Ghost-staging, `https://book.pbe400.org` at cutover. The alternative was a second, divergent theme copy for staging, which would have made the cutover a theme merge instead of a settings change. **It defaults to production**, and the direction matters: an unconfigured *production* site is then already correct and needs no action during cutover, the moment when attention is scarcest, while an unconfigured *staging* site produces a dead link — loud, obvious, harmless. The reverse default fails the other way, quietly sending real members into staging's fake data.

**Naming reconciliation:** the staging project D138 calls *Mixpanel-Staging* is named **`PBE-Staging`** in the Mixpanel console (token `ec05216fbd33b0caa87779d8292bf9fc`, created 2026-07-19). Same project; the theme docs use the console name, the Book docs use D138's. Noted here so a later session does not go looking for a second project that does not exist.

**Ghost-staging shares `mp.pbe400.org`, unmodified.** Only the project token differs between tiers. This works because Mixpanel routes events to a project by the **token in the payload**, not by hostname, and because the proxy imposes no origin restriction of its own — verified against a `staging.pbe400.org` origin: the CDN path answers `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`, and on the ingestion path Mixpanel's upstream reflects the requesting origin back, which Caddy passes through untouched. **Correction to an in-session misreading:** the `/mp-cdn/*` path appears GCS-backed (`UploadServer`, `X-Goog-*`) but is *not* a local mirror or a pinned snapshot — `cdn.mxpnl.com` returns byte-identical generation, hash, and ETag, so Mixpanel simply hosts its own library on GCS and the proxy is the transparent pass-through the theme docs already described. The accepted cost is that staging's analytics now depend on a production asset; both sites sit on `della2` behind the same Caddy, so it is not a new dependency, but reconfiguring the proxy while debugging staging would take production analytics down with it. A staging-specific proxy is deferred, not rejected.

**The Mixpanel `typeof` guard.** `default.hbs`'s identify/track block now checks `typeof mixpanel !== 'undefined'` before running. The library is loaded by per-instance **Code Injection that lives outside the theme**, an implicit contract nothing in the repo enforces; without the guard an instance missing that snippet throws a `ReferenceError` on every page load for a signed-in member, killing analytics with no visible symptom. That is not hypothetical — it is precisely the state Ghost-staging occupies until the snippet is pasted in, so the guard makes deploy order stop mattering.

**Left for 7a-2 to decide, flagged so it is not rediscovered:** whether **Book** routes through `mp.pbe400.org` as well. The proxy defeats ad blockers only because the request is same-site as the page, and **Book-staging lives at `pbe-book-staging.web.app` — a different registrable domain from `pbe400.org`** — so routing its events through the proxy would buy no ad-blocker benefit while adding a CSP `connect-src` entry and a cross-origin hop. At cutover, `book.pbe400.org` makes the proxy genuinely same-site and it starts earning its keep. Book's `api_host` may therefore want to be environment-specific in the same way D138 makes its token environment-specific.

**Scope, and what was pushed out.** Phase 7.6 executed as **OFC-250 only**. **OFC-251** (Ghost-staging article↔Book cross-links) was completed by Forrest ahead of the session — one brother citation in canonical form, hyperlinked to his Book-staging profile, live-verified — which satisfies the phase gate's article→Book path. **OFC-191** (pre-login home page), **OFC-257** (della2 Node 22) and **OFC-258** (Ghost Admin-API `Accept-Version` v6.0) had been parked on the `7.6` label by an earlier triage on the reasoning that one visit to Ghost's internals should do all Ghost work at once; that batching is reversed here. None of the three is Book-facing, Ghost 6.0 has no announced release date, and the pre-login home page is a newsletter-side concern that UAT does not depend on — so all three lose the label and return to their own scheduling. Maali's unused paid-tier scaffolding (tier picker, Stripe billing controls, Upgrade button) is **left standing**, together with the production Code Injection CSS that currently hides parts of it; removing that scaffolding outright — and moving the Code Injection contents into the theme, which has the same argument behind it — is its own ticket to be done in one pass, post-UAT.

**Deployment stays manual and staging-only.** The theme has no CI/CD; Forrest uploads the zip (filename must remain `pbe-news-theme.zip`, or Ghost loses the design settings tied to the theme name) and pastes the staging Mixpanel snippet into Ghost-staging's Code Injection. `pbe400.org` stays on the pre-Book theme until cutover, so this whole diff is a cutover artifact — see `CUTOVER-PLAN.md`.

*New chain — Ghost↔Book theme integration: **D139** (current), implementing D132 (Phase 7.6 exists) and D138 (Mixpanel per tier). Interacts with D20/D104 (the auth bridge, the other direction of travel), N94 (environment-specific build defines — `book_url` is the theme-side analogue), D5/D82 (why Book's analytics config stays asymmetric with the newsletter's). Log-tail order: N122 → D139.*

*Later updated by: **D140** — the question this entry parked ("whether **Book** uses the proxy at all") is answered **no** for now: Book talks to `https://api-js.mixpanel.com` directly, because Book-staging is a different registrable domain from `pbe400.org` and the proxy's only benefit is being same-site. Adopting it is a cutover item, and the `api_host` define and the CSP `connect-src` origin must move together — see `CUTOVER-PLAN.md`.*

### N123 — 7a-1 as built: the uuid lookup is a narrow second seam on the existing read client, runs last in `createSession`, and is the first Ghost call sign-in has ever made (implements D137)

D137 settled *what* and *why*; this records the four implementation choices it left open, and one thing 7a-1 found that D137 had not anticipated.

**The seam is one method, not a fifth `GhostReader` method.** `GhostMemberLookup { findUuidByEmail(email): Promise<string | null> }` is declared alongside `GhostReader` and implemented by the same `GhostAdminReader`, so there is exactly one Admin-API config and one transport — but the two are separate *interfaces* because their consumers have opposite tolerances. A report surface wants every member and fails closed (`503`/`502`) when Ghost is unreachable; sign-in wants one member, must never block on Ghost, and degrades to a uuid-less session. The narrow declaration is what lets `GhostIdentityProvider` depend only on the capability it uses, and lets its tests supply a two-line fake instead of a live Ghost. It is wired as an **optional** dep, so a deploy with no Ghost Admin API configured still signs members in exactly as before.

**The uuid lives on `Identity`, not `Session`.** It is a fact about *who the caller is*, beside the email it is derived from. The contrast is `effectiveRole`, which sits on `Session` precisely because impersonation is *not* an identity fact. Practically this also means it rides the existing whole-session Firestore serialization with no store change, and it is written as an **omitted key** rather than an explicit `undefined`, which Firestore rejects.

**The lookup runs last, after the nonce is consumed.** Every denial check (unlinked / ambiguous / de-brothered) and `ensureUser` complete first, so by the time Ghost is called the sign-in has already been granted and nothing the call does can change the outcome. This makes the fail-soft property structural rather than merely a `catch` block: a *denied* caller triggers no Ghost request at all, so a rejected sign-in cannot be used to probe Ghost, and there is a test pinning that call count at zero. Both degraded outcomes are logged as structured `WARNING`s (never `ERROR` — the sign-in succeeded), and they are distinguished: "no member at that address" means Book and Ghost disagree about who exists, which is a different fact from "Ghost is broken". Neither log carries the email; sign-in logs are not a PII sink (P10).

**Found in build, and fixed narrowly: `GhostAdminHttp` had no timeout at all.** No `AbortController`, no `signal` — every Ghost Admin-API call Book makes, read and write, waits indefinitely on a half-open connection. On an admin report that is merely slow, with a human watching; on the sign-in path it would hang the magic-link callback until Cloud Run's request timeout, which would have made D137's "fail soft" false in exactly the scenario the residual was written for. A bounded wait is therefore not a nicety here but a precondition of the decision. `request` gained an **opt-in** `timeoutMs`, set only on this call (3s); the report and write surfaces keep their long-standing unbounded behavior, with a test pinning that asymmetry so it cannot be changed silently, and **OFC-294** carries the question of whether they should adopt a bound too.

**Two encoding traps, both verified against Ghost's docs rather than assumed.** The NQL filter wraps the email in **single quotes** unconditionally: an unquoted `+` is NQL's AND operator, so `fred+news@example.test` would parse as two clauses and silently match nothing — a wrong answer, not an error. `URLSearchParams` supplies the required percent-encoding (`+` → `%2B`). Ghost's own docs confirm both halves are needed; OFC-275 is the standing reminder that a bad filter fails against real Ghost while every unit test passes, so the wire query string is asserted directly in tests.

The second trap was **caught in code review, not in the build**: quoting alone is insufficient, because `'` is itself valid RFC 5322 atext. `o'brien@example.test` is an ordinary address a fraternity roster will eventually contain, and unescaped it *terminates the NQL string after the `o`*. Ghost's filter documentation states that a quote inside a quoted string must be escaped; the value is therefore backslash-escaped, with the **backslash doubled first** (escaping the quote first would yield a `\'` that the backslash pass then turns into `\\'`, re-exposing the quote). The severity is asymmetric and that is why this is escaped at the string level rather than left to Ghost to reject: the benign outcome is a `400` and a brother who is silently never identified, but the malign one is a mangled filter matching a **different** member, whose uuid would be adopted as this caller's `$user_id` — and under Simplified ID Merge that misattribution is **unrecoverable**. The lesson generalizes past this call site: the quoting rule and the escaping rule are separate requirements, and satisfying the first reads as if it satisfied the second.

*Implements **D137** in the analytics-identity chain D62 → D88 → D137 → **N123**. Interacts with D104 (the handshake this appends a step to), D97 (the verified, normalized email it keys on), D81/D134 (why nothing is persisted), and D95 (`/api/me` stays `no-store`). Spawned OFC-294. Log-tail order: D139 → N123.*

## Phase 7a-2 (2026-07-20, the Mixpanel walking skeleton)

### D140 — Three corrections to D138, made in the build: the analytics token defaults to **empty**, the core build is imported by its documented specifier, and Book talks to Mixpanel directly (resolves the question D139 left open)

D138 settled the shape of Book's Mixpanel integration and 7a-2 built it. Three of its particulars did not survive contact with the code, and each is amended here rather than quietly diverged from.

**1. The token defaults to empty, not to production.** D138 put the token on N94's build-define pattern — "prod by default, overridden for staging" — and that rule is correct for what N94 governs. `BOOK_PBE_NEWS_URL` is a link: defaulting to production means an unconfigured production build is *already right*, and the failure mode of a wrong value is a dead link somebody notices and nobody is harmed by. **An analytics token inverts both halves of that argument.** There is today no `prod.env` and no production deploy workflow — only `staging.env` and `deploy-staging.yml` exist — so the only builds that would actually pick up a production default are local dev builds and CI. And CI is not a bystander here: Playwright builds the real production bundle and drives it through the whole app on every `verify:gate` run. A production-defaulting token would therefore write synthetic events into Mixpanel-Prod — the dataset carrying real members' usage since 2026-05-27 — on every gate run, and analytics history is precisely the kind of thing a later cleanup cannot undo. `BOOK_MIXPANEL_TOKEN` therefore defaults to **the empty string**, which disables analytics outright; `staging.env` carries the staging token, and the production token is added when the production deploy path is built (OFC-253, recorded in `CUTOVER-PLAN.md`). **The accepted cost is real and stated plainly:** a production build that is never told its token ships with analytics silently off. That failure is quiet, which is the argument against it; it is also harmless and repairable, which is why it wins over a failure that is equally quiet and permanent.

**2. The core build is imported as `mixpanel-browser/src/loaders/loader-module-core`.** D138 named `mixpanel-browser/dist/mixpanel-core.cjs.js`, measured at 31.4 KB brotli. Both files exist in v2.81.0 and both work — the package publishes no `exports` map, so the deep dist import is legal — but the loader is the specifier Mixpanel's own README documents for "the core SDK with no option of session recording", and being ESM source rather than a pre-bundled CJS blob, Rollup can tree-shake through it. Measured on this branch against a 223.8 KB baseline: the loader adds **30.5 KB**, the dist file **31.2 KB**. Documented *and* smaller, so the undocumented path had nothing left arguing for it.

**3. Book talks to Mixpanel directly; the proxy waits for cutover.** D139 explicitly left for 7a-2 the question of whether Book routes through `mp.pbe400.org`. It does not. The proxy defeats ad blockers only by being same-site as the page, and Book-staging at `pbe-book-staging.web.app` is a different registrable domain from `pbe400.org` — so adopting it today would buy no ad-blocker benefit while adding a cross-origin hop and a second CSP entry. `connect-src` therefore gains exactly `https://api-js.mixpanel.com`, which is `mixpanel-browser`'s own `DEFAULT_CONFIG` value read from source rather than inferred from the theme's proxy rules. At cutover `book.pbe400.org` makes the proxy genuinely same-site and worth adopting; the `api_host` define and the `connect-src` origin must then move **together**, and `CUTOVER-PLAN.md` says so, because moving one without the other fails as a CSP violation rather than as anything legible.

**A fourth particular, corrected rather than amended: what the core build actually excludes.** D138 says choosing it "means neither feature is present to be switched on by accident." Verified against the built bundle, that is true of session replay in the way that matters and looser than stated in the way that doesn't. The rrweb recorder *implementation* is genuinely absent — zero occurrences of `rrweb`, `rrdom` or `MixpanelRecorder` — so replay cannot record. But the recorder *plumbing* remains (a `recorderManager`, an `autocapture` object that is constructed and initialised, and the config keys `record_sessions_percent` / `start_session_recording`), with no payload behind it. Two consequences. First, `init()` passes `autocapture: false` and `record_sessions_percent: 0` **explicitly**, as documentation-in-code that survives a library upgrade changing a default, rather than relying on the build's shape. Second, the claim is now enforced instead of asserted: `scripts/assert-no-session-replay.mjs` joins `verify:gate` and fails the build if the recorder reappears — modelled on D108 layer 3, and matching on the rrweb markers rather than on the config-key strings, which are present in a *correct* bundle and would make the check fail against the very thing it is meant to bless.

*Amends **D138** in the analytics-delivery chain D138 → **D140** (current). Resolves the `api_host` question D139 parked. Interacts with N94 (whose default-to-production rule this deliberately inverts for one define, and only for this one), D74 (the ceiling raised alongside), D88 (`ignore_dnt` retained), and D108 (the assertion pattern borrowed). Log-tail order: N123 → D140.*

### N124 — 7a-2 as built: the analytics seam holds no Mixpanel code, page views key on route `handle` metadata, and the D74 ceiling rises to 270 KB

**The seam splits logic from library, for a testing reason that turned out to be structural.** `lib/analytics.ts` holds every decision — when to identify, what may ride an event, how a result count is bucketed — and imports nothing from `mixpanel-browser`. `lib/analyticsClient.ts` imports the library, builds a four-method client, and registers it; `main.tsx` is the only caller. The immediate motive was testability: `mixpanel-browser` touches `window` at module scope and the SPA's unit tests run under Vitest's **node** environment with no jsdom, so a static import anywhere in the logic path would have made the whole module untestable and pushed the P6 rules out to Playwright, where they would be checked by observation rather than by assertion. The shape is the same seam `api.ts` already uses for its 401 handler. The side benefit is the one worth keeping: **until a client is registered every analytics call is a no-op**, so a token-less build — local dev, CI, e2e — is not "analytics that fails" but "analytics that isn't there", with no error path to reason about.

**The import stays static on purpose, and the reason is counter-intuitive enough to be worth a comment in the file.** Lazily importing Mixpanel only when a token exists would keep 30 KB out of token-less builds, which looks like a pure win. It is not: CI builds without a token, and `check-bundle-size.mjs` measures what CI builds — so the lazy version would make the D74 ceiling stop measuring the bundle members actually receive. A budget that no longer measures the shipped artifact is worse than a slightly larger dev bundle.

**Page views key on route `handle` metadata, not on a parsed pathname.** Each route in `App.tsx` declares `handle: { analyticsRoute: "/brother/:id" }`, and the hook reports the deepest declared pattern. The alternative — deriving a pattern from `useLocation().pathname` with a regex — would work and would be one file smaller, but it leaves a live code path from a URL to an event property; one bad regex and `/brother/5247` ships. With handles, the set of *app-authored* strings that can reach Mixpanel is the set written in the route tree. ⚠ **That is necessary but not sufficient, and the first draft of this entry wrongly claimed otherwise** — the library attaches `$current_url` on its own, which is what **N125** corrects; read the two together. Mixpanel's own `track_pageview` option is separately disabled (it would fire a second, URL-bearing pageview event of its own). Page views fire only when authenticated, so the sign-in screen is not filed under `/`, and dedupe is on `location.key` — never sent, only compared — so re-renders and StrictMode's double-invoked effects don't double-count while a genuine `/brother/1` → `/brother/2` navigation still counts twice.

**`reset()` on sign-out is unconditional, and the uuid-less session is the case that needs it most.** The obvious reading is that a session which never identified has no identity to drop. The opposite is true: `reset()` regenerates the *anonymous device id*, and leaving a stale one in place on a shared or family machine — this audience skews 60+ and shares computers — would let the next brother's `identify()` retroactively absorb the previous brother's anonymous events into his own timeline, since Simplified ID Merge back-fills a device's anonymous history onto the user. That misattribution is unrecoverable (N123). Reset therefore fires on **both** routes out of a session: the sign-out button, and N76's central 401 interceptor when a session lapses mid-use.

**The one feature event is `Search Performed`, carrying a bucketed match count and nothing else.** No query text, no matched ids: what a brother typed and whom it matched are the two things P6 exists to keep out. The count is bucketed (`0` / `1` / `2-10` / `11+`) rather than exact because "exactly 1 result, at this instant, for this identified brother" is a sharper hint at *who was looked up* than the event needs to answer the question it exists for — does search find people, or come back empty? It fires once the query has been unchanged for a second and the name-search worker has settled, so typing "smith" reports one search rather than five; the query text is held in a ref solely to avoid reporting the same search twice, and is compared, never sent. ⚠ The **count** and the **firing conditions** were all three wrong in the first draft and are corrected in **N125** — the short version is that it counted post-filter rows rather than search matches, and cancelled itself in exactly the cases where the search had succeeded.

**The D74 ceiling rises 250 → 270 KB, in this PR, attributable to this change** (the OFC-286 rule). Measured: 223.8 KB before, 254.5 KB after — so the old ceiling was not tight but *exceeded*, and the raise was a precondition of the feature rather than housekeeping. 270 KB restores roughly the working margin 250 KB used to give. Forrest's note on the record: the 250 KB was an arbitrary forcing function chosen to require a conversation before the bundle grew again, and it did its job. Phase 7b's Lighthouse baseline (OFC-286) is where the number should next be re-derived from evidence.

**Two configuration choices worth naming.** `ignore_dnt: true` is carried over from D88 — but note it is **not** a default: `mixpanel-browser`'s `DEFAULT_CONFIG` sets it `false`, so D88's "retained" only stays true by being written down in `init()`. And persistence is switched to `localStorage` from the default cookie: a cookie rides every same-origin request, and this audience is on slow links with many `/img/*` fetches per page, so the default quietly taxes exactly the constraint the whole project optimizes for.
