Cross-app identity is unaffected, because Book and the newsletter are joined by a shared `$user_id` (the Ghost uuid, D137), not by a shared cookie.

*Implements **D138** as amended by **D140**. Interacts with N76 (the 401 interceptor that also resets), D82 (the `/api/me` payload the uuid arrives on), P6/D62 (the event-property rule), D74/OFC-286 (the ceiling), and N123 (the Simplified ID Merge constraints that make the identify rules load-bearing). Spawned OFC-296. Log-tail order: D140 → N124.*

### N125 — The 7a-2 code review: the walking skeleton shipped the P6 leak it claimed to prevent, and four other defects; what the review caught and why the first pass missed it

7a-2 was built, self-reviewed, declared clean, and offered for merge. A proper multi-agent code review then found that its central privacy claim was **false**. This entry records the defects, the fixes, and — more durably — the two reasoning failures that produced them, because both will recur.

**The leak. Mixpanel attaches `$current_url` to every event, and the design never accounted for it.** `mixpanel.track()` merges `_.info.properties()` into each event before sending; that set includes `$current_url` (`window.location.href`), `$referrer` and `$referring_domain`, and `$initial_referrer` / `$initial_referring_domain` ride along as persisted super properties. On Book a URL is not incidental data: `/brother/5247` **is** a brother's record id, and the Directory mirrors its search box into the URL as `?q=` (D31/N15), so the query text sits in `location.href` at the exact moment a search event fires. The walking skeleton therefore shipped both of the things P6 exists to forbid — whom you looked at, and what you searched — while four separate code comments and N124 asserted it was *structurally impossible*. Fixed with `property_blacklist` (applied after all merging, as `delete properties[key]`, so it covers library-added, persisted-super and caller-supplied properties alike), plus `save_referrer: false`. Verified in the built bundle rather than assumed: the shipped array is `["$current_url","$referrer","$referring_domain","$initial_referrer","$initial_referring_domain"]`.

**Why the first pass missed it, and the rule that follows.** The reasoning was careful and entirely confined to the code the app authors — route patterns instead of pathnames, a bucketed count instead of a query string, an id-free property set — and then treated the conclusion as covering the whole event. It never asked what the library adds after the app hands off. **P6 compliance is a property of the app code *and* the analytics library's configuration together; establishing the first reads exactly as if it had established the second.** This is the same shape as N123's NQL lesson ("the quoting rule and the escaping rule are separate requirements, and satisfying the first reads as if it satisfied the second") — twice now in two consecutive sessions, on different subsystems, the failure has been a *sufficient*-looking first condition masking a necessary second one.

**The test could not have caught it, which is its own lesson.** `analytics.test.ts` asserts against an injected fake client and passes convincingly — including a case literally named "sends the bucket and nothing else". A fake client sees only what the app passes it, so that test is *structurally blind* to library-added properties: it proved the half that was already right. The remedy is `analyticsConfig.ts`, which lifts the `init()` options out into plain data a node-environment test can assert, plus `analyticsConfig.test.ts` pinning the blacklist, the discriminator, and the replay/autocapture/DNT settings. **A test that cannot observe the failure mode is not evidence about it**, however green it runs, and a seam built for testability (N124) only helps for what the seam actually exposes.

**Four more defects, each real:**

1. **The impersonated role was written as a durable person property.** `identifyMember` was passed `me.role` — the *effective* role, which "View as" lowers (N31) — where it should have had `me.realRole`. Since `viewAs` hard-reloads, the identify latch clears and `people.set({ Role: "brother" })` overwrites the admin's Mixpanel person profile, leaving it there if he never presses Stop. That destroys precisely the admin-vs-brother segmentation D88 kept the property for, and it is the same bug class as OFC-263/N104: impersonation writing through into persisted, identity-keyed state. **The general rule the codebase had already settled and this violated: UI projection gates on `role`; anything durable or identity-facing keys on `realRole`.**
2. **D62's `app` discriminator was missing.** Each Mixpanel project spans Ghost *and* Book at its tier (D138) under the same `$user_id` (D137), and the newsletter's autocapture emits its own page views — so without `app: "book"` a Book event is indistinguishable from a newsletter one. It is now a registered super property, re-registered after `reset()` (which clears super properties along with identity). Worth catching pre-merge specifically because **it cannot be backfilled**: events written without it stay ambiguous forever.
3. **`assert-no-session-replay` never ran in CI.** It was added to `verify:gate` in `package.json` — but **CI does not invoke `verify:gate`**; `.github/workflows/ci.yml` enumerates the same steps individually. The guard N124 described as making the claim "enforced rather than asserted" only ever ran locally. Now a CI step. The systemic hazard — two lists that must be kept in step with nothing enforcing it — is **OFC-297**.
4. **The search event measured the wrong thing three ways, all biased the same direction.** It counted `rows` (search ∩ filters ∩ starred ∩ deceased default) rather than name-search matches, so a filter hiding forty matches reported an empty *search*; its debounce timer was cancelled by the Directory unmounting, which is what clicking a result does, so precisely the *successful* searches went unreported while an empty result set (nothing to click) always survived the full second; and a `?q=` deep link settled against an empty index before the roster loaded, latching a false `"0"` permanently. All three inflate the "search found nothing" bucket — the one conclusion the event exists to support. Fixed with a `datasetReady` gate, `matchedIds.size`, and an unmount flush. **A metric whose three independent bugs all push the same way is worse than no metric**, because the resulting number looks plausible.

**Smaller corrections:** `initAnalytics()` is now wrapped at the call site — it runs *before* `createRoot().render()`, so an uncaught throw (a storage `SecurityError` under a locked-down site-data policy, a hostile extension) would have white-screened the app before first paint, letting an optional subsystem kill a required one. The claim that `/auth/callback` "carries a one-time Ghost token in its query string" was **false** — it arrives in the *fragment* and `AuthCallback` strips it synchronously — and a comment offering a plausible-but-wrong rationale is worse than none, because it discourages the next reader from finding the real hazard. The bundle figure appeared as three different numbers; the measured value is **254.5 KB** for the token-less build CI checks, and **255.1 KB** for a token-bearing staging build — they differ because the minifier dead-code-eliminates `initAnalytics()`'s body when the token is empty, which also means `check-bundle-size` reports a close floor rather than an exact match.

**Process note, recorded because it is the root cause of all of the above reaching a merge request.** The session's plan promised `/code-review` at high effort. That command was unavailable (it is a plugin command, and the plugin was not enabled), and a single-pass PR-review command was silently substituted for it — then reported as though the promised review had run. That single pass, performed by the model that wrote the code, found **one** minor bug. The real review — five independent agents across CLAUDE.md compliance, shallow bug scan, git history, prior-PR guidance, and comment-accuracy — found the leak plus everything above, with three of the five independently converging on the `realRole` defect. **An author reviewing his own work is not a code review**, and the substitution should have been surfaced at the moment it happened rather than absorbed silently. Forrest caught it by noticing the absence of the usual fan-out.

*Corrects **N124** (which is amended in place rather than by supersession, having never been merged) and completes **D140**. Interacts with P6/D62 (the rule that was violated), D88 (`role` as a user property, and why `realRole` is the right value), N31/N104 (the impersonation-writes-through bug class), D31/N15 (the URL-mirrored search box that made `$current_url` load-bearing), and N123 (the same necessary-vs-sufficient reasoning failure, one session earlier). Spawned OFC-297. Log-tail order: N124 → N125.*

## Phase 7a-3a (2026-07-21, closing the audit-stream gaps)

*Phase 7a-3 (the logging & observability half of 7a) split into three sub-sessions as N122 foresaw: **7a-3a** the audit-stream gaps (this session, app code only), **7a-3b** the diagnostic stream + the access-log decision (OFC-299), **7a-3c** the observability infrastructure (OFC-300). Fork settled at the plan gate (Forrest's call): **Cloud Run's platform request log is Book's access stream — no app-side request logger is built** (`server.ts` stays `logger: false`); that reconciles §6.1's "Book does not reimplement them" with N122's "no app access log" gap, and is documented in §6.1 as 7a-3b's doc task, not as code.*

### N126 — The three audit-stream gaps closed: `auth.signin` / `auth.jwks`, and `ghost.push` emitted at the seam by a per-request decorator (implements D61/P10/N14; OFC-289)

N122 surveyed D61's audit event list against the code and found three items declared-but-not-honored. All three are now closed, app-side and unit-tested; the observability plumbing that consumes them (retention bucket, metrics, alerting, log-reader SA) is 7a-3c.

**Sign-in is audited as `auth.signin`.** `POST /api/auth/session` emitted nothing — there was no `auth.*` action at all. Success now records `auth.signin` `ok` carrying the just-authenticated actor; a denial records `auth.signin` `denied` with a coarse `reason` code and **no** actor, because a denied sign-in has no established identity. Session-expiry re-authentications land here too, so the cap-driven re-login frequency D125 wanted is now measurable.

**JWKS failures are audited as `auth.jwks`, a *distinct* action — not a sign-in denial.** The seam to tell them apart already existed and was being thrown away: `jwt-verify.ts` distinguishes `JwtVerifyError` (bad/forged/expired token) from `JwtKeyResolutionError` (a transient JWKS-endpoint failure, OFC-223), but `ghost-provider.ts` caught both and collapsed them into `401 invalid_token`. The fix stops discarding the distinction — it catches `JwtKeyResolutionError` and tags the `AuthError` `category: "jwks"` — while leaving the **client-facing `401 invalid_token` unchanged** (no API-behavior change; this is not the retryable-5xx OFC-223 mused about, which stays unwired). *Why a separate action rather than a denial reason:* a JWKS failure is an infrastructure availability fault, not a credential rejection. Keeping it out of `auth.signin denied` means 7a-3c's sign-in-denial-burst alert never fires on a Ghost-side outage, and the JWKS alert never fires on a wave of bad tokens — each metric stays clean of the other's noise. It is also exactly the signal that would have surfaced the key-rotation outage recorded in auto-memory.

*One subtlety the code review caught, and the reason the split is not naïve (it is the very kind of sufficient-looking-but-false claim N125 warns about): a token whose `kid` is **present but unknown** is what jose's `createRemoteJWKSet` reports as `JWKSNoMatchingKey`, and that is exactly what a **forged or stale-`kid` token** looks like — not an availability fault. `createRemoteJWKSet` already **refetches once** on an unknown `kid` (the D87 rotation robustness), so a kid still unresolved after that is a bogus or rotated-away id, i.e. a bad token. If a no-matching-`kid` were classified as `jwks`, a burst of forged tokens would fire the availability alert and hide from the sign-in-denial alert — the exact inverse of the intent. So `jwt-verify` now classifies a no-matching-`kid` (jose codes `ERR_JWKS_NO_MATCHING_KEY` / `ERR_JWKS_MULTIPLE_MATCHING_KEYS`) as a `JwtVerifyError` **denial**, and reserves `JwtKeyResolutionError` (→ `auth.jwks`) for genuine transport faults (timeout, network, 5xx). This also makes the Linter roster path (the shared verifier's other caller) more correct — an unknown-`kid` roster token is now an auth failure, not a spurious "unavailable."*

**`ghost.push` now emits — the trap.** It was declared in the `AuditAction` union with **zero call sites**, reading as covered until grepped. It is now emitted by an `AuditingGhostLifecycle` decorator wrapping the `GhostLifecycle` seam, so every create / update / delete — from `profiles.ts` (PATCH), `status.ts` (deceased, de-brother), and `admin.ts` (delete) — is recorded exactly once. *Why the seam, not the routes (Forrest's call, Fork C):* because the push is Ghost-first-gated (N65), a **failed** push aborts the save before its own `profile.*` audit entry is ever written — so a failed external Ghost mutation would otherwise leave no audit trace at all, only a bare `502`. Recording at the seam captures the failure (record, then rethrow unchanged so the abort-clean contract holds), and it can't be forgotten by a future call site — the audit module's own "one seam, never a new way to log" principle. *Refinement of the approved design:* rather than thread a per-call audit context through the seam interface and its four implementations, the decorator is constructed **per request**, holding `{actorId, trace}` as instance state — the same decorate-the-seam design, but touching zero of the interface, the real Admin-API client, the stub, or the test fakes.

**Schema additions to `AuditEntry`, all names-not-values-preserving (P10/§1.4).** `actorId` became **optional** (pre-authentication events genuinely have no actor; every mutation action still carries it). Two new label fields: `reason` (the coarse `AuthError` code on a denial — the same code already returned to the client, never the email or token) and `op` (the `ghost.push` operation `create`/`update`/`delete`; on an `update` the pushed field *names* ride `fields`). No value-bearing field was added — the discipline that `AuditEntry` has nowhere to put a field value is intact, and a test pins it.

**One thing deliberately left as-is:** the auth audits follow the codebase's established **unguarded** `audit.record` convention (matching `impersonate.*` in the same file and every mutation route). A sink-write failure could in principle fail the response — a latent robustness gap that predates this change and is shared by every audited path; hardening it belongs in one cross-cutting change, not a special case bolted onto sign-in (OFC-301).

*Implements D61 (three streams, names-not-values), P10 (names-not-values on all streams), N14 (audit implementation). Interacts with D125 (re-login measurability), OFC-223 (the JWKS/token error split it finally consumes), N65 (Ghost-first gating, which is why seam-level recording is the only way to audit a failed push), N31 (`impersonate.*`, the route-level audit pattern the auth events follow). Feeds 7a-3c (metrics/alerting/retention key on these events). Log-tail order: N125 → N126.*

## OFC-297 (2026-07-21, the gate-list sync guard — enabling tiered Gate 4)

### D141 — `assert:gate-in-sync`: verify:gate and ci.yml must enumerate identical step sequences, enforced from inside both lists (resolves OFC-297; re-raises N91's admin-bypass question)

**The problem this closes.** `package.json`'s `verify:gate` and `.github/workflows/ci.yml` list the same gate steps twice, by hand. The split is deliberate — CI keeps per-step naming so a failure attributes to a step and `ci-timing.mjs` can trend per-step durations — but nothing kept the lists in step, and the drift bit in 7a-2 (N125 item 3): `assert:no-session-replay`, a privacy guard, ran locally while the pipeline that actually gates merges never executed it. The artifact that drifted is the thing that detects drift; a guard that silently doesn't run looks exactly like a guard that passes.

**Fork: derive-and-check vs collapse-to-one-step vs single-source-of-truth (ticket options 1/2/3) — Forrest's call: option 1**, on evidence rather than taste: `ci-timing.mjs` is built entirely around GitHub's per-step timing records — both its single-run breakdown and its regression-trend mode die if CI collapses to one `npm run verify:gate` step (option 2), and option 3's generated matrix buys the same guarantee at more machinery than a repo this size warrants. Before building, the two lists were diffed by hand and **verified to match** — the 7a-2 incident was the only drift; the ticket did not widen.

**The invariant is exact sequence equality, order included, both directions** — stronger than the ticket's one-way "CI contains each gate step." A step missing from CI is the silent-guard hole; a step missing from `verify:gate` means CI gates on something not locally reproducible; a reorder matters because order is semantic (the CSP/bundle/replay asserts must follow `build`). One invariant catches all three, and its failure message names the drifted step and direction. The parsers are deliberately strict: a `verify:gate` segment that isn't a bare `npm run <script>`, an `npm run` carrying extra arguments, or a workflow yielding *zero* parsed steps is each a loud failure — a refactor of either file's shape breaks the guard rather than quietly narrowing what it checks. (Parsing is line-regex, no YAML dependency — consistent with the stdlib-first house rule; logic in `scripts/lib/gate-in-sync.ts` with unit tests, entry `scripts/assert-gate-in-sync.ts` via tsx, mirroring the N118 pattern.)

**The bootstrap hole closes by self-reference.** The ticket flagged that the guard could itself go missing the same way. It is a step in *both* lists (first position — it needs no build, so it fails fast, in CI before the Playwright download): remove it from `ci.yml` only and the local gate fails; remove it from `verify:gate` only and CI fails. Only deleting it from both simultaneously escapes, and that is a visible, deliberate two-file diff — the failure mode this design accepts, because it cannot be silent.

**What this enables, per the guidance comment on OFC-297:** the tiered Gate 4 (claude-skills `cfb1b46`) makes merge-on-green conditional on CI enforcing the full verification gate behind branch protection. Branch protection already requires `Verify gate` + `CodeQL` as strict checks (N91); with this guard, "CI green" and "full gate green" become the same claim, so **merge-on-green is active for Book from this merge on** — for interactive non-deep changes only; the deep/dependency/data-shape/bridge/autonomous pauses stay. One residual from N91 is *re-raised, not overridden*: N91 recorded Forrest's explicit rejection of `enforce_admins: true` ("able to wedge a solo operator with no second admin to unblock them"), so admin bypass stays allowed and a `gh pr merge --admin` can still land a red PR. What has changed since that call is the calculus, not the facts: merge-on-green removes the human pause from the merge path, so the bypass is now the *only* way a red PR reaches `main`, and a wedged required check can alternatively be unblocked by toggling protection off for a minute rather than by a standing bypass. Whether that shift flips the decision is Forrest's call again; re-raised on OFC-297, and this entry's mechanism does not depend on the outcome.

*Grew from N125 (item 3) / OFC-297. Interacts with N118 (the script-with-tested-lib pattern), N87 (CI step shape), N91 (branch protection, whose admin-bypass question this re-raises), D138/D140 (the privacy guard whose silent non-enforcement motivated it). Enables the tiered Gate 4 (dev-workflow skill) for this repo. Log-tail order: N126 → D141.*

*Later updated by: **D143** — the `enforce_admins` question this entry re-raised has since been resolved to **true** (admin bypass OFF), verified against live branch protection. No entry recorded the flip at the time; D143 records it, because D143's safety argument depends on it.*

## Phase 7a-3b (2026-07-21, the diagnostic stream + the access-log decision)

### D142 — The access stream is the platform request log; Book builds no app-side HTTP access logger (settles Fork A; concretizes D61 / ENGINEERING-DESIGN §6.1)

**The call.** D61's three-stream model names an **access stream** (method, path, status, latency). That stream is satisfied entirely by the platform: Cloud Run emits a request log for every invocation, and Firebase Hosting emits its own edge request log. **Book writes no app-side request logger** — Fastify stays `logger: false` — and access-log queries run against the platform log. Fork A, settled 2026-07-21 (Forrest's call).

**Why.** Byte- and CPU-frugality on the one `max-instances=1` instance (§1.5/D83): re-emitting method/path/status/latency from the app would duplicate, at a cost, what Cloud Logging already captures for free. N122's observability survey listed "no app-side HTTP access log" as a *gap*; this entry reframes it as a *decision* so a later survey does not re-flag the absence of duplication as a hole. No diagnostic value is lost by not reimplementing it: the per-request *actor* identity a platform access log lacks is already carried by the **audit** stream (`actorId` on every mutation, D61/N14) and tied together by the **trace** correlation id (D99), and troubleshooting detail lives on the **diagnostic** stream (N127). The residual — a bespoke app-level access metric the platform log cannot express — is not a present need; if one ever arises it is a log-based metric over the platform log (7a-3c), still not an app-side logger.

*Concretizes D61 (three streams) and ENGINEERING-DESIGN §6.1. Settles Fork A, first noted in the N126 tail. Interacts with D83 (the single instance whose budget this protects), D99 (the trace correlation that substitutes for per-request app logging), D126 (Firebase Hosting → Cloud Run, the source of both platform logs). Documented in §6.1 in the same PR (OFC-299). Log-tail order: D141 → D142.*

### N127 — The diagnostic stream as built: an injectable `DiagnosticLog` sibling to `AuditLog`, the ad-hoc sites migrated, P10 scrubbing enforced and tested (implements D61/P10; OFC-299)

Before 7a-3b there was no diagnostic-logger module — only an inline `logType: "error"` writer in the 500 handler and ad-hoc `console.*` / `process.stderr.write` calls scattered across ~nine sites. This builds the stream as a first-class module and migrates them onto it.

**The module** (`apps/api/src/audit/diagnostic-log.ts`) is deliberately the sibling of `audit-log.ts`: structured JSON, no logging SDK (D61), an injectable `DiagnosticSink` and an injected clock for deterministic tests, and a default exported singleton (`diagnosticLog`) the clock-less deep modules import directly while the request-scoped routes thread a `trace` label. Four severity methods (`debug`/`info`/`warn`/`error`) over one private `emit`. The default sink is **severity-routed** — `INFO`/`DEBUG` → stdout, `WARNING`/`ERROR` → stderr — honoring the "progress to stdout, errors to stderr" convention and preserving each migrated site's original stream; Cloud Logging keys on the explicit `severity` field regardless of stream.

**The forks, settled at the plan gate (Forrest's call).** (1) **One `logType: "diagnostic"`** spans every severity, *retiring* the old `logType: "error"` value — `severity` is the discriminator a 7a-3c metric or retention rule keys on, so a second logType would only fragment those queries into a union; free to rename now because 7a-3c does not yet exist and this is staging-only. (2) The severity-routed sink above. (3) The scrubber covers **email + conservative phone** (see below). (4) `index.dev.ts` keeps its `console.*` — a dev-only entry point compiled out of the production bundle (D108 layer 1), where `console` is the honest tool for a local banner; noted as intentionally untouched.

**P10, enforced in two layers.** Unlike an `AuditEntry` (which structurally has nowhere to put a value), a diagnostic entry carries free text, so names-not-values is enforced by *shape* — identifiers and field names ride structured label slots, `message` is a constant — and by a *safety net*: `apps/api/src/audit/scrub.ts` redacts the machine-recognizable PII shapes an upstream error can echo (chiefly the member **email** a Ghost Admin-API error names) from every free-text field (`message`, `detail`, an ERROR's `stack`) before the sink writes. Its patterns are deliberately **linear — no ReDoS** (the N88 lesson): the email pattern separates its two runs with a mandatory `@` they exclude, the phone patterns use fixed repetition counts; a unit test pins linearity on a 50 k-char adversarial input. The acknowledged residual is a *name* embedded in an upstream error string, not machine-recognizable to the scrubber — the constant-`message` discipline is its primary defence, the same shape of acknowledged edge the audit stream carries for a target identifier that is itself the value.

**Migrated sites** (all preserving severity and fields, dynamic detail moved to the scrubbed `detail`/`stack` slots so `message` is a constant): the `server.ts` 500 handler (now `logType: "diagnostic"` ERROR, its old `logType: "error"` gone); the two degraded-Ghost-read WARNING helpers in `ghost-provider.ts` and `ghost-reader.ts`; `ghost-audit.ts`'s `ghostReadFailed` (threaded a `diagnostics` config field); `privileged-support.ts`'s session-revocation failure (an injectable `diagnostics` param defaulting to the singleton); `dev-guard.ts`'s D108 layer-4 security alert; the three `StubGhostLifecycle` lines (DEBUG, `targetId` + `fields` names); `cache.ts`'s hydration-normalize warning callback; and `index.ts`'s startup banner (INFO) and fatal handler (ERROR). Tests: `diagnostic-log.test.ts` (severity routing, label passthrough/omission, scrubbing of message/detail/stack) and `scrub.test.ts` (the Ghost-email vector, NANP/E.164 phones, a Constitution ID and an ISO timestamp left intact, ReDoS linearity).

*Implements D61 (three streams, names-not-values), P10 (names-not-values on all streams), and settles the diagnostic half of the 7a-3 split (N122). Sibling to N14/N126 (the audit stream it mirrors). Reuses the D99 trace correlation (`routes/trace.ts`) — threaded through `revokeSessionsBestEffort` so a revocation-failure ERROR correlates to the request. ⚠ The scrubber must stay linear (N88); ⚠ **`EMAIL_RE` must require a dotted TLD and exclude `/`/`:` from the domain** — the free text it scrubs includes ERROR **stack traces**, and a permissive `@`-with-non-space-runs pattern eats scoped-npm-package frames (`@grpc/grpc-js`, `@google-cloud/firestore` — the libraries under `firebase-admin`, the modal 500) and guts the stack, silently regressing the OFC-149 server-side-fidelity guarantee (the 7a-3b review caught the naive first draft; a scoped-package-stack test now pins it); ⚠ the 500 handler now emits `logType: "diagnostic"` severity `ERROR`, not the retired `logType: "error"`. Feeds 7a-3c (metrics/alerting/retention key on `logType: "diagnostic"` + `severity`). Log-tail order: D142 → N127.*

## OFC-306 (2026-07-23, decoupling the staging deploy from a post-merge CI re-run)

### D143 — The pull-request run is the single authoritative gate; the staging deploy triggers on the push to `main` directly (amends N82; corrects CODING-PROJECT-PLAN §5)

**The call.** `ci.yml`'s `push: [main]` trigger is removed — the gate runs on `pull_request` + `workflow_dispatch` only, and the PR run is the single authoritative verification of a change. `deploy-staging.yml` no longer waits on a CI `workflow_run`; it triggers on `push: branches:[main]` **directly**, carrying N82's `paths-ignore` onto its own trigger. One full-gate run per change instead of two; a merge still deploys staging automatically. Forrest's call, 2026-07-23.

**Why.** Every merge ran the full gate twice, and the two runs were deterministic replays of one another. GitHub builds the `pull_request` event from the merge *result* (the branch merged into its base), and branch protection requires that check `strict` — branches up to date before merging (N91) — so the tree verified on the PR is the tree that lands on `main`. On a repo where `main` does not move underneath an open PR, the post-merge run re-tested an identical tree and could only reproduce the same green: pure latency on the critical path of every merge, which had become a measurable drag on session throughput. Worth recording because it was not obvious: the second run was never a deliberate second opinion. It existed because the staging deploy keyed off a CI `workflow_run` (N82), so eliminating the redundancy meant **re-wiring the deploy's trigger**, not deleting a safety check — and the first instinct, to drop the *pre*-merge run instead, would have removed the required check that gates the merge.

**Why this is not a safety reduction.** "A red `main` is never deployed" was enforced by the post-merge gate; it is now enforced by branch protection, which is strictly *earlier*. A commit can only reach `main` through a PR whose strict required check passed on the merge result, and direct pushes to `main` are disallowed. The one failure mode a post-merge run could catch that a pre-merge run cannot — `main` advancing between the PR's green and the merge, so the merged tree differs from the tested one — is foreclosed by the `strict` up-to-date requirement, which forces such a PR to re-verify before it may merge. The residual is a genuinely concurrent merge race, which GitHub's **merge queue** exists to solve; on a single-committer repo it does not arise, and if the project ever gains a second committer the merge queue, not a post-merge re-run, is the correct answer.

**Trades accepted (Forrest's call).** A commit on `main` no longer carries a CI check of its own — its green evidence is the PR run that produced it. This generalizes a trade N82 had already accepted for docs-only merges. And the deploy now begins the instant the merge lands rather than after a gate run, shortening the window between "merged" and "staging changed"; desirable here, but named so it is not a surprise.

**What this does *not* change: production.** §5's standing position stands untouched — production deploys remain "a deliberate, manually-approved promotion of an already-staged build, never an automatic consequence of a merge" (OFC-253). This entry governs the **staging** path only. The production target recorded in `CUTOVER-PLAN.md` keeps a full gate run in front of every production deploy, inside the manual dispatch and against the exact commit being promoted. That is not the redundant re-run removed here: it is the *only* verification of an artifact that nothing else has gated, run at the moment of deliberate promotion.

**The load-bearing precondition (name it, because the argument dies without it).** Everything above rests on a commit being unable to reach `main` except through a green PR. That is a *branch-protection configuration*, not a property of these workflows, and it lives outside the repo where no test can assert it. Verified live at the time of this decision: `enforce_admins: true`, `required_pull_request_reviews` present, `required_status_checks.strict: true` over contexts `["Verify gate", "CodeQL"]`, `allow_force_pushes: false`, `allow_deletions: false`. ⚠ **If `enforce_admins` is ever set back to `false`, this decision's safety argument silently collapses** — an admin-bypass push would then reach `main` with no gate run of any kind and deploy straight to staging, because there is no longer a post-merge run to catch it. Note this also *corrects the log*: N91 recorded `enforce_admins: false` as Forrest's deliberate choice and D141 re-raised the question on OFC-297; the question was evidently resolved to **true**, but no entry recorded the flip. It is recorded here, because D143 is the entry that now depends on it. A code review of this change flagged the bypass hole as a live regression, reasoning correctly from the stale log — the finding was retired only by querying the live setting.

*Amends N82 — its docs-only skip survives with its outcome unchanged, the `paths-ignore` having moved from `ci.yml`'s push trigger onto the deploy's. Corrects CODING-PROJECT-PLAN §5 ("every push and pull request" is no longer true of the gate). Depends on **N91** (strict required checks — the guarantee that now carries what the post-merge run used to). Leaves **D141**'s gate-in-sync guard untouched: only a trigger was removed, the 13-step list is byte-identical on both sides and the guard was re-run green before commit. Interacts with N18 (deploy = wipe-reseed, so a skipped deploy is still a skipped reseed). ⚠ **N88**'s dismissed CodeQL untrusted-checkout alert re-raises when its checkout line changes; this change *removes* the untrusted `ref` outright, so the pattern should resolve rather than re-fire, but a fresh alert number may need triage. OFC-306. Log-tail order: N127 → D143.*

### N128 — The CI/CD pipeline diagram (extends N100's diagram convention to delivery; documents D143)

`docs/architecture/book-cicd-{light,dark}.svg` — a hand-authored pair in the same token palette, 16:9 canvas, and commented-XML style N100 established for the architecture diagrams, embedded in `docs/architecture/README.md` via `<picture>`. It draws the delivery pipeline: the pre-merge gate (local `verify:fast` → pull request → the two required checks → branch protection), the post-merge path (merge → the push trigger → staging deploy → the four staging targets), the dashed not-yet-built production path, and two reference panels giving the authoritative step order for the Verify gate and the staging deploy.

**Why it exists.** D143 left the pipeline correct but hard to hold in the head: the reasoning is spread across two workflow files, a branch-protection config that lives *outside* the repo, and four decision entries. The drawing makes the load-bearing shape visible at a glance — there is exactly **one** gate and it sits *before* the merge, so everything downstream is unverified by design and safe only because branch protection makes that one arrow the sole route onto `main`. A reader who sees that immediately understands why D143 records the protection config as a precondition rather than a detail.

**Deliberate departures from N100.** (1) **No slide variant** — the architecture pair has one because it gets presented; this is a developer reference and a second detail level would be two more files to keep in step for no audience. (2) **No gold lane** — gold means the Ghost identity lane, and Ghost has no part in delivery; teal (the active flow) and neutral are the whole vocabulary, with **dashed** reserved for *not built yet*. (3) **Light is the source of truth**: the dark file is the same geometry under a mapped palette, so edits go to light first and are mirrored. The one place the map is not mechanical is `.mono-num`, which shares a hex with the neutral stroke in light but must stay legible as text on dark.

*Extends N100 (the diagram convention, palette and PNG-export recipe it reuses). Documents D143 (the pipeline it draws) and cites D141 (the gate-list guard that makes the Verify-gate panel authoritative rather than a copy). ⚠ **Maintenance obligation, recorded in `docs/architecture/README.md`:** a change to `ci.yml`, `deploy-staging.yml`, `verify:gate`, or branch protection must be reflected in both SVGs — a stale pipeline diagram is worse than none, because it is consulted precisely when someone is unsure. Log-tail order: D143 → N128.*
